# PlusPlus — Decisions Log

The append-only architectural record. **Record new decisions here as they're
made** (same format as always: **Date — Decision — Reason**); root CLAUDE.md
keeps only the standing laws that every session needs. Read this file when
touching an area with history — the reason a thing is shaped the way it is
usually lives here.

> Record architectural and significant implementation decisions as they're made.
> Format: **Date — Decision — Reason**

**2026-07-23 — Sheet/tray scroll indicators sit flush at the edge: pad a ScrollView's CONTENT, never the ScrollView itself** — Dave, from a screenshot of the New-exercise sheet: "The scroll bar on this sheet is more inset than I'd expect. Why isn't it all the way at the right edge?" Cause: the shared sheet idiom `VStack { SheetHeader; ScrollView { content } }.padding(.horizontal, 18)` applied the horizontal inset to the OUTER container, so the ScrollView's frame — and the vertical scroll indicator that rides it — sat 18 pt in from the sheet edge. The scroll indicator tracks the ScrollView's bounds, so padding the whole ScrollView drags the bar inward. Fix (mechanical, one class of 13 sites across 9 files — `ExerciseEditorView`, `ShareImportSheet`, `RoutineCatalogScreen`'s `GearCheckTray`, `LibraryView`'s `GearPickSheet`, `ExercisePickerView`'s two filter sheets, `EquipmentCatalogScreen`'s `EquipmentTypeFilterSheet`, `ScheduleTray`, `CatalogDetailViews`' `AddToRoutineSheet`, `EquipmentLibraryTray`, `EquipmentResolveSheet`'s two sheets, `GitHubSyncTray`, `RevealSurface`'s `WhatsNewTray`, `RoutineDetailView`'s `RoutineSettingsScreen`): drop the outer `.padding(.horizontal, N)` and put N on each visible sibling (`SheetHeader`, explanatory `Text`, bottom action button) AND the ScrollView's content, so the ScrollView spans full width and its indicator lands at the true trailing edge. Same visual margins for content; the bar moves out to the edge. `SheetHeader` deliberately carries no horizontal padding of its own — it inherits from the parent — so the padding lives at the call site, matching the per-context inset (18 for sheets, 16 for the pushed `RoutineSettingsScreen`). List-based screens and the ones already padding inside the ScrollView (Today, the catalog/detail mains, ActiveSession, `ExerciseConfigSheet`, `ExerciseDetailSheet`) were correct and untouched. Layout-only, device-visible, CI-invisible for feel — the inset itself is deterministic. See `.claude/rules/ui-interaction.md` (the new ScrollView-padding law).

**2026-07-23 — Mascot SCALE-OUT round: 7 moves → 17, sampling every movement/equipment class, + the authoring-system refactor** — Dave: "find 10 more exercises to demonstrate. pick ones to give us a pretty good sample of the types of movements and equipment. implement them to the best of your ability. then do a refactoring pass on this whole thing to improve the system." The ten (all names verbatim SeedData built-ins): Lateral Raise (dumbbells, one-channel abduction), Glute Bridge (floor-supine, the shoulder-blade pivot), Sit-Up (floor-supine, pure torso channel), Overhead Press (barbell, authored bar line past the face), Barbell Row (held hinge, arm-only pull), Goblet Squat (the first `.cupped` hands — `plantingPalms` reused with an upward palm normal), Pull-Up (the first HANGING move), Jump Squat (the first live ballistic windows — the synthetic-jump harness made real), Kettlebell Swing (two hands on one short handle, hip-snap rhythm), Reverse Lunge (asymmetric split stance, stance-ankle anchored). Framework additions, all invariant-backed: `MascotProp.kettlebell/.gobletDumbbell/.pullUpBar` (+ renderer builds and the generalized `heldEquipment` applier), `MascotSupport` pull-up bar geometry (height 1.38 scanned for a clean dead hang), `MascotDynamics.hangsFromBar` + the HANG LAW (`hangingMovesKeepHandsOnTheBar`: palms on the bar line ≤ 8 mm, ONE STATION along it — the barbell's slide law inherited by the fixed bar — and feet never grounding), held-prop masses in `MascotBalance.centerOfMass` (the dumbbell pair had been weightless), and the pull-up bar capsule renamed "barPullUp" so the fingers-never-pierce law's bar-prefix filter covers it (a silent coverage hole). Hard-won authoring laws are in docs/recipes/mascot-move-authoring.md ("Scale-out lessons"): scan WITH the servo's objectives or it drags keys off station; one basin family per multi-config path; authored bar geometry via per-sample `palmTarget`; feedforward station compensation; eased 6-step legs over dense or continuation-seeded bakes; bounded-authority pins clamped inside the anatomical table; never author AT a joint stop (the spline overshoots ~1° past keys); zero-sum leg chains keep lerped soles parallel; the helmet's chain radius makes literal chin-over-bar impossible (the neck-arch finish is the honest top); flare waypoints carry arms past the helmet. Refactor pass: `MascotPoseBuilder.liftCycle` (the curl's lift-first rep shape, now shared by curl/lateral-raise/sit-up), `MascotPoseBuilder.supineTiredBeat` (the bench's shrug-and-glance, now shared by bench/bridge/sit-up — three verbatim copies died), the tests' triplicated `loadHeight` collapsed to one helper, and the camera framing gained hanging + floor-supine cases. Deliberately deferred, with reasons: STRICT single-support balance for the lunge's step (needs a stance-shift solver — the com visibly riding the stance foot; the current step skims low instead), swing-inertia invariants (the bell is hand-held through the whole arc, so the ballistic class can't apply; elasticity/rails still land with their first moves), the effort/eccentric/pause laws for moves whose load the palms/chest rule can't measure (Pull-Up's fixed palms, Glute Bridge's hips — generalizing `loadHeight` per-archetype is refactor-round-2 material), and the pull-up wrap's thumb chirality (config scanned overhand-reading; the barbell thumb law doesn't run on the fixed bar — eyeball on device). Kit 454 tests green on Linux. ⚠️ All ten moves need Dave's on-device read (the sweep proves physics, not feel): the OHP face-dodge, the row's held hinge, the goblet cup, the pull-up's neck-arch finish + station hold, the jump's flat-foot flight, the swing rhythm, the lunge's skimming step.

**2026-07-22 — Mascot HAND round: the hand exists in the physics model — tangent-wrap grips, flat planted push-up palms, the plank's neutral fists, and the deadlift de-shake** — Dave's device pass, three screenshots + one feel note: "it looks like the fingers are going straight through the dumbbell handles. This sort of stuff should be impossible. Figure out how to enforce that." / "This hand placement for pushups is pretty bizarre" / "Hand placement for plank is also pretty weird" / "The deadlift movement feels shaky." Root cause of the first three: hands and fingers had NEVER existed in the Kit's physics model — they were renderer-only boxes (the collision sweep rightly exempts hands because gripping IS contact, but nothing replaced that exemption with hand-specific laws), the dumbbell rendered at a DIFFERENT wrist offset than the palm channel the fingers wrapped (so the curl's finger bases sat ~4 mm from the handle axis, deep inside a 14 mm-radius handle), and the floor moves reused the fist geometry as curled-under "puppy paws." Structural fixes:
- **`MascotHand` — the hand as a shared contract** (the `MascotGrip`/`MascotSupport` pattern): palm slab, three fingers, and thumb as SEGMENTS (center/rotation/size/capsule) in the wrist frame, per hand STATE — `.gripped(aroundRadius:)`, `.planted`, `.fist`, `.idle` — with `state(for:)` the one per-move rule (forearms-bear-weight → fist, hands-bear-weight → planted, barbell → gripped at bar radius, dumbbells → gripped at handle radius). The renderer builds its hand meshes from the SAME segment list the invariants turn into capsules — a hand exists in the pixels and the proof, or in neither.
- **Gripped = tangent wrap.** Fingers are three short segments per finger placed TANGENT to a circle of (grip radius + finger half-thickness + 2 mm slack) around the grip channel — tangent placement, not chord placement, so the inner face touches at its midline and the ends flare AWAY; piercing is impossible by construction when the bar runs on the channel axis. The dumbbell offset is UNIFIED into `MascotGrip.palmOffset` (one channel; the renderer parents the dumbbell there and `equipmentCapsules` agrees) — the curl's grip is now EXACTLY tangent (0.0 mm). What remains on the barbell moves is the diagonal-grip allowance shifting the bar within an outer finger's wrap plane by finger-x·tan(skew): the gripped finger spread tightened ±18→±15 mm and the slack absorbs most; solved worst cases squat 1.1 / deadlift 3.0 / bench 5.0 mm — bounded ≤ 6 mm by the new `handsNeverPierceWhatTheyHold` (which also bounds the hand's axial reach against the dumbbell HEAD's flat inner face, disc-model like the plates law; `MascotGrip.dumbbellHeadHalfWidth` joined the contract).
- **Planted (push-up) = a genuinely flat palm, and the arm re-authored to afford it.** A flat planted hand is NOT a wrist property: fingers-forward + palm-down is ~180° of twist about the forearm, split (the `grippingTheBar` anatomy again) across humeral spin + pronation + the elbow's radioulnar share — and the census put dead-forward fingers at a 14–19° palm-tilt feasibility floor, so the finger target is forward-INWARD ~40° (what real loaded hands do). `plantingPalms` is a whole-left-arm solver (8 DOF, mirrored) with the planted WRIST position non-negotiable (weight 100 — at 30 the solver sold 26 mm of hand-skate to shave orientation), an elbow fore-aft stack (laterally soft — deep reps flare the elbows), and Levenberg-Marquardt BACKTRACKING instead of plain damped GN: near the infeasible deep bottom several joints ride their stops and a plain clamped step CORNER-LOCKS (the descent direction points out of bounds on coupled coordinates, the clamp zeroes it, iteration freezes 20+ mm off target); shrinking the step until the residual improves and raising damping when nothing does walks along the active bounds. The push-up chain re-authored: the straight arm plants the hands slightly AHEAD of the shoulder line (the forearm lean is what buys wrist extension 90−lean), the bottom keeps the forearm stacked (the old folded shoulder −10/elbow −130 bottom left the palm unreachable-flat at ANY wrist angle), and the wrist-extension range widened 80→92° (solver 90) — loaded support extension genuinely exceeds free-motion tables. Where the twist chain still tops out at depth, `settledPlanted` anchors the hand by its LOWEST point (`solvingToes` for hands, two correction passes, lift or pull-down): the hand rocks forward onto its planted fingers, heel proud — which is what a loaded hand actually does — and `plantedHandsRestFlatOnTheFloor` enforces never-pierce (≥ −3 mm), never-hover (≤ 10 mm in the work phase), fingers extended along the floor.
- **Plank = neutral fists, not palms.** A horizontal forearm's palm-down needs ~108° of pronation against an 88° stop — which is WHY real forearm planks rest on neutral fists (thumb up, pinky edge down). New `MascotDynamics.forearmsBearWeight` names the support honestly; the plank's hands are `.fist` (the gripped wrap closed around nothing, radius 10 mm) at wrist zero-plus-full-pronation, the elbow flexion bisected until the fist's lowest surface grazes 1 mm; `plankFistsRideTheFloor` enforces the band and thumb-side-up. The plank's breathing sway was also rebuilt: the old root-lift bob floated the anchored forearms ±3 mm; now every hold sample re-runs the floor closure (fixed elbow anchors + fist clearance) so breathing lives in the torso and the contacts never move — and `tiredBeat` grew a `solve:` hook so both floor moves re-settle the phew/exhale poses onto their contacts (the chest-lift can't hover the hands).
- **Deadlift shake, root-caused twice over:** (1) the grip servo's redundant arm DOF had no preference inside its null space, so Gauss-Newton bounced between nearby solutions knot to knot (shoulder roll flapping ±10–17° between adjacent baked samples) — a soft stay-near-seed term (`wSeed` 0.3) picks one point smoothly, which also made the servo's doc claim of regularization TRUE (review nit); (2) `coordinating`'s correction quantum stair-stepped ~0.6°/knot — now 96 steps of 0.0025 rad (same total authority, finer grain). Bar-path second differences ≤ 1.3 mm (residual knee-pass junction easing kinks only).
- **Grip-round review findings folded in** (swift-reviewer, MEDIUM+2 LOW+2 nits): the `coordinating`→`grippingTheBar` composition is not structurally bounded — the deadlift's 5 mm servo bound shipped 6.7 mm of bar-into-thigh (1.3 mm from the invariant); the servo bound now reserves real headroom (4 mm; solved worst 4.7, and 3 mm bought nothing but more bang-bang nudge oscillation). The bench touch was re-scanned against the SOLVED cycle, not the seed (the old comment's "5 mm" described a pose that shipped at 6.8): touch elbow −139.8→−137.4°, solved worst 4.7 mm. The recipe's stale `aligningGrip` reference and 20° grip bound were corrected, and the Jacobian comment.
Kit **441 tests** green on Linux (438 + the three hand invariants). Hand-round review fold (swift-reviewer, core verified clean — mirror algebra, renderer parity, tangent geometry, LM loop, determinism): the three hand invariants now iterate EVERY move and key on `MascotHand.state(for:)` instead of hardcoded move lists — the rule that gives a move its hand pixels gives it its proof, so scale-out moves can't silently escape coverage; the bench's ~1 mm wrap-graze margin is named at its solve site; the `plantingPalms` bounds comment states the deliberate wrist-extension divergence; `fingerDirection` dropped a dead, mirroring-ambiguous `side` parameter. Renderer: hands/dumbbells rebuilt from the contract (`MascotRig` builds every hand box from `MascotHand.segments`; per-prop wrap radius). ⚠️ Device pass (with the held mascot-build dispatch, from MAIN when Dave asks): the curl grip hugging the handles, the barbell wraps at the new tighter spread, the push-up's flat forward-inward hands INCLUDING the deep-bottom rock-onto-the-fingers read, the plank's thumbs-up fists, and the deadlift's steadiness.

**2026-07-21 — Mascot GRIP round: hands keep one station on the bar, wrap it overhand, and can never touch a plate — the whole-arm `grippingTheBar` servo replaces wrist-only alignment** — Dave's device pass on the merged bench press: "the mascot's hands are sliding all over the bar … looks like it's currently underhand, should be overhand … sometimes intersecting with the bar and plates. We must make sure that the grip for every exercise is correct and that physics are respected." Diagnostics: the bench palms slid 99 mm along the bar (out to the plate's inner face — a fist INSIDE a plate), the deadlift slid 33 mm, and BOTH wrapped thumb-out (supinated/underhand — the round-earlier "signed" axis fix pinned the wrong sign; the squat's rack scan alone had landed thumb-in). Root causes and their structural fixes: **(1) Station.** Nothing ever constrained the palm's position ALONG the bar — the orientation-only wrist servo watched the axis while the arm chain slid the hand down it. `MascotPoseBuilder.grippingTheBar` re-solves the whole LEFT arm per baked sample (shoulder 3 DOF + elbow pitch/yaw + wrist 3, damped Gauss-Newton over a 9–10-term residual, mirrored right) with the palm pinned to its station; new invariant `handsHoldOneStationOnTheBar` (≤ 8 mm of slide across the whole cycle, Squat/Deadlift/Bench). **(2) Overhand.** The wrap side is ~180° of rotation about the forearm and NO single joint owns it — anatomy splits it across shoulder internal rotation (~90°), the elbow's radioulnar share (~23°, which is why elbow yaw joined the solve), and wrist pronation (~88°); at the deadlift bottom and bench touch the chain tops out just short of the full flip, and the ~20° leftover is the natural diagonal bar placement real lifters show (the grip-axis invariant widened 20°→25° for exactly this, with the anatomy in the comment). New invariant `theGripIsOverhand` (left thumb ≤ −0.85 along +x, hand broadly continuing the forearm). The Gauss-Newton SEED picks the basin: the bench authors its endpoints in the overhand basin; the deadlift passes an `armSeed` INTERPOLATED from the pose's own hinge angle (a constant seed left the standing end so far from home the solver crossed basins and put the bar 57 mm into the belly — the hinge-tracked seed keeps every sample's start near its solution, and a fixed-seed-family + smooth target is a continuous map where per-sample greedy search is not). **(3) Plates are physics.** Hands are rightly exempt from the shaft-collision sweep (gripping IS contact) and the sweep's plate capsules bulge hemispherically along the axis anyway — so the new `handsNeverTouchThePlates` models the plate's real inner FACE as a disc and keeps the whole fist (`MascotGrip.fistRadius`) axially inside it. **Composition law:** `coordinating` first (it speaks the simple pitch-only arm convention and owns the bar's PATH — its shoulder-pitch clearance nudge swings a hanging bar forward only under that convention), `grippingTheBar` second (rebuilds the arm on that path and owns the hand); the deadlift keeps its authored arms SIMPLE for the first servo and hands the second its basin seed. **Seam exactness moved from gates to determinism:** `repCycle` now emits every endpoint appearance as `solve(seed)` — the same pure call — and `MascotPose.lerp` returns exact endpoints at t = 0/1 (floating point's `a + (b−a)` need not equal `b`), so pause stillness survives a servo with no identity gate. Fallout tuned: deadlift lockout lean −15°→−13° and its tired beat settled to 0.55 (the pronated arm carries the phew's chest-lift swing on a longer lever — at full settle the bar crossed the over-midfoot bound mid-beat); bench touch re-scanned 3.5 mm shallower (graze 8.5→5 mm). The wrist-only `aligningGrip` is REMOVED (superseded; dead abstractions don't stay). Squat needed nothing — its rack passes all three new laws as authored. Kit 438 tests green on Linux. ⚠️ Device pass: the overhand wrap read on all three barbell moves, hands fixed to their stations, the deadlift's internally-rotated arm look (elbow pits toward the body — anatomically right for double-overhand), the bench press arc.

**2026-07-21 — Kit axes separation: switching is one shared mechanism, catalog filters are pure local lenses** — the last parked piece of the kit-surface untangle (Dave picked "separate the two axes"; then "do that part now too"). The two orthogonal concepts had been tangled: **switching the active kit** (global scope) lived in TWO switch UIs, and one of them was folded INTO a browse filter (the routine catalog's `RoutineKitFilterSheet`, which both switched the app-wide kit AND filtered), while the exercises catalog could only filter, not switch. Now: **switching is one mechanism** — the canonical `EquipmentLibraryTray`, reached identically from the Kit tab (header switcher), both pushed catalogs, and the reveal drawer; and **each catalog's filter is a pure LOCAL lens** that judges against whatever kit is active and never changes global scope. Concretely: (1) the **routine catalog** gained a "Browsing [kit ▾]" switch strip (the shared `LibrarySwitcherKey` → `EquipmentLibraryTray`, mirroring the equipment catalog's "Adding to" strip) and its kit chip became a plain `SelectableChip` "Can do now" (a local `.mine`↔`nil` toggle matching the exercises catalog's availability vocabulary); `RoutineKitFilterSheet` (the second switch UI, only a day old) and the `KitFilterChip` component were **deleted**. (2) The **exercises catalog** gained the same inline kit switcher in its header (you no longer have to leave for the Kit tab to change what "Can do now" judges against); its "Equipment" facet was already a pure lens. Net −157 lines. What's deliberately NOT changed: the per-catalog filter OPTIONS stay distinct (routines are all-or-nothing "Can do now"; exercises keep can-do/can't-yet/picked) — their multiplicity is contextual; and the membership editors stay separate (already sharing `EquipmentRowContent`). This completes the arc — #423 visibility → #424 one tray → #425 one naming rule → #426 the `null` kit → this. App-target only; device pass for the routine "Browsing" strip switching live behind the tray, and the exercises header switcher fit beside the longer title.

**2026-07-21 — A baked-in permanent no-equipment kit, `null`** — Dave, while we were untangling the kit surfaces: "bake in a no-equipment kit, so every person always has two options, and nobody needs to make a no-equipment kit." Name settled on **`null`** (Dave's programmer wink — the empty set, pairs with the default kit `main` and the `++` mark; an empty membership already means bodyweight-only). Every store now always carries `null` alongside `main`. Design: **identity is the reserved NAME** (`EquipmentLibrary.bodyweightName = "null"`), because the interchange already merges libraries by lowercased name — so seed / export / import all dedup on it for free, no new synced field, no migration, no interchange-census change. `SeedData.ensureBodyweightKit` (launch one-shot, AFTER `ensureEquipmentLibrary` + `renameDefaultKitIfNeeded` so the count-based Home→main rename still fires) creates it if absent and **re-creates it if deleted** — the "baked in" guarantee. It's **protected** (the tray hides its Rename/Delete menu) and **immutable**: the guarantee lives at the model — `EquipmentLibrary.setMembership` no-ops when `isBodyweight`, so no surface can give it equipment whatever it asks. Two write paths bypass `setMembership` and got their own guards (swift review): the **interchange import** clamps a bodyweight-named library to empty (else a bundle carrying an old custom "null" kit with gear would permanently populate the immutable one on restore/sync), and **Operator** rename/delete guard on `!isBodyweight`. And because the null kit is ALWAYS present, two count-based rules were corrected to count only REAL (non-null) kits: `activeNamePhrase` (a lone-real-kit user still reads "your kit", not the name) and the tray's delete guard (never strand a store on null-only). UI reflects the immutability where you'd otherwise add: the Kit tab drops its "Add equipment" row + shows a distinct empty state, the equipment catalog suppresses the ADD/REMOVE swipe and reads "On null" instead of "Adding to …", and the equipment-detail card becomes a read-only note ("On the null kit · switch to another kit to add equipment"). Its gear read-out is a wink caption (Dave's line, trimmed to a row): **"just you, plus maybe shoes."** **Tied to the "separate the axes" answer:** a permanent `null` kit makes the routine catalog's separate **"No equipment" filter MODE redundant** — you just switch to `null` — so that mode is gone (`GearFit.bodyweightOnly` removed; it was `@State`, not persisted, so no stored-enum hazard), leaving the routine Kit sheet as [kits, incl. `null`] + "All routines". By-design consequence: browsing bodyweight-only routines now SWITCHES the app-wide active kit to `null` (a global scope change, the routine sheet's existing kit-row paradigm) rather than a local mode; the broader axes-separation (a header switch pill + pure-local lenses on both catalogs) is still the paused follow-up. Deleting your last non-null kit leaves only `null` (immutable) — recovery is "New kit…" in the tray, always present. Dave's pick of `null` (over "No equipment") means his existing MANUAL "bodyweight" kit stays a separate user kit he can delete; the baked-in one is `null`. App-target only; 4 new `SeedDataTests` (create / idempotent / recreate-after-delete / membership-rejected). ⚠️ Device pass: the null row's caption + protection in the tray, the Kit-tab/catalog/detail immutability surfaces, and that switching to `null` scopes the whole app to bodyweight.

**2026-07-20 — Kit-surface consolidation: one switch tray, one naming rule, one possessive, one edit-contents label** — Dave, after a device mishap (added equipment to the wrong kit because the active kit wasn't legible where he was adding) then "figure out the right degree to which and ways in which we ought to unify" the kit-indication/switch/create/edit surfaces. An inventory found 7 name-the-active-kit indicators, 4 switch entry points funneling into **two different trays with disjoint capabilities**, and drifting possessive vocabulary. The chosen degree: **unify the mechanism and the source of truth; keep the contextual manifestations.** Two PRs. **PR A (#424) — one tray.** `EquipmentLibraryTray` (Kit tab, catalog, routine catalog) did switch/create/rename/delete; the reveal drawer's private `LibraryTray` did switch/create/edit-contents but NOT rename/delete, so what you could do to a kit depended on which door you came through. Made `EquipmentLibraryTray` the single canonical tray reached identically from all four entry points, with ONE optional contextual extra — an `onEditContents` shortcut — passed only by the reveal drawer (the one caller remote from the catalog); the Kit tab and catalog pass nil since editing is already there. Deleted `LibraryTray` (~146 lines) + its dead downstream-count helpers. **PR B (this PR) — one naming rule + vocabulary.** The `count > 1 ? name : "your kit"` logic was inlined at multiple prose sites and starting to diverge; extracted it to ONE helper, `EquipmentLibrary.activeNamePhrase(in:storedID:generic:)`, and routed the equipment-detail add card + the equipment-check tray blurb through it. Articulated the latent rule (now in app-surfaces.md): **a switcher CONTROL always shows the raw kit name** (a control needs a label even with one kit — the Kit-tab pill, the catalog "Adding to" strip, the routine Kit chip), while **PROSE and verdicts name the kit only once more than one exists, else "your kit"**. Unified the possessive to **"your kit"** ("My equipment"/"YOUR KIT ✓" retired as user-facing possessives; `GearFit.mine`'s raw value stays internal filter-persistence, and the old ALL-CAPS "YOUR KIT ✓" template verdict was already gone with the routine-card unification) and the open-the-catalog-to-edit-membership label to **"Edit your kit…"** (was "Edit my equipment…" in the exercise-picker filter and "Choose your equipment" in the tray). Deliberately NOT unified (contextual, not accidental): the several membership editors (catalog swipe, detail toggle, Kit-tab-list swipe, equipment-check toggles — they already share `EquipmentRowContent`) and the per-item shapes of the indicators; no grand "Kit Manager" screen (the tray + catalog already cover management — that would be the premature abstraction the repo warns against). ⚠️ App CI-verified; device pass for the tray from all four doors (esp. the reveal drawer's now-present rename/delete) and the reworded labels/prose across kit counts.

**2026-07-20 — Workout-execution device-report fixes: Live Activity teardown race, in-workout list coloring, countdown beeps** — Dave's on-device workout surfaced a batch of execution-time bugs (parent #416, sub-issues #417–#421). This branch lands the three tractable-from-a-remote-session ones; #418 (live HR) and #379/#417 (phone→watch launch + sync) are deliberately NOT touched here — both hinge on running/mirroring an `HKWorkoutSession` (the clean live-HR fix IS the mirrored session), which is #379's architectural scope and needs a 2-device validation pass, so a speculative HealthKit rewrite here would risk the one HR path that already works (the post-workout recap). The three fixes:
- **#419 — the whole-session Live Activity never appeared (Dynamic Island AND Lock Screen).** Root cause was a teardown race in `WorkoutActivityController.begin()`: it called `endAll()` (which ends every activity inside a `Task`) immediately before `Activity.request(...)`. The new activity published into `Activity.activities` synchronously, before the `endAll` task body ran, so the loop ended the just-created activity with `.immediate` — suppressing both surfaces for the entire workout. The feature was fully built and entitled (#322); it just tore itself down. Fix: snapshot the pre-existing activities into a **value array** before `Activity.request`, then end only that snapshot — race-free by construction, the new activity can never be in the set. `end()` (finish/discard) still ends everything. Also split the `areActivitiesEnabled` guard to log the disabled case via OSLog (`activityLog`), since a silent no-op is what hid this. ⚠️ ActivityKit renders only on a physical device (never Simulator), and this path was never device-validated — needs Dave's on-device pass: start a phone-only workout, background it (island) and lock (lock screen).
- **#421 — color the in-workout exercise list by status.** Dave: completed = purple, current = green, upcoming = grey while working / **pulsing green while resting or transitioning**. The purple-done/green-current grammar (#201) already shipped at the set-pip level in `SessionOverviewSheet`; this extends it to the row (name color via a `BlockStatus` → `nameColor`) and adds the fourth case. `ActiveSessionView` passes `isResting: restEndDate != nil` (covers both rest and #369 transitions — no `LiveSession.isTransition` op-field needed since the pulse is driven from the phone's local phase). The pulse is a `repeatForever` name-opacity + breathing background wash on the not-yet-done rows, **gated on `accessibilityReduceMotion` with a static-green fallback** (WCAG 2.3.3, per the app-surfaces motion law). The per-exercise sheet's DONE label also went purple for consistency. ⚠️ The pulse is device-only feel; reachable by opening the overview during a rest countdown.
- **#420 — countdown beeps.** A soft tick on each of the last three seconds of a rest/switch countdown and a distinct higher "go" tone as the next exercise begins. New `CountdownCue` synthesizes sine-wave WAV tones **in memory** (no bundled assets to ship/verify) and plays them via `AVAudioPlayer`. Hooked into `RestView`'s `.onChange(of: remaining)` — the tick guard is `newValue < oldValue && (1...3).contains(newValue)` so a +30s extension (which raises `remaining`) never beeps, and the "go" tone rides the natural `remaining <= 0` landing (a manual Skip stays silent — you're already looking at the phone). New **COUNTDOWN CUES** toggle in the Settings tray, **default ON** (Dave, on his device-report read: unlike an unasked talking coach, a rest countdown beep is a conventional, expected timer affordance, so unlike voice cues it ships on and the user can silence it; `CountdownCueSetting.isEnabled` reads an unset key as ON to match the `@AppStorage` default). Phone only — the watch keeps its terminal rest haptic; a 3·2·1 haptic ramp on the wrist is a noted follow-up. **Audio-session ownership was refactored out of the two cue classes into a shared `WorkoutAudioSession` (swift-reviewer catch):** the beeps are the app's SECOND audio source after `VoiceCueSpeaker`, and two independent owners each toggling `setActive` on the one process session raced — the go-tone fires the instant the next exercise's voice cue speaks, so the tone's deferred `setActive(false)` could cut a mid-sentence cue, and a dropped decrement in either left the user's music ducked with no sweep. `WorkoutAudioSession` is the single refcounted owner: `.playback` + `.duckOthers` (silent switch can't mute; music ducks), ALL cue work (both classes) on its one shared serial queue (`setActive` is a blocking mediaserverd IPC, off-main), a **generation-guarded deferred** deactivate so a run of cues doesn't thrash the music, `hold`/`release(after:)` bracketing each cue and `sweep()` force-clearing at workout end (wired next to every `VoiceCueSpeaker.stop()`). `CountdownCue` also releases its hold immediately when `AVAudioPlayer.play()` returns false, so a failed/interrupted beep can't strand the session. `VoiceCueSpeaker` migrated onto the same owner with its activate-before-speak ordering preserved (same serial queue). ⚠️ Audio is device-only (CI proves wiring + inert-under-UI-test, never sound) — needs Dave's on-device pass with music playing and BOTH cue types on: tone pitches/length, duck/recover feel across the run, silent-switch audibility, the +30s/Skip guards, and no cue-cuts-cue.

**2026-07-20 — The Equipment tab is renamed "Kit"; the kit switcher truncates instead of crowding the heading; "gear" is retired from user-facing copy** — Dave, from a screenshot where the on-row heading read "Equip…" (clipped by the "bodyweight" switcher beside it): "rename the equipment library to just Kit, in the tab label and heading, so its heading will be guaranteed to fit… and make it so that even if the current kit's name is very long, the trigger for the kit tray will truncate instead of crowd out the view heading." (1) **Tab + heading → "Kit"** — the tab now IS your active kit, and the three-letter word can't clip on the shared icon row; the `AppTab.equipment` enum case, the `revealRoot(tab: "equipment")` signal, the `EquipmentLibrary` type, and the `program/equipment-libraries/` interchange path all stay as frozen internals (only the two display strings changed, in `RootTabView` + the `EquipmentTabView` `CatalogTabHeader`). (2) **Switcher truncation** — `LibrarySwitcherKey`'s name gained `.truncationMode(.tail)` (kept `.lineLimit(1)` + `.minimumScaleFactor(0.6)`); a long kit name shrinks a touch then truncates rather than growing into the title, because the heading already claims its space first via `layoutPriority(1)` (2026-07-19) so the switcher is what yields. NO hard `maxWidth` cap — a first pass added `.frame(maxWidth: 160)` but that frame is greedy in the header HStack (it competes with the trailing `Spacer`) and left a gap before the chevron for short names like the default "main" (swift-reviewer catch); the cap wasn't load-bearing since `layoutPriority` already protects the heading. (3) **"Gear" retired** — Dave then said "I think we should drop 'gear'." Answered with a **context mix** (his pick): the your-set sense → **kit**, the single-item / catalog sense → **equipment**. The **"Equipment catalog" name stays** (his pick — it's the universe you add FROM, not a kit). Swept every user-facing string: the Exercises-tab "Gear" filter facet → "Equipment" (now matching the picker's facet), "Picked gear" → "Picked equipment", the routine verdict "YOUR GEAR ✓"/"NO GEAR" → "YOUR KIT ✓"/"NO EQUIPMENT" (the multi-kit variant already named the kit), "Gear check" → "Equipment check", "Choose your gear" → "Choose your equipment", "Needs your gear first" → "Needs your equipment first", the kit-tray copy ("your gear" → "your equipment", "its gear" → "its equipment"), the equipment-detail "You have this gear." → "You have this equipment.", and Operator's user-visible change-preview lines ("gear becomes/updated/cleared" → "equipment …"). LEFT as internal (not user-visible): the `gearMode`/`pickedGear` AppStorage keys, `gearCheck*`/`revealChooseGear` accessibility identifiers, the `"gear"` SF Symbol, and Operator's `add_gear`/`remove_gear`/`replace_gear` **tool names + `@Guide` model-prompt text** (a tuned on-device-model contract — a rename there is a separate, riskier change, deliberately deferred). The **voice skill** (`.claude/skills/voice/SKILL.md`) was the source of truth ENDORSING "gear" (vocab table + two calibration examples), so it was updated in the same pass — otherwise `copy-reviewer` would reintroduce the word. Tests updated: `SmokeTests` ("Needs your equipment first") + `ChangeEngineTests` ("equipment becomes Probe Bench"). **Follow-up in the same PR (Dave):** the awkward kit-tray caption ("One kit per place you train. Switching changes what counts as your equipment everywhere.") was simpler said elsewhere already — the reveal-surface kit switcher already carried a ship-quality line. Rather than keep two versions, the explainer became the ONE canonical string `EquipmentLibrary.switchingBlurb`, referenced by both switcher captions (reveal + the Kit-tab tray). Final wording (Dave's, verbatim): **"Your selected kit determines which exercises your routines can include.\n\nSwitch kits when you travel, and add to your kit to unlock more exercises."** (a deliberate two-beat blank line). A refined variant was floated ("what you can train" instead of "routines can include", since the kit flags availability rather than blocking routine composition per flag-don't-hide #113); Dave kept his original wording — his call. the voice skill's calibration example was aligned to "Switch kits" (was "Switch sets" — ambiguous now that "kit" is the term and "sets" also means exercise sets). The build-48 What's-New changelog line still describes kits in changelog voice — left as a dated historical announcement, not a competing live explainer. ⚠️ App CI-verified only; the switcher-truncation fit with a long kit name is device-only (per the 2026-07-19 heading note) — needs Dave's on-device look at the Kit tab with a long-named kit.

**2026-07-19 (even later) — The tape scrubber replaces the wheel for distance and calories, not just time spans; `DurationTape` generalized to `MetricTape`** — Dave, from a device screenshot: "Don't use this vertical wheel for distance. Use our custom side-to-side one, like we do for duration. Same for any other reasonable places." The horizontal tape scrubber (the iOS-27-timer ruler, 2026-07-15) was time-span-only. Generalized it: Kit's `DurationTape` geometry became `MetricTape` — a pure integer-"unit" tape (linear unit↔points, clamp, `ticks(in:)` with a `minorStride`/`labelStride` schedule and an `isLabeled` flag instead of the old duration-specific `s%30` label owner). A "unit" is the tape's smallest addressable step and the SwiftUI layer maps it to the metric's real value via a per-metric `quantum`: **1 s** for duration/rest/transition, **1 m** for metered distance, **0.01 mi/km** for road distance (so 3.14 mi is reachable, not just the wheel's 0.25 grid), **1 cal** for calories. `WorkoutMetric` gained `usesTapeScrubber` (the picker-routing gate — the time spans + the two wide-range continuous WORK metrics, distance and calories) and `scrubberTape(distanceUnit:) -> (quantum, MetricTape)?`; strides echo the old wheel grain (25 m/250 m, 0.05/0.25 unit, 5/25 cal) so it reads familiar. `isTimeSpan` stays NARROWER than `usesTapeScrubber` — it now means only "render the readout as clock text (m:ss)"; distance/calories read as value-plus-unit ("1.5 mi", "300 cal") with bare-number tick labels (the readout carries the unit). The SwiftUI `DurationScrubber`/`DurationScrubberPane` became generic `MetricScrubber`/`MetricScrubberPane` (`Views/Components/MetricScrubber.swift`), taking the tape + `tickText`/`valueText` closures + a per-metric VoiceOver `adjustStep` (1 s for time as before; the metric's real stepper stride in units for the rest — 50 m, 0.25 mi, 5 cal — so an a11y swipe moves a meaningful amount, not one hundredth). ALL the original write-discipline invariants are preserved verbatim (never write on open; `touched`-gated commit on user-driven settle or `onDisappear`; an out-of-range/off-quantum stored value displays clamped-and-snapped but survives an untouched open-and-close — the value↔unit `quantum` round-trip only commits when the user actually moves the tape). `DurationTape` slimmed to just the compact-duration `label(for:)` helper (still used app-wide for "3×45s") + `isTimeSpan`. `MetricWheelSheet` (the single choke point, presented from all six pick sites) branches on `usesTapeScrubber`. Left on the WHEEL by design: loads (weight/assist — plate semantics), short lists (reps/height/rpe), and machine dials (pace [a rate, deliberately excluded per the 2026-07-15 note], speed/incline/resistance/cadence, and power — dials, not work metrics); power (300 rows) and cadence (210) are the borderline candidates if Dave wants them later. Kit 435 tests green on Linux (`DurationTapeTests` → `MetricTapeTests`, +distance/calorie coverage). ⚠️ App CI-verified only; the gesture/scroll feel is CI-invisible (XCUITest bypasses the scroll overlay) — needs Dave's on-device pass on the distance AND calories picks in every unit (drag precision, flick inertia, the 0.01-mi grain, out-of-range survival, the readout/tick labels). Note: Dave's message was cut off after "Also," — a second ask may be pending.

**2026-07-19 (later still) — Tab-root headings move onto the icon row, left of nothing but the ++ key** — Dave: "have the headings for the four main views sit up top, left-aligned, to the right of the ++ button, still big." The four tab roots (Today · Routines · Exercises · Equipment) previously wore their `.title` heading on a line BELOW the icon row; now the heading rides the icon row itself, immediately right of `AppMenuKey`, with the trailing keys (search, +, the Equipment kit switcher) pushed to the far right by a `Spacer`. Font stays `.title` bold — it fits the tightest case (Equipment + kit switcher + search) even on the smallest supported device, so no shrink was needed and all four keep ONE font size (Dave's constraint). The on-row title carries `.lineLimit(1)` + `.layoutPriority(1)` (NOT `.fixedSize`): it claims its space first so the fixed trailing keys stay reachable, and any horizontal squeeze falls on the variable-width kit switcher (which already carries `minimumScaleFactor(0.6)`) rather than ejecting a key off-screen — the swift-reviewer + axiom-accessibility catch on the first pass, which used `.fixedSize` and would have shoved the search/switcher keys past the right edge at large Dynamic Type. **At accessibility text sizes the heading reflows to its own line BELOW the icon row** (`dynamicTypeSize.isAccessibilitySize`, `.lineLimit(2)` + `.fixedSize(vertical:)` so it wraps at full size) — the canonical "reflow, don't cap the size" fix (#164), keeping every icon-row key reachable when the title would otherwise be enormous. The heading also hides while the header's expanding search field is open (the field spans the row). Implemented in the shared `CatalogTabHeader` (Routines/Exercises/Equipment) and Today's hand-rolled twin. ⚠️ Layout-only, but the on-row fit with long custom kit names AND the accessibility-size reflow are device-only — needs an on-device look on the Equipment tab at default and at an AX text size.

**2026-07-19 (later) — The sheet-corner concentric experiment is removed; icon keys are plain 11-pt rounded squares everywhere** — Dave, on the build device pass: the concentric (asymmetric) corner on the exercise picker's search key read as an "uneven corner radius, no bueno." Removed the `concentricAtSheetCorner` flag from `HeaderIconButton`/`HeaderSearchField` and the `ConcentricRectangle` branch entirely; every icon key is now `RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 11)` with no per-context variation. (The create-row-buttons and the picker-top cleanup from the same day stand.)

**2026-07-19 — Icon keys revert to rounded squares (concentric only at a sheet's top corner); create rows become buttons** — Dave, on the build-99 device pass. The 2026-07-18 all-circles round was a blunt fix for "rounded squares look wrong in a sheet's top corners"; the right fix is iOS 26 corner concentricity, so: (1) `HeaderIconButton`/`HeaderMenuKey`/`AppMenuKey`/Operator send-stop go back to `RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 11)` + `.raisedKey()` (`ConfigIconButton` → 8), and (2) a key in a SHEET's top corner passes `concentricAtSheetCorner: true`, which draws its cap as `ConcentricRectangle(corners: .concentric(minimum: .fixed(11)))` so the corner continues the sheet's curve; the `.fixed(11)` floor means it's never tighter than the plain square and degrades to the square where no rounded container shape exists (pushed screens, tab roots — SwiftUI provides the container shape only inside system containers like sheets). Only the exercise picker's search key sets it today (the one sheet-native custom header with a top-corner icon button); the sheet-presented `pushedScreenChrome` catalogs (Edit-my-equipment etc.) stay plain square for now — deferred, since the chrome can't tell it's in a sheet. Same round: the "New …/Add …/Create …" rows were bare `.plain` green text that read as floating; the private `CreateRow` (green bordered raised key) was promoted to `Components/RaisedKey.swift` and now backs every create/add row, so creation reads as a real button. ⚠️ The concentric effect is device-only (CI can't render it) and its strength depends on the actual sheet corner radius; needs Dave's on-device look.

**2026-07-18 — Search, filtering, creation, icon keys, headings, and sheet dismissal are now consistent app-wide** — Dave asked to unify the search/filter UIs and the creation flows, with no dead-end empty results. Settled and shipped as one pass:
- **One search UI everywhere**: the expanding in-header field (`HeaderSearchField`, extracted from `PushedScreenChrome`) — a top-right magnifier that expands into a field spanning the row, an in-field `delete.left` CLEAR that keeps focus, and a separate `xmark` COLLAPSE key where the magnifier was. The persistent `SearchField` bar is DELETED; `CatalogTabHeader` gained an optional `search:` (magnifier in the icon row, big title hides while searching), so the Exercises tab, the Equipment kit tab, and the Routines tab now search the same way as the pushed catalogs. The Exercise picker dropped its system toolbar for the same custom chrome. A pre-seeded query auto-expands the field on appear.
- **Creation is always the top list row**, in two verb-keyed families: **Create** (`New <object>` / `Create "<Sentence cased query>"`) where the row makes a custom object inline — the Routine catalog, Exercises tab, Exercise picker, Equipment catalog; and **Add** (`Add <object>` / `Add "<query>"`) where the row NAVIGATES to a catalog to bring something into your collection — the Equipment kit tab and the Routines tab, threading the query into the catalog's search (`RoutineCatalogDestination.query`, `EquipmentCatalogScreen(initialQuery:)`). Query sentence-casing is `String.sentenceCasedFirst` (first letter only, so "iPhone"/"EZ-bar" survive — NOT `operatorSentenceCased`).
- **No dead-end empty views**: the create/add row is always present, plus a "Clear filters" `QuietKey` when facets are active (matching the Routine catalog reference). The bare "Nothing matches these filters." dead-ends are gone; `LibraryEmptyState` and the `ContentUnavailableView("No Routines")` overlay are deleted.
- **Icon-only buttons are CIRCLES** (Dave: rounded squares looked wrong in sheet corners): `HeaderIconButton`/`HeaderMenuKey`/`AppMenuKey` at 44 pt → radius 22, `OperatorTray` send/stop at 40 pt → radius 20, `ConfigIconButton` at 30 pt → a Circle. `RaisedKeyStyle` is UNCHANGED — its plate `cornerRadius` is a parameter, so radius = side/2 makes both cap and plate circular. Labeled keys keep their rounded-rect pill.
- **One sheet-top button vocabulary**: `xmark` is reserved for collapsing search, so a sheet/tray DISMISSES with a text key (`SheetDismissKey`: "Cancel" to abandon edits, "Done" view-only). `SheetHeader.closeOnly`'s ✕ and the hand-built ✕'s in Operator/GitHub/the start tray are retired to that key.
- **Heading treatment by the nature of the title**: tab roots keep the large left title below the icon row; fixed-label utility/catalog screens keep the small centered chrome title; a pushed detail screen showing a dynamic NAME clears its chrome title and leads the body with a large left header that wraps to two lines (Exercise/Equipment/Template detail now match RoutineDetailView; SessionDetailView keeps its centered title + subtitle as the record exception). `SheetHeader` titles wrap to two lines; `SessionOverviewSheet`'s undersized `.body` title → `.title3`.
⚠️ All of it is CI-buildable but device-only for feel: the search expand/collapse + focus, the circular-key press, the picker's new chrome + stacked config sheet, the owned-tab query→catalog threading + auto-expand, and the detail-screen name wrap. See the search-filtering-ui-consistency branch.

**2026-07-18 — The rail ring-drag is now a universal range-unite: press ANY exercise, drag to any row, and everything between joins one superset** — Dave, in three tightening steps (bidirectional solo-join → ring-to-ring merge → "no matter which exercise is pressed, drag to the top or bottom and unite the whole span"). The final model generalizes and REPLACES the incremental deltas (`mergeSoloInto`/`absorbRing` and the `soloRunAfter`/`soloRunBefore`/`grabbedEdge` restriction were all interim and are deleted). The rule now: the pressed group is the ANCHOR (always survives, keeps its block config/uuid, never splits). TWO independent axes — **unite** is driven by the finger's POSITION (once it leaves the anchor group into a neighbour above/below, every WHOLE group spanned unites — solos AND existing supersets alike, to the list end), and **eject** happens only while the finger stays INSIDE the anchor, contracting from the pressed member's nearest edge (`grabbedEdge`, latched on first movement — NOT the drag direction; Dave chose to keep edge-inward eject). Decoupling them is load-bearing: an early cut latched the edge from drag DIRECTION, which made a 2-member superset undisbandable via the rail and let a twitch-then-reverse drag silently disband a ring (swift-reviewer catch) — deriving eject from the pressed member and unite from the finger fixes both. Kit (`RailArrangement.swift`): `RingSpan` is back to `firstFlat`/`lastFlat` + `absorbBefore`/`absorbAfter` (now counts of whole groups, unrestricted) + `ejectFirst`/`ejectLast`; `RailRing.span` branches on `hit.group` vs the pressed group — outside → unite (absorb = group-index distance, span covers whole groups, edge ignored), inside → contract from `edge`. `grabbedEdge` restored; `moveRailGesture` latches it from the pressed member (recovered from `pressY`). App: the general `Routine.mergeGroup(_:direction:context:)` (any-size generalization of `mergeSoloGroup`, kept for the solo a11y callers) preserves member order (moved members FOLLOW the target's when merging up, PRECEDE when merging down); `commitRing`'s absorb loops call it once per spanned group (re-reading the index each pass as neighbours collapse in), so the pressed group absorbs the whole range in order. Eject stays `splitExercise`. The a11y block also offers "Merge with superset above/below" (gesture-free #164 parity) via `mergeGroup`. By-design: uniting discards the absorbed groups' own `sets`/`restSecondsOverride` — one block config wins, the anchor's. Kit 427 green on Linux (ring tests rewritten: contract-tail/head, contract-to-one-row, unite-over-solos both directions, unite-across-a-whole-ring both directions, ring+ring, drag-to-bottom-absorbs-a-trailing-ring, press-any-member-anchors-its-whole-group); +3 app `mergeGroup` model tests. ⚠️ Gesture-layer feel is CI-invisible (XCUITest bypasses gesture overlays) — needs Dave's on-device pass: press a solo / a ring member / anywhere, drag to the top AND the bottom, confirm the whole span highlights and unites in order and the landing plays; and that dragging an edge back inward still trims. — Direct manipulation should let you gather a superset from any adjacent pieces in one stroke, from any starting row; the earlier per-neighbour special cases were stepping stones to this single rule.

**2026-07-18 — Expanded in-header search splits clear from close (Apple's two-control pattern)** — Dave: when the search field is expanded from its icon, there was no way to empty the query without collapsing the whole field. The single `xmark` inside the field in `PushedHeader`'s `searchField` did three jobs at once (clear text, unfocus, collapse). Split it Apple-style into two distinct affordances: **(1) an in-field CLEAR key** shown only when the query is non-empty (`clearSearchButton`, label "Clear text") that empties the text and KEEPS focus (`searchFocused = true`, so the keyboard stays up and typing resumes); **(2) a separate CLOSE key** (`HeaderIconButton` with `xmark`, `dismissSearchButton` id preserved, label "Close search") placed OUTSIDE the field box in the header HStack, which clears + unfocuses + collapses as before. **The inner glyph is `delete.left` (backspace), NOT an ✕** — settled with Dave from a four-option exploration (backspace / "CLEAR" mono label / `xmark.circle.fill` / `eraser`): a second ✕ next to the close ✕ reads as a duplicate, and the backspace glyph says "erase what I typed," scoping the inner control to the text and the outer to the mode. The clear key carries a full 44 pt tap target (HIG floor) with the glyph trailing-aligned so it reads near the field edge; field trailing padding is conditional (`hasText ? 10 : 13`) and the field is now narrower to make room for the close key on its right (the title is hidden while expanded, so its centered-`ZStack` `.padding(.horizontal, 100)` math is unaffected). No smoke test touched — the only ids the tests drive (`routineCatalogSearchFieldToggle`, `searchField`) are unchanged; `dismissSearchButton` kept its id for continuity, `clearSearchButton` is new. App-target only; needs an on-device pass (the two-control layout across Dynamic Type, that clear keeps the keyboard up, that close still collapses). — Emptying a query and leaving search are two different intentions; fusing them forced a full collapse to erase one character, and a non-✕ inner glyph keeps the two controls from reading as the same button twice.

**2026-07-18 — The catalog design vocabulary, codified as shared components** — Dave, iterating on the equipment/exercise surfaces: two rules and a componentization. **(1) Two capsule tiers.** All-caps is reserved for section labels; a capsule is not a section label. So the **filter chips** (interactive — `FacetChip`/`MultiFacetChip`/`TrayFilterChip`/`SortChip`) drop the mono/all-caps for **sentence-case plain font** and keep their border + blue-fill-when-selected (they're buttons); call sites pass sentence-case facet names ("Kit"/"Type"/"Muscle"/"Gear"/"Equipment"). The **card/row data capsules** (non-interactive — a property shown on an item) get the **soft `surfaceRaised` fill, NO border** style the routine gear pills already use ("a stroked capsule reads as a button"), via a new `CardTagCapsule`; the routine pills were refactored onto it so it's one source of truth (its `fill` override carries the amber "gear the kit lacks" wash). **(2) Filters connect to their cards.** The property a filter or sort controls now appears as a matching `CardTagCapsule` on the items it narrows — the muscle group on exercise rows (↔ the Muscle filter), the category + the "N exercises" count on equipment cards (↔ the Type filter / Most-exercises sort). **(3) One representation per item.** How an item reads is aligned across surfaces via shared bodies: `ExerciseRowContent` (the Exercises catalog + the picker) and `EquipmentRowContent` (the equipment catalog card + the active-kit list), each in `Views/Components/CatalogItemRow.swift`. The two prior duplicated inline renderings (the picker's plain name+subtitle, the kit list's "N exercises · custom" mono text) collapse into the shared body. **Necessary exceptions** are parameters: the picker drops the chevron (`showsChevron: false` — a tap selects, not pushes), the kit list drops the in-kit glyph (`inKit: nil` — every row is in the kit there). Accessibility ids (`equipmentCard-<name>`, `favSwipe-<name>`), swipe actions, and tap targets stay with each call site (on the `SwipeRevealRow` / Button wrapper), so the smoke flows are untouched. **Deferred (a follow-up call):** the detail-header identity tags (BUILT-IN/CATEGORY) and the routine-catalog verdict chips ("YOUR GEAR ✓", "NEEDS X") are still all-caps — some read as labels rather than data, so whether they de-cap is Dave's call. **Open, parked:** whether the three tabs should reach container parity (routines = cards, exercises/equipment = rows) — decided to land this grammar-unification first and evaluate with all three side by side, since a large scannable catalog wants row density while a few rich composed routines earn cards. ⚠️ All device-only (pure visual/layout); app targets CI-verified. — One vocabulary, enforced by shared components instead of re-described per screen, so a filter, a card, and a row visibly belong to the same system.

**2026-07-17 — Build-94 feedback round: equipment catalog + onboarding polish, and the per-gear "Tracks" config removed** — Dave's device-pass notes on build 94. **Filters (one vocabulary):** the equipment catalog's five inline type chips (a second, non-mono chip shape next to the facet chips) read as uneven spacing, so they moved into a single TYPE tray trigger (`EquipmentTypeFilterSheet`, multi-select over `SeedData.equipmentCategories`, modeled on `MuscleGroupFilterSheet`) — now the whole row is KIT facet · TYPE tray · MUSCLE tray · a neutral `SortChip`. That both implements "type filter as a sheet like muscle" and fixes the spacing for free. **Sort:** the exercise count is a sortable property now, not just a capsule — SortChip offers Name (unchanged default: search-rank when querying, alphabetical when blank) / Most exercises (count desc, name tiebreak). **Card layout:** the "N exercises" capsule sat next to the chevron and read as the tap target, so it moved into the row's LEFT column beside the name; the in-kit state dropped its "in kit ✓" words for a right-side accent `checkmark.circle.fill` glyph in the slot the capsule left. **Category rename:** "Bodyweight anchors" isn't a real term (it held benches, racks, stations, and floor tools) → **"Bodyweight gear"** (enum case + rawValue; the accounting test keys on names, unaffected). **Equipment detail:** Add-to-kit is a **prominent toggle card** now (Dave: make it unmistakable that adding gear takes an action, removable from the same spot) — accent when on, removal left the … menu (which is custom-delete only now). The exercises/routines cross-links + "New exercise/routine with…" are **hidden during setup** (`EquipmentDetailScreen.isOnboarding`, passed from the catalog's `setupMode`) so onboarding stays on add-and-configure; the Equipment tab keeps the full #137 graph. **"Tracks" removed:** the per-gear metric-default config (`EquipmentMetricsSheet`, a 7-toggle grid added in the equipment-catalog PR) confused even Dave, who couldn't say why it existed. Ruling: metrics are a property of the EXERCISE, not the equipment — a barbell tracks nothing; a Bench Press tracks weight×reps — and the exercise editor already owns that choice (TRACKED VALUES) with full control. The sheet was the most overwhelming thing on the screen for near-zero real use, so it's deleted; the `metricsData`/`suggestedProfile` field STAYS on the model (existing overrides still load/export; new custom exercises still seed metrics from the gear type), so it's fully reversible. CONFIGURE now shows only "Weight step", and only for loadable gear (non-loadables get no CONFIGURE section). **Onboarding scroll:** the reveal-upward scaffold now pins step 1 (equipment) at the top of the scroll container on first open AND caps the below-step-1 headroom to one viewport minus the step's measured height (`.onGeometryChange`) minus bottom pad, so "step 1 at top" is the maximum downward scroll — it can't be pushed off the top; steps 2–3 stay above, reachable by scrolling up. ⚠️ All of this is device-only (gesture/scroll feel, the toggle, the sheet, the pinned scroll — none CI-visible); SmokeTests updated for the toggle (switch value, not "IN YOUR KIT ✓" text). — The catalog reads as one filter vocabulary with a real sort, gear is a thing you clearly mark that you have, onboarding can't lose its first step off the top, and a config that was confusing even to its author is gone with its data preserved.

**2026-07-17 — Exercises lose their "library": the Exercises tab IS the whole catalog, curated by favorites, with persistent filters** — Dave: an exercise isn't a thing you own or can access at a gym like a piece of equipment — it's a thing you choose to do. So there's no library to fill and no empty cold start; the tab lists the whole catalog (247 built-ins + customs), always, narrowed by filters and curated by favoriting. `Exercise.inLibrary` is **frozen** (the `Equipment.inLibrary` precedent — kept for store compatibility, no live read/write) and `Exercise.isFavorite: Bool = false` is the new curation (literal default, lightweight-safe). **Surface:** `ExercisesTabView` absorbs the catalog and `CatalogBrowseScreen` is deleted; rows favorite on a leading swipe (green FAV/neutral UNFAV, per-row `favSwipe-<name>` ids), delete customs on a trailing swipe (built-ins have no trailing action), tap into detail, and show a star when favorited; a star in the detail header (`favoriteExerciseButton`, accent when lit) replaces the old add/remove-my-exercises. **Filters persist** across launches (Dave: "set it and it stays") via namespaced `@AppStorage` (favorites, gear mode, picked gear, muscle groups; search deliberately not persisted — a stale invisible query reads as data loss). The **GEAR facet** has four mutually-exclusive modes (All / Can do now / Can't yet / Picked gear), the last opening a `GearPickSheet` over ALL equipment via a binding interceptor; the modes replace `showUnavailable` + availability-hiding wholesale (the catalog never hides by default now). **Consumers converted:** the picker draws from the whole catalog, favorites-first, with a FAVORITES chip (its library-escape row + `libraryCount` gate died); `RoutineCatalog.instantiate` and `WorkoutSession.saveAsRoutine` stop auto-joining a library; Operator's `find_items` `inLibraryOnly` → `favoritesOnly`, the digest's "catalog only" → "favorite", and a built-in "delete" unfavorites-or-explains (the catalog keeps it) with undo. **Interchange:** the export basis flips from `inLibrary` to "customs + annotated + favorited" (#328's "self-contained for what's yours" thesis preserved); `ExerciseDTO.isFavorite: Bool?` written-only-when-true (the `isOutdoor` precedent), `inLibrary` deprecated to parse-and-ignore (decode-tolerance test; PLATFORM.md note). **Upgrade continuity:** a one-shot `adoptLibraryAsFavoritesIfNeeded` favorites an upgrading store's in-library built-ins — UNLESS every built-in is in-library (the pre-#185 default noise) — so a user's curation and their synced repo's exercise files stay continuous across the export-basis change. **The populate offer (#204) is deleted outright** (Dave's call to bless the recommendation): with the whole catalog always visible there is nothing to populate, so equipment setup just marks done. ⚠️ Kit verified locally (363) + CLI (26); app targets are CI-verified. On-device pass needed: populated-store upgrade → favorites + repo-diff continuity; filters survive relaunch (and search doesn't); all four gear modes incl. the hand-picked tray; the favorite swipe/star; the picker at 247 rows; onboarding without the populate beat; Operator `favoritesOnly` dispatch. — The catalog stops pretending exercises are property; favorites are the honest curation, and the repo stays self-contained for what's genuinely yours.

**2026-07-17 — Equipment catalog rebuilt as browse-into cards with a leading quick-add; equipment detail leads with Add-to-kit and configures via sheets; "library" → "kit" with default kit `main`** — Dave's design (pick → tune → keep moving): the toggle-row browse made gear a checkbox when it's really a thing you set up. (1) `EquipmentCatalogScreen` replaces CatalogBrowseScreen's equipment kind: rows are cards tapping into the redesigned detail (pushed via `.navigationDestination(item:)` ON the browse — it is itself a boolean destination at every call site, so a value append would break back-pop, #291; the item destination is legal from all of them); a leading swipe-right reveals the quick add (SwipeRevealRow grew a dual-edge API — `SwipeRevealOpen` id+edge token, per-edge halfway-commit/flick laws shared, trailing-only call sites unchanged via a convenience init). **The gesture conflict and its law:** the full-width pop pan begins at ~10 pt and would win every rightward drag, so `PopGestureGate` learned an edge-only mode — while a screen declares `.leadingRevealHost(active:)`, back-swipe requires a start in the 44 pt edge band, on that screen only, handed back the moment detail pushes. Rows carry a quiet "N exercises" capsule + category caption, fed by ONE per-render pass over the exercise graph (the old browse scanned all exercises per row); filters are a KIT facet, a MUSCLE tray (gear whose exercises train the selection), and five inline type chips over a NEW static name→category table (`SeedData.equipmentCategories`, all 101 built-ins, accounting-tested like FormCues — no model column, no migration, no interchange ripple). (2) `EquipmentDetailScreen`: Add to kit at the top (primary act; "IN YOUR KIT ✓" once in; removal in the … menu), then CONFIGURE as sheet-per-value rows — Weight step reuses the set screen's `IncrementSheet` (same field, same copy; it was always the same value, two UIs), Tracks opens the new `EquipmentMetricsSheet`. **Built-ins became metric-configurable** — the `suggestedProfile` setter always supported the override (and configured built-ins already export); the read-only rendering was legacy UI, and the sheet carries reset-to-catalog (#136's revert precedent). Create-custom now saves synchronously and pushes the new gear's detail (configure right away; the save-first line is the tray-flicker law). (3) The user-facing term for an equipment library is **kit** across every equipment surface (tray, reveal, GEAR facet footer, browse/detail); `EquipmentLibrary` the type and the interchange's `program/equipment-libraries/` path are frozen internals. The default kit is **`main`** (plain first reading, git second; activity-neutral where "Home" wasn't): `EquipmentLibrary.defaultName` changed, and `SeedData.renameDefaultKitIfNeeded` (UserDefaults one-shot) renames ONLY a lone kit still named "Home" — multi-kit stores and renamed kits are curation and are never touched. Smoke coverage: onboarding's equipment step rewrote from toggle taps to card→detail→Add-to-kit→back, and a new leading-swipe regression test mirrors `revealDelete`'s jitter-absorbing shape. ⚠️ Gesture feel, the edge-only back-swipe, item-push correctness from all four call-site classes, and the Home→main one-shot are device-only. — A catalog you configure from, not just check off; one gesture grammar with the pop conflict resolved structurally; and the kit vocabulary landing in code the same day the voice doc defined it.

**2026-07-17 — Two onboarding-motion tweaks: the welcome key's chevron marches forward, and the Today setup scaffold reveals its steps upward one at a time** — Dave, on the first-open flow. **(1) The "Start building" key's single chevron blooms into a three-chevron forward march** (`WelcomeView.swift`/`IntroView`). The old ignition flew the lone chevron off to the right (`offset x: 44`, opacity → 0); now, when the key wipes green, two more right-facing chevrons slide out to its right (inserted via `.transition(.move(edge: .leading).combined(with: .opacity))` so they read as emerging from behind the resting one) and a lit highlight travels left→right across the trio — the lit chevron at full opacity, its neighbours dim (0.25) so the two that emerged stay visible as a track. Driven by a `chevronActive` index stepped 0→1→2 twice (`hop % 3`, 6 hops × 0.15 s, ending on the rightmost aimed at Today) inside the existing `launchTask`, BEFORE the `.success` haptic + dive — so the transition to Today is delayed ~0.9 s (Dave: "delay the transition for a sec so the user can see that"). Reduce Motion keeps the single static chevron and skips the march (opacity is gentle but the emerge is positional; WCAG 2.3.3), holding a half-second beat before the dive instead. `--uitest-reset` still short-circuits (`instant` → immediate `onFinished`); the welcome smoke test (`--uitest-welcome`, `instant` false) runs the real ~1.9 s ignition, well under its 10 s land-on-tabs timeout, and `welcomeStartButton` / "PlusPlus" are untouched. **(2) The Today setup timeline reveals upward, one step at a time** (`TodayView.swift`). The three setup steps keep their bottom-up commit order (schedule top, routine, equipment bottom); the CHANGE is the scroll. A fresh install now lands with step 1 (equipment, the bottom-most / first-to-do) seated at the TOP of the scroll area, its two siblings above it off-screen (reachable by scrolling up) — Dave settled on **reveal-upward** ("next step sits above previous") over a downward checklist. Each step carries a stable `.id()` scroll anchor (constant across its gated/ready/done states so identity never churns); the opening scroll targets `activeSetupAnchor` (the lowest incomplete step) instead of the today anchor during setup, and on returning to the Today root after finishing a step (`isTodayRootVisible` going true — the equipment screen, routine catalog, and schedule editor each complete a step behind a push) the next step, which sits above, smoothly scrolls up to the top (a `Theme.Anim.flourish(.easeInOut(0.5))` reveal, deferred a runloop so the pop settles). Because the bottom step can only reach the top with a screen of scrollable space beneath it, a viewport-tall `Color.clear` spacer is added below the steps during setup only (below the fold, gone with the scaffold at the first logged session). The returning-user path (no setup) is unchanged: `activeSetupAnchor` is nil, `openingScrollTarget` falls back to the today anchor, the spacer is absent, and the reveal handler no-ops. ⚠️ App-target only: both are pure on-device motion (inert under UI test / absent on CI) — the chevron march, the emerge slide, the reveal-scroll timing, and the per-step landing all need Dave's on-device pass. — A key that shows forward momentum before it commits, and an onboarding that walks you to the next step instead of dumping all three at once, both make the first open feel guided rather than static. **Follow-up (same day, Dave on the branch build):** (a) the key's label now rides in a fixed-width box sized to the longer string ("Start building", a hidden placeholder + trailing-aligned live label) so swapping to "let's go" can't change the text-box width and shove the chevron — the chevron stays put through the label crossfade. (b) The "setup N of 3" caption under the Today title was removed: the timeline steps already carry their own "N of 3" badges, so the header echo was redundant (the caption now simply drops during setup); `setupDoneCount` went with it.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot SUPPORT CLASS opened: the flat bench (`MascotSupport` + `MascotProp.flatBench`), the supine Bench Press as move #7, the five-points-of-contact invariant, and the analytic GRIP servo** — The first of the approved scale-out unlocks (bench/seat support was chosen as the highest-leverage next structure: ~25 pressing/seated moves wait on it). **(1) The support contract:** `MascotSupport` (in MascotCollision.swift beside `MascotGrip`) is the one source of truth for the bench — pad top height 0.28 (a human 43 cm bench scaled to the 1.15 m bot), half-extents, world placement, and the pad as three collision RAILS at mid-thickness whose radius equals half the pad thickness, so a torso capsule resting exactly ON the pad reads as depth-zero graze to the existing equipment sweep (lying on furniture and "equipment never inside the body" compose instead of fighting). The pad's foot end deliberately stops just past the glutes — the thighs angle down past it to the planted feet, and a longer pad catches them. **(2) The supine placement** came from the recipe's scan discipline, with three lessons now written into the recipe: the torso capsules' radius spread (pelvis 0.075/abdomen 0.08/cowl 0.085) means a LEVEL body can't graze the pad everywhere — ~1.2° of head-up tilt balances all three contacts inside the band; the helmet out-bulges the back plane by 4 cm, so ~7° of chin tuck rests the head honestly ON the pad; and the legs reach the floor through hip EXTENSION (+21°, near the +25° anatomical stop) with the ankle closing the chain to a flat sole. Arms were solved by coordinate descent to the bar line: palms exactly on it at both ends (grip 0.0° off axis), TEXTBOOK vertical forearm (elbow under the bar in the side view — the demo camera) at the chest touch, full-reach lockout stacked over the shoulder line. **(3) The five-points law** (`benchMovesKeepFiveContactPoints`): head, upper back, and glutes within a graze-to-12 mm band of the pad top and both soles on the floor, at EVERY frame of the whole cycle — rest beat included, which forced the bench its own quiet rest beat (the standard happy-tired "phew" tips the chest proud and the chin up, which lying down would drive INTO the pad; supine tired is a shoulder shrug and a sideways glance). Plus `benchPressTouchesTheChestAndLocksOut`: bar within 12 mm of the cowl at the touch, over the chest, ≥0.24 m of travel, elbows ≥−12° at lockout, bar stacked over the shoulders (±3 cm). **(4) The GRIP servo** (`MascotPoseBuilder.aligningGrip`), the round's structural find: a joint-space lerp between two perfectly-gripped endpoints swings the hands up to 34° OFF the bar axis mid-press, so barbell spans re-aim the wrists at every baked sample. Two hard-won rules live in its implementation: the alignment objective must be SIGNED — under the invariant's `abs()` a 180° hand flip reads as perfectly aligned, and a searcher hops between the two branches on adjacent samples (an 11 rad/s wrist snap) — and greedy per-sample search is NOT a continuous map even with a fixed sign, so the servo is ANALYTIC (Rodrigues minimal rotation carrying the current grip axis onto the bar axis, conjugated into the wrist's local frame via the new `Mat3.transposed`/`Mat3.eulerAngles`, round-trip-pinned to the rotation order contract). Left wrist solved, mirrored to the right: requires and preserves exact bilateral symmetry. **(5) Renderer:** bench pad + legs built from `MascotSupport` (equipment green over dark legs), and a third camera framing class — supine moves read from the side at bench height (`rootRotation.pitch < −π/4`). Kit 410 tests green on Linux (407 → 410). ⚠️ Needs on-device validation with the next mascot build (dispatch still held): the bench read (pad size, leg look), the supine silhouette, bar-to-chest depth perception, the grip through the press arc, the quiet rest beat. Scale-out note: incline/decline benches are a pad-angle parameter on this contract; seats are the same contract with a shorter pad + backrest.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot build-88 feedback round: natural pauses become an invariant, the deadlift learns its first pull, cross-trainer feet, the straight-line law, muscle-suggesting lathes with collision parity, and an infinite orbit** — Dave's build-88 device pass, six items, each fixed at the structural level. **(1) Natural pauses:** the curl rolled straight from rep to rep. Every rep move now dwells at BOTH turnarounds (the curl gained an exact-copy bottom dwell wrapping the loop seam; the calf raise a bottom beat), and `everyRepPausesAtItsTurnarounds` makes it a law: at least two genuinely-still windows of ≥4% of the rep each, seated where the load's height actually bottoms and tops out (±12 mm). The window-LENGTH bar is what gives the test teeth — an eased reversal grazes zero speed for an instant; only an authored dwell holds it. **(2) Deadlift first pull:** build-88 showed the bar deflecting around the knees ("that looks painful" — correct, it isn't proper technique; the KNEES move out of the bar's way, the bar path stays vertical). The move gained a knee-pass waypoint (hip −40/knee 44, back angle UNCHANGED from the floor: knees extend first, hips stay closed) staged on both sides of the bottom via a numeric scan, servo-enforced to ≤5 mm graze. **(3) Feet:** reshaped to a smooth cross-trainer silhouette (0.16 m long, low profile, heel ~30% behind the ankle) — the landmarks live in the SKELETON (`soleHeelOffset`/`soleBallOffset`/`toeCapFrontOffset`) and skeleton, collision capsules, support polygon, and renderer meshes all read the same numbers; the ankle sphere slimmed 0.038→0.03. **(4) The straight-line law:** the push-up read hips-sagging/head-craned. Push-up AND plank were rebuilt around an honest line (hip pitch 2°, near-neutral gaze-down neck) on a toe-anchored IK closure — the toes are the pivot and never slide; the body pitch is bisected for wrist height and the shoulder solved for reach (the previous wrist-anchored interpolation swept the toes through a 3 cm arc). `floorMovesHoldAStraightLine` enforces it geometrically: chest–hip–knee and hip–knee–ankle within 8° of collinear, the head within 12° of continuing the line, at every working frame (the tired beat's proud chest-lift is exempt on purpose). **(5) Muscle pass:** `MascotMeshes.muscle` — a generalized Catmull-Rom-profile lathe (the plate lathe's vertex emitter extracted and shared) — sweeps each limb with a muscle-suggesting radius curve (deltoid cap 0.034, forearm swell, quad 0.042, calf 0.036) and narrows the abdomen to a waist (x-scaled lathe), per Dave: "a bit more human like shape … some approximation", not an anatomical model. The mesh↔capsule parity law held: `MascotCollision.segmentRadii` now carries the swell MAXIMA, and the suite stayed green without pose retuning because the path servos re-solve against the fatter capsules at animation-bake time (the deadlift bar rides ~6 mm further out on its own). **(6) Infinite orbit:** the azimuth clamp existed because the room had three walls; the room got its fourth (+z 2.5 m, beyond the 2.2 m camera radius) and the clamp died — the orbit now spins the full circle in either direction, forever. Kit 380 tests green on Linux (378 → 380). ⚠️ Needs on-device: the shoe read, the muscle silhouette in both color schemes, bar-past-the-knees, the curl's bottom beat, the push-up/plank line, full-circle orbit feel.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot capability round (Dave's picks): eccentric tempo enforced, the servo/rep-cycle promoted into the authoring layer, a contact-derived support polygon, the FOREFOOT HINGE — and the sixth move (Single-Leg Calf Raise) proving all of it at once** — Five improvements Dave selected, landed as one round. **(1) Eccentric control:** the lowering half of every rep is now deliberately slower than the drive ("control the negative" — textbook tempo the animation itself teaches), enforced by `theEccentricIsControlled`: the load's peak downward speed stays under 0.9× its peak upward speed on all rep moves. **(2) The authoring layer** (the scale-out play — real, present duplication only, per the no-premature-abstraction law): `MascotPoseBuilder.coordinating` is the ONE path servo (CoM over feet + bar over midfoot + equipment clearing the legs, per baked sample; the squat's and deadlift's near-identical local functions collapsed onto it) and `repCycle` is the shared descend-pause-drive-settle constructor with the slower eccentric in its defaults.
