Full archetype builders (squat-family, hinge-family…) wait for their second member. **(3) Balance got honest about geometry:** `MascotBalance.supportPolygon` derives the support region from what is ACTUALLY touching (sole corners + palm pads within 2 cm), x and z both — the invariant now checks the CoM inside it, so a single-leg stance narrows the polygon to one foot and a heel raise shrinks it to a toe cap, automatically. **(4) The forefoot hinge:** `leftToe`/`rightToe` joints at the ball line (ankle-local (0, −0.022, 0.08); zero angle reproduces the rigid foot EXACTLY, the clavicle pattern), split foot meshes + split rearfoot/toe-cap collision capsules (mesh↔capsule parity), sole landmarks re-homed (cap front corner lives in the TOE frame). **(5) The proving move:** Single-Leg Calf Raise — weight shifts over the stance foot (hip adduction, ankle-roll countered), sways forward onto the ball, and pivots the heel up AROUND the anchored toe joint while the cap stays flat; at the top, the polygon IS one toe cap and the CoM must live there. First asymmetric move (the symmetry invariant's promised exemption), authored with `anchored(.leftToe)` as the pivot solve. Two sign inversions caught by invariants during authoring — plantarflexion is POSITIVE ankle pitch on this rig, and hip EXTENSION (not flexion) sways an anchored-foot body forward — now pinned in **docs/recipes/mascot-move-authoring.md**, the new recipe capturing the whole authoring loop (archetype → intent → scan → solvers → sweep), the sign conventions, the shared physical contracts, and what every invariant demands. Kit 378 tests green. — This round is the scale-out dress rehearsal: a genuinely novel movement pattern (unilateral, pivoting, shrinking support) landed with zero new invariant exemptions beyond the designed one, using only promoted shared machinery.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot full-ROM round: below-parallel squat, a deadlift that pulls FROM THE FLOOR, full curl arc — and path SERVOS that keep mid-rep frames as honest as the endpoints** — Dave: "make sure the mascot is getting proper full range of motion on all applicable exercises — it should go a bit deeper into the squat, for instance." The audit found two moves teaching partial ROM: the squat stopped a thigh's width ABOVE parallel, and the deadlift bottomed at knee height — a rack pull wearing a deadlift's name. Both got scanned full-depth bottoms (the same numeric-scan discipline as the rack: every candidate holds balance, bar path, collision clearance, floor contact, and legal joints simultaneously): the squat now sinks the hip crease BELOW the knee (hip −100°, knee 135°), and the deadlift catches with the plates ~8 mm off the floor (hip −92°, knee 112°, 85° of hinge). The curl opened to a −5°…−132° arc. Each has a matching ROM invariant (hip-below-knee at depth; bar within 2 cm of plate-rest height, and never in the floor; ≤10° extension / ≥128° flexion), so shallow reps are now CI failures — push-up depth was already enforced, the plank is a hold. **The structural lesson: deeper endpoints exposed that a joint-space lerp between two LEGAL poses is not itself legal** — mid-descent the hips travel back faster than the torso leans, dragging the deadlift bar 2.3 cm through the knees and sagging both moves' center of mass behind the heels. The fix is per-sample PATH SERVOS in the baked spans (the push-up's grounded() pattern, generalized): the deadlift eases its shoulders forward until the bar clears the leg capsules and leans the spine until the mass is back over the feet; the squat leans the spine until bar AND center of mass sit over the midfoot — identity at the endpoints so the pause seams stay exact, densely baked (24 knots) so the smoothing spline can't dip between corrections. This is real biomechanics, not a hack: lifters coordinate continuously; the servo IS that coordination. To power it, the mass model moved from the tests INTO Kit (`MascotBalance` — segment masses + bar mass + centerOfMass), one source of truth shared by invariants and authoring, same as `MascotGrip`. 377 Kit tests green. — Full ROM is the actual product promise of a form demo; a mascot that squats high teaches a high squat, and now the depth of every move is a test, not a hope.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot: the clavicle YOKE — the shoulder girdle got its visible structure** — Dave, on the round-3 note that the shoulder ball could part from the chest cowl under scapular motion: the arms must never read as detached; if the rig needs a structure to properly demonstrate form (a scapula), give it the structure. A charcoal yoke segment now spans each clavicle — from inside the chest cowl out through the shoulder ball, parented to the clavicle PIVOT, so girdle rotation (a shrug, the back-squat rack's retraction) carries the shoulder WITH its structure and no angle can open a gap — with a matching clavicle→shoulder capsule in `MascotCollision.segmentRadii` so the invariants see the same body the pixels show. The racked bar clears the new volume inside the 8 mm graze (the existing sweep verified it; no rack retune needed); 377 Kit tests green. Ships in build 86 (runs 83-85 were parallel main/Operator builds — the run number IS the build number). — The standing rule this cements: **a body part exists in BOTH the renderer and the collision model, or in neither** — mesh↔capsule parity is what keeps "nothing clips" a provable claim as the rig grows.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot round 3: the rig gained the human shoulder girdle (never work around a missing DOF), the floor contract moved to the real mesh surfaces, and the invariant set grew self-derived motion-quality + dynamics (gravity) rules** — Dave's build-81 feedback (proper grip, nothing through the floor, joints bend only human ways, cue pacing) plus two overriding laws he set mid-round: **the mascot must be able to do ALL movements a human can** (when the v2 back-squat rack proved unreachable with legal joints, the WRONG fix — shipped briefly as a front rack — was changing the exercise; the RIGHT fix was upgrading the rig), and plan ahead for dynamic moves (jumps, swings, throws) and complex equipment (bands, kettlebells, rowers) with real physics: gravity, inertia, elasticity. What landed: **(1) Clavicles.** `MascotJoint` grew `leftClavicle`/`rightClavicle` between chest and shoulders (the old chest→shoulder offset split at the girdle; zero angles reproduce the old rig exactly, so no other move changed). Scapular elevation/retraction is what a back rack leans on — with it, the numeric scan (60k samples + coordinate descent over the 9-DOF arm space) found a legal behind-the-neck rack: palms ON the bar line at the traps (~3 mm deliberate graze — a bar RESTS there), grip axis 5.6° off the bar, elbows folded the proper way pointing down-back. Wrist yaw was re-understood as true forearm pronation/supination (the forearm axis IS the wrist frame's local Y) and ranged ±90°. The squat is a back squat again, with the standing hold carrying a subtle honest lean: this bot's spine is its body CENTERLINE (a human's is dorsal), so a trap rack sits ~10 cm behind the neck axis and the incline is what keeps the loaded bar over the foot — bar path, balance, and rack position all invariant-enforced. **(2) The floor contract got honest.** Three modeling lies died: the rest pose stood 2.7 cm SUNK (root rest height now puts soles exactly at y=0); the foot collision capsule ran ankle→pointed-toe-reach (a solver target dangling 9 cm below a standing sole — now a capsule along the real sole line); and the toe solver targeted that same reach point, leaving the actual toe corner of the foot mesh 4–5 cm under the floor in every push-up/plank frame. The solver now plants the SOLE CORNERS — and because the sole-height curve is non-monotone in ankle pitch (two foot attitudes reach most heights), it scans for crossings and picks the branch nearest the authored ankle angle: **the author's eyeballed value states intent; the solver refines it to exact contact**. Same honesty for hands: the grip-channel palm offset is not a floor-contact point — a new `MascotGrip.contactPadOffset` (the flat hand's underside) is what floor invariants measure, the push-up wrists rose to put the hand mesh ON the ground (re-solved endpoints: bottom pitch 77.5°, hip 15.5°), and a `MascotDynamics.handsBearWeight` flag lays the renderer's fingers flat instead of the relaxed half-curl that dug fingertips in. **(3) Anatomy as a table:** per-joint (pitch, yaw, roll) ranges for a reasonably fit human, left-canonical with mirrored twins negating yaw/roll, swept across every frame of every move. **(4) Self-derived quality invariants** (nobody asked; any trustworthy demo needs them): no self-collision, exact bilateral symmetry for symmetric moves, the bar stays level, no joint faster than 8 rad/s, effort peaks while the load RISES, something always touches the ground, synced cues cover actual motion, tempo bounds. **(5) Dynamics scaffolding for the catalog's future:** `MascotDynamics.airborneWindows` declares deliberate flight; the ground-contact invariant exempts those windows and a BALLISTIC invariant takes over — the root must fall at 9.81 m/s² (±25% for spline smoothing) and must genuinely leave the ground — proven live by a synthetic jump test whose half-gravity "floaty" twin is rejected. Inertia (swung kettlebells: load path curvature vs effort), elasticity (bands: effort tracks stretch, anchored force direction), and machine constraints (rower seat/treadmill belt as kinematic rails + support surfaces) are the named next steps in this framework — each becomes a declared property on `MascotDynamics` with a paired invariant when the first such move lands. **(6) Cue pacing:** `MascotCue.window` became optional — nil = STATIC (always listed, never flashing); each move carries 1–2 synced cues with windows ≥ 30% of a rep, ≥ 1 static, test-enforced (build-81: fast-cycling highlights were unreadable). Bar-position tests now measure the PALM midpoint (where the renderer puts the bar), not wrist joints — the old measure hid a real 2 cm deadlift bar drift, caught and re-tuned (lockout arms −15°, not −16: the tired beat's chest lift swings a hanging bar forward). Kit 324 tests green on Linux; app renderer consumed the new constants (flat planted fingers, stage top at y=0). Build 82. — The through-line: every feedback item became a MODEL fix plus an INVARIANT, never a pose tweak — the rig does what humans do, the floor is where the meshes say it is, and the physics rules the ~250-move scale-out will need (gravity first) now exist with a proof harness before the first jump is ever authored.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot: equipment can never pass through the body — a general collision invariant, with grip geometry shared Kit↔renderer** — Dave's build-81 follow-up ("make sure the equipment never passes through any parts of the mascot's body") generalized round 2's narrow bar-vs-hip check into full equipment-vs-body collision: `MascotCollision` (Kit) models the body as capsules over the FK frames (radii mirroring the renderer's mesh volumes; the head a sphere; **hands and forearms deliberately excluded** — gripping IS contact) and the equipment as capsules (bar shaft + plates along the palm-to-palm axis; dumbbell handles + heads in each wrist frame), on a new `mascotSegmentDistance` primitive. The invariant samples every propped animation's full cycle and allows ≤ 8 mm of grazing contact (a deadlift bar deliberately rests against the thighs; resting ≠ passing through). **The grip geometry moved into Kit (`MascotGrip`)** — palm/dumbbell offsets and every prop dimension — and the renderer now builds its meshes and solves the bar transform FROM those constants, so the proof and the pixels share one source of truth and cannot drift. First run caught two real clips the eye hadn't: the deadlift bar 3.9 cm inside the thigh at the bottom (the bot's short arms put the bar at knee height; fixed with arms 8° forward of plumb) and the curl's inner dumbbell heads 3.4 cm inside the thighs when hanging (fixed with 12° arm abduction — which is also just how humans hold dumbbells). Kit 313 tests green on Linux; build 82 ships the corrected poses. — Like the round-2 physics rules, this is scale-out insurance: all ~250 future moves get collision-checked for free, and a clipping prop is a CI failure, not a TestFlight screenshot.

**2026-07-16 — Mascot round 2 (build-80 device feedback): textbook form became INVARIANTS, the camera became ours, and the bot got its look** — Dave's build-80 pass surfaced 11 issues; the fixes hardened into structure. **(1) Physics/form as Kit tests, not eyeballs:** new invariants — toes touch the ground and stay planted (floor moves), a volume-weighted center of mass stays over the feet (standing moves; strict at held positions, a few mm of heel-edge tolerance mid-transition — dynamic balance is real), the bar tracks the midfoot and never intersects the torso (barbell moves), push-up depth + neutral neck. The poses were re-authored until green: squat rebalanced (thighs to parallel, knees over toes, 45° torso — the first cut's hips-33-cm-back bottom genuinely would have tipped), deadlift lockout arms ~16° forward so the bar rests on the thighs (it was inside the belly), and the push-up rebuilt around toe-pivot physics: a per-sample body-pitch solve keeps hands AND toes pinned (solved constants live in the move file; three hard-won solver lessons — a sign-flipped feedback gain back-flipped the bot 220°, independent per-sample ankle solves hop the ankle equation's two roots and kink the spline, and the mass model must be THIS bot's mesh volumes, not human tables: its head is ~8 L). The skeleton grew **big cartoon feet** — deliberately: the support polygon is what lets chunky proportions squat deep and balance (ASIMO's feet are huge for the same reason). **(2) Motion smoothing:** `MascotSmoothing.curved` — cubic Hermite, Catmull-Rom tangents, zero tangents at pause knots — replaced the chained ease-in-outs that stopped dead at every keyframe ("a bit jerky"). **(3) Happy-tired law:** the end-of-set beat is chin-up, chest-proud, slow breath — never a slump; tired eye lids stay LEVEL (half-closed = serene; the droop tilt read sad). The mascot always looks happy, even tired. **(4) The demo camera is hand-rolled:** `.realityViewCameraControls(.orbit)` ignored the authored `PerspectiveCamera` on device (the plank demo opened inside the mascot's face) and its pinch zoom was unbounded — replaced with our own orbit+pinch (clamped elevation/radius, per-move default framing matching the inline card's proven angles, camera always on the mascot). Flagged unknown #1 from round 1: resolved, in the bad direction, hence owned. **(5) The look:** matte white panels over charcoal joint spheres (ASIMO-adjacent, not a copy), the green ++ eyes EMBEDDED in a dark face panel (they floated off the face), equipment in brand green with bar shafts a darkened accent, everything matte (no metallic), weight plates as rounded-edge cylinders via a code-generated lathe mesh (`MascotMeshes.roundedCylinder`, MeshDescriptor revolution — still zero bundled assets, emitted double-sided so a winding mistake can't render invisible), and a procedurally-drawn dot-grid room (CGContext → TextureResource; no texture files). Kit 311 tests green on Linux. — Form quality is the product here; encoding "textbook" as executable invariants means the 250-move scale-out inherits the same guarantees, and every regression Dave caught by eye becomes a test failure the next time.

**2026-07-16 — Routines-tab card rebuilt, its entrance calmed, the catalog stops re-offering added routines, and a routine now carries its own one-line description** — A live-feedback pass with Dave on the Routines library. **(1) The card is three rows** (Dave: "3 rows max"): name + chevron; a description row; then a facts-and-gear row (`📅 cadence · ~estimate` + gear). The old flat stack (schedule pill identical to gear pills, a separate muscles line, workload counts) read as undifferentiated pill soup — schedule looked like gear, and a pill next to the chevron read as the tap target. Now schedule is icon-led (calendar), gear are SOFT TAGS (filled `Theme.surfaceRaised`, amber `Theme.notes.opacity(0.14)` when unavailable — no stroke, because a stroked capsule read as a button beside plain-text rows), set/exercise counts dropped. **Cardio** routines read "cardio" instead of a meaningless "full body" (`isCardio` = every exercise's `metricProfile` tracks `.distance` or `.pace`), and a gearless run/walk drops the synthetic "bodyweight" tag entirely. **(2) The just-added entrance stopped clipping**: the old `scaleEffect(1 + 0.03·entrance)` grew the card past its row width so the List clipped its left/right edges (border and all) until it settled. Replaced with a fade: the new card is held OUT of the `ForEach` (`displayedRoutines` filter on `revealNewCard`) for a ~300 ms beat, then `withAnimation` flips it in so it cross-fades while the cards below slide down; the green creation-ring flash fires ~340 ms AFTER, once it's landed (a cancellable `flashTask`, cancel-on-disappear so a recycled row can't inherit it). No scaling at all, so nothing can clip. `moveRoutines` rebased onto `displayedRoutines` so `.onMove` indices match the collection the ForEach shows (swift-reviewer LOW). **(3) The catalog hides already-added routines** (Dave bug: a routine in the library still showed as addable, because "Added" was only local view state) — `filtered()` excludes templates whose name matches an existing routine (the key `instantiate`'s uniqueName dedups on); a routine renamed away from its template frees the template again. **(4) A routine carries its own `summary`** (Dave: the catalog's brief descriptions were the routine's voice, and `instantiate()` was throwing them on the floor). New optional `Routine.summary` (lightweight additive column — existing rows migrate as nil, no backfill; the swiftdata.md law, no `= UUID()` shared-constant hazard since there's no default) + additive `RoutineDTO.summary` (writer emits it when present, absent round-trips a pre-field file unchanged; census + completeness test + PLATFORM.md prose/example updated, Kit 360 + CLI 26 green on Linux). `instantiate()` copies the template's curated one-liner onto the routine; the card's description row shows it (falling back to the muscles/cardio line when a routine has none), mirroring the catalog's name / description / meta shape so the two surfaces stop diverging. In-app EDITING of the summary is deferred (templates seed it, the repo file is editable, an in-app field is a follow-up); template provenance (a `templateID` for rename-proof dedup) also deferred. ⚠️ App-target only: the card layout across Dynamic Type, the fade/flash entrance, the cardio/gear suppression, the catalog dedup on return, and the store migration adding `summary` all need the on-device pass CI can't give. — The library card and the catalog row are the same routine; making the card speak the routine's own description (instead of discarding it on add) and read as facts-not-buttons closes the disconnect Dave felt, and a fade that never exceeds full size can't clip its own edges.

**2026-07-16 — Set screen: every configurable metric is a card, and the stepper increment is adjustable mid-workout as an EQUIPMENT property (#391)** — Dave, on a set-screen screenshot: reps sat as a cramped bottom row while weight got a full card; "reps should go in a card like weight does, same for anything else configurable." And separately: mid-set you sometimes realize you need a finer stride (2.5 lb microplates instead of 5), so make changing the increment doable during the workout, "not just for weight, but any steppable value." **(1) One card per metric.** `SetLoggingView` retired `repsRow`/`secondaryRow`/`stepperKey`; ALL configurable metrics now render through one `metricCard` (formerly `bigMetricCard`) — mono label, big value opening the wheel, live "last · Δ", two full-width stepper keys, carry-forward note. Rep work stacks WEIGHT/ASSIST then REPS; cardio leads with its driver; secondaries follow as more cards. Reps unified onto the generic `SetLog.actual/target/setActual(.reps)` accessors, so its own wheel/row machinery (`showingRepsWheel`, the reps-only `RepTargetWheelSheet` binding) went away. **Layout:** the header extracted to a computed `exerciseHeader`; the rep/cardio stage bottom-anchors above Log set via the established `GeometryReader { ScrollView { VStack{…}.frame(minHeight: proxy.size.height) } }` pattern (the pausedView/RestView idiom), so short content hugs the CTA and a tall stack (big Dynamic Type, many metrics) scrolls instead of shoving Log set off-screen. **(2) The stride is an equipment property — reused, not reinvented.** Settled with Dave after two false starts: the increment persists to the long-standing `Equipment.weightStep` (resolved through `Exercise.weightStepOverride`, the min stride across loadable gear), NOT a new per-exercise or per-session override — "step size should be only an equipment property." So there is **NO schema/interchange/migration change**: an earlier draft that added an additive per-exercise `stepOverridesData` (and a matching `ExerciseDTO.stepOverrides`) was fully reverted once Dave clarified. Three small helpers on `Exercise` centralize it: `stepOverride(for:)` (the resolved stride, load metrics only), `canAdjustStep(for:)` (gate — true only for weight/assist with loadable gear), and `setStep(_:for:)` (writes the chosen value onto EVERY loadable piece so the min-resolution stays honest and the change travels with the gear wherever it's used). Because it's a gear property, adjusting it deliberately applies to every exercise on that equipment — the whole point of "equipment property." Only weight/assist get the affordance; other metrics have no equipment-backed stride (a follow-up could give `Equipment` a per-metric step map, considered and deferred as scope Dave didn't ask for). **(3) The interactions.** An increment icon button in each load card's upper-right opens `IncrementSheet` — plate-shaped presets from a new pure-Kit `WorkoutMetric.stepChoices(weightUnit:distanceUnit:)` (Linux-tested), current stride lit, tap-to-apply-and-persist. And press-and-hold on the ± keys auto-repeats the step until release (`HoldRepeatKey`): the tap stays a plain `Button` (reliable, accessible, XCUITest-drivable), the hold rides one `.onLongPressGesture(perform:onPressingChanged:)` — `perform` starts a repeat `Task` at the 0.3 s threshold, `onPressingChanged(false)` stops it. **swift-reviewer caught two gesture defects in the first cut** (two independent simultaneous gestures): (a) the repeat leaked — a bare `DragGesture.onEnded` never fires when a scrolling ancestor CANCELS the child drag, so a hold-then-scroll left the value climbing on its own; `onPressingChanged` fires on both release AND cancel, closing it; (b) a hold appended one extra step on release (the Button's tap-up fired after the repeat), now swallowed via a `didRepeat` flag. Cancelled on disappear (the deferred-beat rule). **(4) One standardized config icon button.** Dave: use the SAME SF Symbol app-wide for every "configuration icon button." The app had no existing adjust glyph (`ellipsis` is the options MENU affordance, settings are labeled rows), so `ConfigIconButton` (new, `Views/Components/StepControls.swift`) fixes `slider.horizontal.3` — iOS's conventional adjust-settings glyph (confirmed via the Axiom design skill) — in ONE place; every future config icon button draws `ConfigIconButton.symbol`, so consistency is enforced by construction. Kit 352 / CLI 26 green on Linux (new `stepChoices` tests). ⚠️ App-target only: the card layout at large Dynamic Type, the increment sheet, the press-and-hold repeat (a gesture-layer change XCUITest can't see — taps bypass the gesture overlay), and that a changed stride sticks to the gear for the next workout all need an on-device pass. — Reps and the machine-dial metrics deserve the same legible, thumb-sized control weight already had; and the stride belongs to your plates, so the mid-workout adjuster just surfaces the equipment property that already existed, from the one place you actually notice you need it.

**2026-07-16 — Voice cues: a spoken form-cue line as each exercise starts (three-way mode, default off)** — Dave asked for a voice giving form guidance at the start of an exercise; feature named "Voice cues" (Dave). Shape: **(1) content is a static curated table, not model output and not stored data** — `FormCues` (`Models/FormCues.swift`), one short line per BUILT-IN exercise with FULL catalog ACCOUNTING (257 = 247 cued + 10 `deliberatelySilent`, enforced by `FormCuesTests`: every SeedData row has a cue XOR a deliberate exclusion, and every key must resolve to a catalog name — the RoutineCatalogTests drift rule). The exclusions (Dave's instinct, generalized): steady locomotion + console cardio (Running, Walking, Cycling, Treadmill Run, Stationary Bike, Assault Bike, Elliptical, Stair Climber, Vertical Climber, Upper Body Ergometer) — continuous self-evident movement with no setup moment to coach; technique ergs (Rowing, Ski Erg) and skill cardio (Jump Rope, Heavy Bag) KEEP cues because sequencing is real coaching. Lines are setup/execution reminders only (≤ 120 chars, one sentence, imperative, anti-shame, house copy rules apply even though the text is spoken), and CUSTOM exercises stay silent — we can't know the movement behind a user's name, and a wrong cue is worse than silence (the isLoadable can't-classify-intent rule). Foundation Models generation was rejected: form advice is a safety surface, and the Operator law (the model proposes, the app disposes) argues even harder against a model speaking unreviewed coaching. **(2) Three-way mode, not a toggle** (Dave): `VoiceCueMode` — `always` / `refresher` / `off` (default OFF: an unasked voice is a surprise, and VoiceOver users already have a voice in the room; a garbage/unset preference parses to OFF). REFRESHER = speak only when the exercise is new to you or not done in a month (30 days): no completed set with that snapshot name in any finished session inside the window AND none earlier in the current session; the history scan is an autoclosure so it only runs in refresher mode. Settings tray → VOICE CUES renders it as SegmentedTabs (Every time · Refreshers · Off) with a caption that explains the SELECTED mode. **(3) The speaker is the app's first audio**: `VoiceCueSpeaker` (`Platform/`, the WorkoutActivityController singleton pattern, inert under `--uitest-reset`) wraps `AVSpeechSynthesizer` with `.playback` + `.spokenAudio` + `[.duckOthers, .interruptSpokenAudioAndMixWithOthers]` — the silent switch can't mute a cue (an apparently dead setting reads as broken), music ducks and comes back via `.notifyOthersOnDeactivation`, podcasts pause instead of overlapping. ALL audio work rides a private serial queue (swift-reviewer): `setActive` is blocking IPC and the trigger fires in the render pass that animates the SWITCH screen in, so it must stay off-main; deactivation is decided by an outstanding-utterance COUNT (never delegate delivery timing — didCancel has been seen arriving synchronously inside stopSpeaking) and RETRIES on a backoff because a swallowed busy-error would leave music ducked for good. NO `audio` background mode: backgrounded = no cue, acceptable v1. **(4) The trigger rides `activeExerciseKey`** (the GPS meter's re-base identity) in ActiveSessionView — the key flips to the up-next exercise the moment its transition starts, so the cue plays during the SWITCH countdown (racking over), never mid-set; same-block rounds are one key (announce once), superset partners are distinct keys, and dedup keys on persisted `startedAt` + block so view remounts can't re-announce within an app run (a relaunch mid-workout re-announces once — a serviceable "where was I"). A WATCH-driven finish also cuts speech (`.onChange(of: session.isFinished)`) — the mirror path never passes through the phone's finish button. **(5) Voice choice** (Dave): `VoiceCueVoice` stores an `AVSpeechSynthesisVoice` IDENTIFIER (empty = system default; a deleted voice falls back silently). The picker (a Voice row under the mode control, hidden while Off) lists the device's installed ENGLISH voices from `AVSpeechSynthesisVoice.speechVoices()` — compact/Enhanced/Premium tiers as distinct labeled entries (users download the better tiers in iOS Settings → Accessibility → Spoken Content → Voices, and the caption says so); novelty voices (a joke voice coaching form) and Personal Voice (needs its own authorization flow — fine follow-up) are filtered; Siri's voices aren't exposed to apps at all. Picking a voice speaks a sample cue (`preview()`) so it can be judged without starting a workout; the voice list is snapshotted per tray appearance (enumeration has real cost). **(6) Content is expert-audited** (Dave: "make sure the form tips are what a true expert would say"): all 247 lines reviewed by a six-agent PT/CSCS-framed audit panel (accuracy → novice-first priority → jargon → style law); 234 confirmed, 13 revised — jargon novices can't act on ("hit depth"/"sit to depth" → "until your thighs are parallel", "lats on" → "press down on the bar with straight arms", "full lockout" → "hips fully straight", "hips open" → "body straight from knees to shoulders"), missed top-priority setup/safety cues (Side Plank's elbow-under-shoulder, Heavy Bag's straight wrists, Good Morning's flat back), and ambiguity (Arnold's "palms in" → "palms facing you", Donkey Calf Raise's "finish tall" which could cue standing mid-rep). Watch speech deferred (the wrist's language is haptics). ⚠️ Speech/audio-session behavior is on-device-only — CI proves content accounting and compilation, not sound.

**2026-07-16 — The durable run record, PR 4: the record shows the run (map · stats · splits), and outdoor becomes a user-facing toggle (#378)** — The payoff surface, closing Phase 0 of the running push. **(1) `RunRecordSection`** (`Views/Components/`, mounted atop `SessionDetailView` when the session carries a run — gated on the SUMMARY, not only the sidecar, so a summary-without-route record still shows stats; indoor records render pixel-identical): a static MapKit `Map` (`interactionModes: []`, camera fitted to the track's padded bounding box) stroking one `MapPolyline` PER SEGMENT in `Theme.accent` — a recorded route is data, green, and a pause gap renders as a gap, never a phantom line; the headline stat line (`figure.run` distance · pace `/mi` · `↗` gain) in the record's mono caption ink from the denormalized columns (renders before the blob parses, and even when no sidecar exists); a Swift Charts `BarMark` pace-per-split chart + a splits table, BOTH in neutral ink with no fast/slow coloring and no per-split deltas (anti-shame: a slow mile is a fact, not a warning; the chart shows shape, not judgment). The GPX parses off-main in `.task` (`Task.detached`) — a long run's sidecar is ~1 MB of XML. First `import MapKit`/`import Charts` in the app — both first-party. Splits quote against the first outdoor set's snapshot `distanceUnit` (decoded profiles only), falling back to miles. **(2) The "Outdoor (GPS)" toggle** lands in the exercise editor under the distance vocabulary, shown only when the profile tracks distance or pace (`draft.canBeOutdoor` — the same pairing the validator enforces), flat per the press grammar, `Theme.selected` tint, with a plain-facts caption. The data plumbing (draft carry, suppression, interchange) all landed in PR 2 — this is just the visible switch. Display math (pace m:ss, split labels incl. honest partials, region fitting) pinned by unit tests; ⚠️ the rendered map/chart and the toggle flow need the Phase 0 on-device pass (#378 lists it; dispatch a TestFlight build from main after merge). — The record IS the reward for a run; showing the route in the data color and the splits without judgment is the whole grammar applied to running.

**2026-07-16 — The durable run record, PR 3: sidecars ride the sync file map byte-verbatim, pulled sidecars attach by pairing, and blob reads go through a SHA-keyed cache (#378)** — The repo half. **(1) The sidecar is just another path in the local file map**: `GitHubSyncCoordinator.localFileMap` places each GPS session's `routeData` bytes at `FileLayout.routeSidecarPath` beside the session JSON — verbatim, never re-encoded, in EVERY map (including the dirty-gate's, or a synced run would read dirty forever). The planner needs no special casing: local-only → pushed in the same commit as the session (SyncEngine's commit-message dedupe now strips extensions so a run commits as "Log workout", not "Log 2 workouts"); remote-only → pulled. **(2) Pulled sidecars attach conservatively** (`RouteSidecars.attach`, after `importBundle` so restored sessions exist): first by the JSON twin in the same pull set (exact identity — the restore case), else by the filename convention (date stamp + slug, numbered `-N` placement suffix stripped but the un-stripped form also tried for slugs genuinely ending in digits), onto FINISHED sessions with no route only, and only when exactly ONE candidate matches — a wrong route on the wrong record is worse than no map, and a skipped sidecar stays in the repo/base to pair on a later pass. The JSON summary is never recomputed from an attached sidecar. **(3) `GitBlobCache`** (Kit protocol, SHA-keyed): `GitHubRepoStore.fetchAll` re-downloaded every synced blob every pass — history grows monotonically and a GPX is ~100× a session JSON, so each sync re-paid the whole archive. Git SHAs are content-addressed, so a hit can never be stale (no invalidation story) and the tree listing supplies the key for free; writes warm the cache with the bytes just pushed. The app wires `DiskBlobCache` (Application Support/BlobCache, ~50 MB cap, LRU-approximated by mtime, pure re-derivable cache; SHA input path-sanitized). **swift-reviewer round (policy settled in-PR):** (a) **pulled bytes WIN** — the first cut never overwrote an existing route, but the engine records every pull into the base assuming it was applied, so a repo-side sidecar edit (the hackable ethos invites it) would read as a phantom local edit next pass and the app would push the STALE bytes back over the user's commit; adopt-on-pull is the only base-consistent policy. (b) **Pairing is deterministic, not heuristic**: the filename's `-N` ordinal names the Nth same-day session of that routine in start order — the SAME rule `sessionPlacement` used to mint the name (the bundle sorts sessions by `startedAt`, which also refutes the reviewer's placement-ping-pong HIGH: enumeration order is already deterministic across devices) — so the old ambiguity-skip class vanishes; an unresolvable ordinal is honest, not guessed. (c) **Unattachable sidecars are BANKED** (`OrphanSidecarStore`, Application Support, path-keyed): without holding the bytes, the base carries a path the local map never will, the dirty gate reads dirty FOREVER, and every edit boundary escalates to a full network pass; banked bytes ride the map verbatim, retry pairing every pass, and leave the bank the moment a session owns them. (d) The push lookup's `#Predicate` dropped its `routeData != nil` clause — external-storage attributes aren't reliably predicate-queryable and the `try?` would have silently no-opped the whole feature; `endedAt` filters in SQL, the route filter runs in memory, and an app test pins the lookup against a real store. (e) Hygiene: `DiskBlobCache` moved to Caches (re-derivable → never backed up, purgeable), and `disconnect()` clears both repo-derived stores. **Known cliff, deliberately deferred:** the dirty gate materializes every route blob per edit boundary — fine at v1 volumes, needs a digest/manifest comparison before plan-era mileage (#381). Kit 350 green on Linux; `RouteSidecarsTests` pin twin pairing, ordinal pairing, unresolved-ordinal banking, pulled-bytes-win, in-progress-never-matches, and the push lookup. ⚠️ Needs the on-device pass from #378: finish a GPS run → repo shows `.json` + `.gpx` in one "Log workout" commit; delete + reinstall → restore re-attaches the route. — Verbatim bytes in every map make sidecar sync a non-event for the planner; deterministic pairing beats conservative guessing; and the cache turns sync cost from O(archive) to O(new).

**2026-07-16 — The durable run record, PR 2: the phone persists the whole-session GPS track as verbatim GPX bytes on `WorkoutSession`, and the run summary + `isOutdoor` flow through the app's interchange mapping (#378)** — The capture/persistence half on the PR 1 contract. **(1) The canonical on-device route blob IS the GPX bytes** (`WorkoutSession.routeData`, `@Attribute(.externalStorage)`): the sync planner re-pulls any path absent from the local file map, so every device must reproduce sidecar bytes byte-for-byte forever — storing the encode-once bytes verbatim makes that trivial, preserves a foreign (hand-dropped/Strava) GPX through sync, and confines writer determinism to one moment per run; `RouteTrack` is parsed on demand for display, never re-encoded. Three denormalized columns (`runDistanceMeters`/`runMovingSeconds`/`runElevationGainMeters`, raw meters/seconds) give cards and the record header cheap truthful stats even when a sidecar never restored. All four are additive optionals with NO property defaults and NO backfill — nil is the truthful value for every pre-GPS and indoor session (the swiftdata.md lightweight-add law; the `= UUID()` shared-constant trap doesn't apply because there are no defaults at all). **(2) Segment banking fixes #348's last-segment-only limitation**: `RunLocationMonitor` banks the live segment into a session-scoped archive on `pause()` and `stop()` (re-base included), so an outdoor→strength→outdoor session records whole; the monitor's `@State`-per-session lifetime IS the archive's reset. `sessionTrack` (segmented, honest gaps) feeds the GPX; `sessionRoute` (flattened) feeds Health, whose single-polyline route can't encode gaps anyway. Accepted consequence, recorded in #378: a mixed run+strength session now classifies as `.running`/`.outdoor` in Health whenever ANY GPS segment exists, not only when a run came last. **(3) Fix hygiene at capture**: a 1 Hz cap (CLLocation burst deliveries would bloat the track and could collide whole-second sidecar timestamps; distance is chord-measured across skipped fixes, not lost) and altitude carried only when `verticalAccuracy` is in 0...25 m, so the elevation series the hysteresis smooths is only readings the receiver vouched for. **(4) Census flips**: `metricsData.isOutdoor` EXCLUDED→EXPORTED on Exercise + SetLog (riding the explicit-profile/carries-profile gates, written only when true); the three run columns EXPORTED via `SessionDTO.run` (both measurements or the field is omitted — a lone one is capture corruption we'd rather drop than validate into history); `routeData` EXPORTED as the repo-layout sidecar, deliberately NOT a bundle field, so its round-trip is the sync layer's to prove (PR 3), not the completeness test's. Known limitations carried from the plan: salvaged (crash-recovered) sessions lose the track (monitor is view-lifetime state), and watch-born sessions still carry no GPX (the watch rebuild #379 owns route sync-back). Unit tests drive `locationManager(_:didUpdateLocations:)` directly (banking, re-base, teleport/accuracy/1 Hz gates, altitude gating — hosted in the app so `allowsBackgroundLocationUpdates` is legal); the completeness test asserts the new fields. **swift-reviewer round (all fixed in-PR):** (a) the positive-measurement gate — a standing-still track (2+ fixes, zero meters) would have stamped `run.distanceMeters = 0`, which the validator rejects, and `importBundle` throws on ANY issue, so one degenerate run could fail a whole repo restore; now a degenerate track stamps nothing AND Health gets no route (the durable record and Health must not disagree about what counts as a run); (b) an `armed` disarm gate on the monitor — `stopUpdatingLocation()` doesn't guarantee no in-flight/batched delivery, and a post-pause straggler (with `lastLocation` freshly nil) bypassed both the 1 Hz and teleport gates, seeding the paused position and stitching phantom distance across the gap at resume; (c) the live `ExerciseDraft` isOutdoor-drop bug fixed NOW rather than with PR 4's toggle (exporting a silently-falsified `false` is worse than exporting nothing): the draft carries the flag through init/adopt/set, suppresses it when the last distance/pace metric is dropped (a bare flag fails validation — the same reason), and Operator's `ChangeInverse` restore threads it so an undo can't turn a run indoor. ⚠️ Real GPS capture, the pause/resume banking, and the Health classification change need the on-device pass listed in #378. — Verbatim bytes make sync determinism a non-problem by construction, and banking segments at every boundary makes the durable record match what the runner actually did rather than whichever stretch happened to come last.

**2026-07-16 — The durable run record, PR 1: a Kit `RouteTrack` + frozen GPX 1.1 sidecar codec, run summary + `isOutdoor` in the interchange (#378; running push plan settled with Dave)** — Phase 0 of the running roadmap (#378–#383): when a GPS workout finishes today, the track goes to Apple Health and is discarded — nothing durable in the app or the repo. This PR lands the platform contract; the app capture/persistence, sync sidecar wiring, and record UI follow (#378 lists the four-PR shape). **Contract decisions:** (1) **Routes are GPX 1.1 sidecars** — `history/YYYY/<same-basename>.gpx` beside the session JSON, paired by NAMING CONVENTION (`FileLayout.routeSidecarPath`), never a JSON link field: computable from a directory listing, zero byte-churn on session files, numbered `-2` suffixes pair for free. GPX because every running tool reads it (the hackable-data ethos: the raw track is usable outside PlusPlus by construction). (2) **The writer is frozen, hand-emitted strings** (`GPX.encode` — not an XML library; byte identity across macOS/iOS/Linux Foundation is a sync invariant), 6-dp coords / 0.1 m ele / whole-second UTC times, golden byte test; the reader is TOLERANT (XMLParser, accepts foreign files, fractional seconds, rtept; timeless points dropped). `RouteTrack.Fix` QUANTIZES at construction to exactly the writer's precision, so decode∘encode is an exact fixed point (tested). (3) **`SessionDTO.run` carries measurements only** (`distanceMeters`, `movingSeconds`, `elevationGainMeters?`) — splits/pace-curve are deliberately NOT stored: they're pure derivations of the sidecar, and append-only history could never correct a stored derivation if the algorithm improved; `RouteTrack.splits(per:)` ships the algorithm publicly instead. Also additive: `isOutdoor` on `ExerciseDTO` + set snapshots (written only when TRUE, riding the explicit-profile gate; validator flags a bare flag without a distance/pace metric — outdoor means "engage GPS", which needs a metric to feed). Schema stays v1 (everything additive, absent = pre-field meaning). (4) **`InterchangeFiles` now skips non-`.json` paths** — it force-decoded ANYTHING under `history/` as a `SessionDocument`, so the first pulled sidecar would have failed the entire sync pass; this guard had to land BEFORE any writer exists. (5) **Kit derivation choices, all pinned by tests:** haversine on the mean-radius sphere; moving time gated at 0.4 m/s (the `LivePaceMeter` floor, so the finish average agrees with the live readout); split seconds are WALL time within segments (standing at a light is part of what that km took) while gaps between segments never count; elevation gain = centered moving-median (radius 2) + **5 m deadband hysteresis** — 5 because the band must exceed noise PEAK-TO-PEAK: a periodic ±2 m altimeter toggle sails through any median filter (period-2 oscillation IS the window majority; a 3 m band accrued 72 m of fictional climb on a flat synthetic run), and undercounting a true climb by up to one band is the accepted anti-overstate cost; `elapsedSeconds(atMeters:)` is public deliberately — it's the odometer feed #380's segment auto-advance needs. Capture policy (for PR 2): 1 Hz fix cap, no thinning — a 2-hour run ≈ 7,200 points ≈ ~800 KB GPX; route fidelity is the product. Kit 330 / CLI 26 green on Linux; swift-reviewer's one MEDIUM (non-finite lat/ele from a hand-edited sidecar poisoning derivations) fixed by sanitizing in `RouteTrack.init`, plus a Darwin twin of the golden-byte test in PlusPlusTests so the byte freeze is pinned where iPhones actually run. — The record IS the product for a running app, and "your runs as files in your own repo" is the identity move no other running app can copy; the contract lands first so every later layer (capture, sync, UI, watch sync-back) writes against a tested, frozen format.

**2026-07-15 — The 3D exercise mascot: a code-defined RealityKit bot demonstrates form (prototype: Squat, Deadlift, Push-Up, Dumbbell Curl, Plank), with ALL pose/animation math in the Kit** — Dave wants exercise tutorials without hosting videos of humans; the answer is a friendly geometric bot that performs the movement in 3D. Design settled with Dave: primitives-only (rounded boxes/cylinders — zero binary assets, the whole character diffs in PRs and is buildable from any remote session); **the face IS the ++ mark** — two "+" eyes, no mouth, no chest mark — and the eyes are expressive: a blink collapses the plus's vertical stroke into a minus, hard phases squeeze them (an authored per-keyframe `effort` 0–1 channel), and the demo loops a SET (N reps, then an authored tired beat: slump, droopy eyes, a breath) rather than a bare rep; hands have three fingers and a thumb, cartoon rules. **The architecture split is the load-bearing decision: everything numeric lives in `PlusPlusKit/Mascot/`** (17-joint skeleton, hand-rolled `Vec3`/`Mat3` — no simd on Linux — keyframe engine with per-segment easing, the face channel as a pure function of set phase, deterministic authored blinks; no clocks, no random), **so every animation is validated by `swift test` on Linux**: seam continuity, no-teleport sampling, human-ish joint limits, FK floor/planted-feet/planted-hands checks, barbell wrist symmetry, face behavior, per-move semantics (~37 tests). A remote session can author and prove a new move without a Mac — the renderer is a thin app-side layer (`PlusPlus/Views/Mascot/`) that maps poses onto entity transforms. Two hard-won authoring lessons baked into the API: **interpolating two planted poses does not keep the feet planted** (FK is nonlinear; the first squat drifted its ankles 8 cm mid-descent) → transitions are baked planted paths (`MascotPoseBuilder.span`, re-solving every sample); and **the root-translation solvers (`plantingFeet`/`anchored`) are what make hand-authored poses honest** — author angles, solve the root. **Animation data attaches by exercise NAME string** (`MascotMoves.animation(forExerciseNamed:)`, mirroring `builtInProfilesByName`): no `Exercise` column, no migration, no interchange/DTO change, no census entry; custom exercises simply show no FORM section. **Renderer contracts:** the Euler→quaternion composition (`MascotPoseApplier.quaternion`) and Kit's `Mat3.rotation` are one contract — R = Ry·Rx·Rz intrinsic — pinned by an app-side parity test over an angle grid (the folded-inside-out bug class dies in unit tests); the mascot is **frozen** (static resting pose, open eyes) under Reduce Motion AND `--uitest-reset` — the app's `UIView.setAnimationsEnabled(false)` kill does NOT cover a RealityKit render loop, and XCUITest waits for quiescence — with the demo sheet swapping the loop for a discrete step-through (`stepPhases`), so the demo stays fully available without motion (WCAG 2.3.3). The rig drives per-frame from ONE `SceneEvents.Update` subscription (delta-timed; pose/face go straight to entities, observable state — active cues, rep index — publishes only on change); a rigid barbell can't parent to one hand, so it solves from both wrist world positions every frame. Surfaces: a FORM section (live inline `MascotFormCard`, fixed camera, hits disabled, paused offscreen/under-sheet/backgrounded) on `ExerciseDetailScreen` (above VIDEO — the native demo leads, the external link is the fallback) and `ExerciseDetailSheet`, expanding into `MascotDemoSheet` — orbit camera (`realityViewCameraControls(.orbit)`), REP n OF m caption, and the move's cues lighting up in notes amber (the form-cue color) exactly when the motion passes through them. Verified remotely: 307 Kit tests green on Linux; the app targets are compile-verified by the PR's macOS CI, and a new smoke flow (`testExerciseSheetShowsFormDemo`) proves the first RealityKit viewport initializes on a CI simulator + screenshots it. ⚠️ **Needs on-device validation** (the two RealityKit unknowns: whether `.orbit` respects the supplied `PerspectiveCamera`, and whether the viewport composites transparently over SwiftUI — fallbacks staged: `cameraTarget`-only framing / an Unlit backdrop plane; plus animation quality, materials in both schemes, scroll perf). Follow-ups deliberately not in the prototype: the remaining ~250 catalog moves (the authoring layer — spans, mirroring, shared sub-poses — exists for exactly that scale-out), an in-workout entry point, speed control. — Videos of humans cost hosting, licensing, and consistency; a code-defined character costs keyframes in a diffable Swift file, gets validated by tests instead of eyeballs, matches the app's 100%-code-defined aesthetic, and doubles as the brand: the thing demonstrating your workout is the ++ mark with a body.
**2026-07-15 — One forgiving search rule for every search surface: `FuzzySearch` in the Kit; discovery is fuzzy, applying changes never is** — Every user-typed search matched by bare `localizedCaseInsensitiveContains` before this: one typo ("benhc", "dumbell", "sqaut"), a missing space ("pushup", "benchpress"), or a gym abbreviation ("rdl", "ohp") returned nothing. Now ONE Kit rule (`PlusPlusKit/FuzzySearch.swift`, pure, Linux-tested) backs them all: fold case/diacritics, split on non-alphanumerics, and require EVERY query word to land somewhere in the candidate (order-free), where "land" is a scored tier ladder — exact word (1.0) > prefix (0.7–0.9, length-graded) > over-typed inflection ("presses"→Press, leftover capped at 2 chars so "deadlft" can't call Dead Bug home) > word-anchored-subsequence abbreviation ("rdl" walks Romanian→D…l, "ohp" reaches Overhead Press; 2–4 chars only, at 5+ you're spelling words and a misspelling must fall to the typo tier, not outrank its honest match) > mid-word substring (3+ chars) > Damerau-Levenshtein typo rescue against the best candidate-token PREFIX (trailing letters free, so "benhc" is 1 edit from "benchpress" too). Multi-word names also match as one glued token (small demotion) — that's the missing-space class. Symbol-only queries and names ("++", "💪" — a user CAN name a routine "++" here) compare literally on the folded text instead of falling out of the token system (swift-reviewer catch: the blank-query "nothing to narrow by" passthrough must not leak into `bestMatch`/find_items, where a token-free name would have resolved to an ARBITRARY routine — a confidently wrong stat — or listed everything as matches; `bestMatch` additionally resolves a blank query to nothing, never a default winner). **Typo budget is length-gated: 0 edits under 5 letters, 1 through 8, 2 beyond** — at 4 letters one edit made "carl" match the entire Cable family (proved against the real 351-name catalog with a scratch harness; the noisy tiers were tuned there, not guessed). **Scores rank**: `ranked(_:query:key:)` filters + sorts best-first with the incoming order as tie-break, so literal hits always sit above tolerant ones and an alphabetical list stays alphabetical within a tier. Wired everywhere a user searches: `ExerciseFilterState` (exercise catalog + picker; the haystack is now name + muscle-group displayName, so "hamstring curl" finds Leg Curl), `LibraryView.candidateEquipment`, and `RoutineCatalogScreen` (name scored at full weight, the summary/style/exercise-list haystack demoted ×0.75; relevance replaces FEATURED order while searching, explicit Name/Time sorts still win). Operator's read side too: `find_items` fragments are fuzzy and ranked (the cap now keeps the LIKELIEST lines, and the tool's @Guide says typos are okay so the model passes the user's words instead of guessing spellings), and `get_stats` resolves a typo'd exercise/routine scope to ONE canonical history name first, exact-scopes the count to it, and speaks the canonical name — never a silent blend of near-matches, and an unresolvable name still honestly counts zero. **The boundary: ChangeEngine write-target resolution stays exact-or-unique-substring** (the model proposes, the app disposes; a forgiving matcher must never pick which routine gets mutated) — only its "Closest:" miss suggestions ride FuzzySearch now (ranked best-first, with the old prefix/substring/shared-word heuristics kept as fallback for partial overlaps the every-word-must-land rule rejects). Deliberately untouched: name-equality identity checks (import dedupe, library-name uniqueness, seed top-up — identity, not search) and the CLI's `stats --exercise` exact filter (documented behavior; adopting FuzzySearch there is a follow-up if wanted). 16 Kit tests pin the tier semantics; app-side filter/data-service tests cover the wiring (macOS CI). — A search box that punishes a transposed letter reads as broken, and every surface inventing its own leniency would drift; one scored rule in the Kit keeps behavior identical everywhere, keeps ranking honest (forgiving ≠ noisy), and keeps the write path strict where forgiveness would be dangerous.

**2026-07-15 — Rest split from transition: a new round of the same block rests, switching exercises gets a short transition (#369)** — Dave: rest (between sets) and transition (switching stations) are different quantities; the single `restSeconds` was serving both, and inside a superset it was actively wrong — the A→B handoff got the full rest, defeating the point of a superset. **The boundary rule** (both platforms, same logic): after a completed set, the next pending log classifies the pause — same `groupIndex` + *different* `setNumber` = a new round of the same block → REST (block `restSecondsOverride` wins, else the routine default); anything else (the superset partner within a round: same block *same* round; or another block) → TRANSITION. Phone: `WorkoutSession.pause(after:) -> (seconds, isTransition)` replaced `restSeconds(after:)`, classifying against `currentLog` so jump/redo reclassifies naturally; watch: the same rule inline in `WorkoutRunView.log` off the plan's `groupIndex`/`setNumber`. **Model**: `Routine.transitionSeconds: Int = 15` + a session snapshot (`WorkoutSession.transitionSeconds`), both constant-default additive columns (lightweight-safe; deliberately stamps existing routines 15 — the behavior change IS the feature). **`0` is legal and means no countdown at all** — the phone skips the rest screen, the watch skips the countdown + notifier. **Defaults**: transition 15 s (range 0–600, step 5); NEW routines' rest default dropped 90→45 (Dave's call — with transitions carved out, rest no longer covers station switches); existing routines keep their stored rest. **Vocabulary**: `WorkoutMetric.transition` joined next to `.rest` with a shared `isBlockConfiguration` — profiles, metric pickers, and extras all filter on it (the validator rejects both identifiers in `metrics`/extras). **Interchange**: additive `RoutineDTO.transitionSeconds: Int?`; absent = the app default (15), and the app's writer OMITS the default per the schema-evolution rule (no mass rewrite of existing repo files; an explicit 15 still round-trips as absent, which decodes identically). Sessions deliberately do NOT carry it (census: execution pacing config, inert once finished — a record's real gaps live in `completedAt`); `TemplateMerge` needed nothing (field-level by construction). **Watch plan**: additive `PlanRoutine.transitionSeconds: Int?` — a pre-transition phone's plan decodes nil and the wrist rests everywhere, exactly the old behavior. **Surfaces**: routine settings gained a BETWEEN EXERCISES / "Transition" stepper under the rest one; the live label is **SWITCH** (phone rest screen, watch, Live Activity/island via an additive `ContentState.isTransition` flag) — "Transition" names the configured quantity, SWITCH is the live-moment word; `skipRestButton`/`extendRestButton` identifiers unchanged. `Routine.estimatedSeconds` (and the catalog template mirror) now counts (rounds−1) rests per block + transitions at exercise/block boundaries — multi-exercise estimates got shorter and more honest. **Deferred**: per-block transition override; the live-mirror rest op stays kind-agnostic (a watch-initiated pause mirrors onto the phone as REST — cosmetic; the phone materialization of a watch-born session does resolve the routine by name to snapshot its transition for custody switches). **Accepted edges** (swift-reviewer): the pause kind/length freezes at log time, so resizing the pending block DURING a countdown can leave one mislabeled/mislength countdown (self-inflicted, +30s/Skip on screen); and a mid-session one-member resize of a superset makes the lopsided tail's handoffs read as rests (errs long, "round" is genuinely ambiguous once lopsided). Kit 276 / CLI 26 green on Linux; boundary-rule unit tests ride `SessionTests`; ⚠️ the live screens (SWITCH label, 0-transition skip, island label, watch label) need an on-device pass. Closes #369.

**2026-07-15 — Catalog equipment audit: Cycling requires the new Bicycle, Slider Leg Curl its Sliders, landmine work its Barbell; a targeted one-shot sync carries the corrections to existing stores** — Dave's follow-up to the config audit: "make sure all exercises require the correct equipment — cycling is counted as bodyweight." Sweep of all 257 rows against their real-world requirements found three defects. **(1) Cycling** shipped equipment-free (grouped with Running/Walking as road cardio, where "the road is not gear") — but a bike IS gear, and the empty list rendered a "Bodyweight" chip. Fix: a new **Bicycle** equipment type (Cardio group — outdoor gear an exercise genuinely requires, the Weight-Vest-for-Ruck precedent; NOT loadable) with a declared profile (`[distance, duration, speed]`, miles), which lets Cycling's explicit metrics override die — the equipment-table derivation now reproduces it byte-for-byte (pinned in tests). Running/Walking stay genuinely equipment-free. **(2) Slider Leg Curl** shipped bodyweight while Slider Lunge and Body Saw require Sliders. **(3) Landmine Row/Press** required only the Landmine — a sleeve you stick a BARBELL into (the Chain Bench Press convention: accessories list the bar they attach to). **Reaching existing stores:** the top-up seeder never updates existing rows, so `SeedData.syncRevisedEquipmentRequirementsIfNeeded` (one-shot, UserDefaults-keyed like the #186 repair, run AFTER loadIfNeeded so the Bicycle row exists) upgrades exactly the rows still at the OLD canonical requirement set — a user's customization never matches the old set, so it's never rewritten, and the one-shot key means removing the restored gear later isn't fought. Judged fine on the same sweep, not changed: bench pressing lists no rack (established convention — only squat-family movements name the Squat Rack); loaded-variant modeling (Walking Lunge/Step-Up/Russian Twist require their dumbbells/ball); improvised-anchor bodyweight work (Nordic Curl, Deficit Push-Up, Donkey Calf Raise) stays equipment-free; implied consumable load (Dip Belt/Wrist Roller/Neck Harness don't also demand a Weight Plate).

**2026-07-15 — Catalog config audit: per-exercise add-time defaults (set count, rep/duration prescriptions, HR-row eligibility) live in the definitions table; the duration floor covers every timed-work profile** — Dave's audit ask: the add-time meta-config treated every exercise as a 3×10 (or 3×45 s) strength block. Sweep found four classes of wrongness, all fixed by teaching the catalog table what it already knew elsewhere. **(1) Set count is now per-exercise** (`BuiltInExerciseDefinition.defaultSets`, resolved via `Exercise.defaultSetCount`, used by `Routine.addExerciseInNewGroup` and `SessionExerciseConfig`): static stretches and dynamic mobility drills land as ONE hold/pass (matching the Full Body Stretch routine's existing 1×30 prescription — hand-adding the same stretch used to produce a contradictory 3×45), steady cardio (Running/Walking/Cycling/Ruck + every cardio machine) lands as ONE piece (3 "sets" of rowing is an interval prescription, which stays a deliberate configuration), interval-shaped conditioning (jump rope, battle ropes, bag rounds, sled, carries) keeps its 3 rounds, and strength keeps the classic 3. `ExerciseGroup.init` lost its `sets = 3` default so no call site can silently bypass the resolution. The stretch/mobility shapes are modelled ONCE as `stretch()`/`mobility()` row builders in the table — a future stretch can't forget its 1×30-no-HR shape. **(2) Catalog rep/duration prescriptions** (`defaultReps`/`defaultDurationSeconds` columns) fix the floors where 10 reps / 45 s is never what anyone does: stretches hold 30 s (the standard prescription), a bag round is 180 s, battle ropes 30 s, an L-sit 20 s, per-side core holds 30 s (Plank/Wall Sit stay 3×45 — bilateral strength holds, not stretches); duration-only cardio consoles (Elliptical, Stair Climber, Vertical Climber, Upper Body Ergometer) get an honest 10-minute steady piece; cleans prescribe 3–5, a Turkish get-up 3, rope/peg climbs 3, Nordics 5, a wrist-roller trip 3. Precedence is #187-shaped: the user's own bumped default → catalog assignment → global floor. The WHOLE prefill is one resolution — `Exercise.addTimeTargets` — consumed by both add paths (`Routine.applyDefaultTargets`, `SessionExerciseConfig.init`), so they can never drift. Computed, not stored — catalog improvements keep reaching existing stores with zero writes, like the profile fallback (`SeedData.builtInDefinition` is dictionary-backed now, the `builtInProfilesByName` pattern). **(3) The 45 s duration floor now applies whenever duration is the profile's ONLY WORK metric, not only to bare `[duration]` profiles** — the loaded carries (`[weight, duration]`: Suitcase/Farmer's/Sandbag Carry) previously prefilled NO work target at all and silently ran the set screen's arbitrary 30 s fallback timer. Profiles with a richer work metric (a rower's distance) still take no fabricated target — the driver-hijack rule stands, and `CatalogConfigTests.tableCoherence` enforces it against future table edits (a `defaultDurationSeconds` on a profile with another work metric fails the suite); the strongman distance carries (Yoke/Farmers Handles/Husafell, `[weight, distance, duration]`) deliberately stay target-less (distance events, the athlete prescribes). **(4) Stretches and static holds drop the Target HR row** (a `supportsHeartRate` COLUMN on the definition row — deliberately not a side table of names, which would silently drift on catalog growth — resolved via `Exercise.supportsHeartRateTarget`, gated in both sheets through one shared `Exercise.showsHeartRateTargetRow`): a "zone 2 hamstring stretch" is meaningless meta-config; carries, jump rope, bag rounds, and all cardio keep the prescription, customs always keep it (the isLoadable can't-classify-intent rule), an already-set target keeps its row (the stale-prescription rule) so nothing becomes invisible-but-active, and the prefill path also respects the flag so a gated exercise never inherits a stale HR default onto fresh entries. Deliberate deferrals, recorded: customs can't carry a per-exercise set-count default (set count lives on the shared `ExerciseGroup`, so a #187-style bump from a group edit is ambiguous for supersets — a custom stretch lands 3×1 until the user adjusts); a superset keeps its HOST group's set count when members join (pre-existing semantics, visible in the sheet). Flagged, not changed: "Calf Raise" duplicates "Standing Calf Raise" (removal would strand existing stores — the top-up seeder only adds); "Slider Leg Curl" requires no equipment while "Slider Lunge" requires Sliders; Dead Bug/Bird Dog stay timed (a defensible prescription style). Pinned by `CatalogConfigTests`.

**2026-07-15 — Creating from a narrowed list carries the narrowing in: the search query prefills the new thing's name, active filters prefill its attributes** — Every create action reachable from a searched/filtered surface now starts from what was being looked for, instead of a blank form (Dave: the empty state's create should be smarter). Three surfaces: the **exercise catalog** (`CatalogBrowseScreen`) already prefilled the name from the query ("Create “query”", #63) and now also passes the MUSCLE/EQUIPMENT filters; the **exercise picker**'s "New Exercise" button (previously a fully blank editor) passes the search text and both filters; the **routine catalog**'s "New blank routine" prompt prefills its name field from the search, and the row's label telegraphs it the same way the exercise catalog does ("Create “query”"). Mechanism: `ExerciseFilterState` grew two pure prefill helpers — `prefillName` (trimmed query) and `prefillMuscleGroup`, which carries over **only when exactly one muscle group is filtered** (an exercise has exactly one; a multi-select is ambiguous, so the editor keeps its own default rather than guessing). The equipment filter passes through whole via `prefillEquipment`: all selected gear lands as the draft's REQUIRES set — a multi-select equipment filter means "any of these" while REQUIRES means "all of these", but the prefill is visible, chip-removable state in the editor, so showing everything selected beats silently dropping it. Two swift-reviewer catches shaped it: the helper prunes `isDeleted` stragglers (the filter state outlives picker presentations, and the prefill is the first path that WRITES the selection into a relationship — the lingering-deleted-model hazard from bug hunt B1), and the suggested-profile merge takes the gear **name-sorted**, not `Array(Set)` (the merge is order-sensitive — the first distance-carrying profile wins the unit — so an unstable order flipped the suggestion run to run; the pre-existing `.onChange` site had the same latent flaw and got the same sort). `ExerciseEditorView`'s two narrow prefill inits (`prefillName:`, `prefillEquipment:`) fused into one `init(prefillName:prefillMuscleGroup:prefillEquipment:)` with defaults; gear still brings its suggested metric profile via `adoptSuggestedProfile` (the #137 semantics, unchanged), and `init(editing:)` dropped its `= nil` default so the two all-default inits can't collide on a bare call. Routine-catalog FOCUS/EFFORT/TIME/GEAR filters prefill nothing — they're template attributes a blank `Routine` doesn't have. — A prefill is a free head start where the intent is unambiguous (the searched name IS the missing thing) and cheap to correct where it isn't; the only-when-single muscle rule keeps the smart default from becoming a wrong default.

**2026-07-15 — Durations and rest pick on a horizontal tape scrubber (the iOS 27 timer idiom); the tiered wheel stays for every other metric** — Dave's ask: durations couldn't be precisely configured — the stepper moves ±15 s and the duration wheel only carries its own 5/15/60 s tiers, so an arbitrary target like 1:37 was UNREACHABLE in the UI even though the interchange stores `durationSeconds` as a plain positive `Int` (a hand-edited repo can say `97` today, and the wheel's `nearestWheelValue` binding would SNAP that to 95 on the first scroll — the hackable-contract promise broken by the UI). Two alternatives were weighed and rejected: **typing** (the repo already tried and deliberately killed `.number` TextFields — "keyboard-free by design" — and "130" is ambiguous between 1:30 and 130 s) and a **two-tier `--`/`-`/`+`/`++` stepper** (on-brand pun, but ~11 taps to cross 30→97 s, a custom four-target control replacing a native `Stepper`, and it overloads the `++` mark, which means create/data-green, as an increment-size label). Dave instead sent the iOS 27 beta timer picker — a horizontal tick tape you drag precisely or flick with inertia — and asked for a PlusPlus-native version, used anywhere a duration is picked. **Shape:** the numeric semantics are a pure Kit type, `DurationTape` (seconds↔points linear mapping at 3 pt/s, clamping, the visible-window tick query — 5 s marks, labels at 30 s/whole minutes — and the "45s"/m:ss label format; Linux-tested, same split as `WorkoutMetric.wheelValues`), plus `WorkoutMetric.isTimeSpan` (duration + rest; pace is m:ss but a RATE, so it keeps the wheel). The view (`Views/Components/DurationScrubber.swift`) gets its physics from a REAL ScrollView — UIKit deceleration and rubber-banding, never hand-rolled — over an invisible strip one viewport wider than the tape so every value can rest at the center caret; a custom `ScrollTargetBehavior` snaps the landing on a whole second; the ruler is a viewport-sized `Canvas` fed by `onScrollGeometryChange` (a 60-minute tape as real content would be a ~11,000 pt raster). Three contract details worth keeping (the last two hardened by the pre-push review round — swift-reviewer + the 8-angle /code-review both converged on the same class): the Canvas reads an `offsetX` state SEEDED in init so the first frame already draws the incoming value (no lower-bound flash before the programmatic scroll); the pane seeds its seconds CLAMPED so an out-of-range stored value (a hand-edited repo can legally hold a 90-minute duration — the validator only rejects non-positives) displays clamped but is never rewritten by merely opening the picker; and all picks/commits are gated on `userTouched`, which only an `.interacting` scroll phase (actual movement — deliberately NOT `.tracking`, so a finger resting on the ruler and lifting commits nothing) or a VoiceOver adjust can set — programmatic positioning structurally cannot write, whatever callback ordering SwiftUI picks. Writes are ONE PER GESTURE, not per frame: `seconds` (readout, tick fill, haptics) updates live locally, but the model binding commits on scroll-settle (`onScrollPhaseChange` → `.idle`) plus an idempotent `onDisappear` (the commit-in-onDisappear law — Done mid-coast or swipe-down mid-flick must not lose the landed value). The wheel committed per settled row, so per-frame writes would have been a NEW cost — each duration write fans out through `setTarget` → `bumpExerciseDefaults` (a JSON encode of the extras map) and each block-rest write through the override un-pinning check, which a mid-flick pass through the routine default would have transiently un-pinned. Grammar: ticks up to the picked value light in `Theme.accent` — the value's magnitude is data, same job as live progress — the rest sit in border ink; the big readout rolls `.numericText`; `.sensoryFeedback(.selection)` per second; VoiceOver gets an adjustable action at ±1 s. **Reach:** `MetricWheelSheet` (moved from ExerciseDetailSheet.swift to `Views/Components/`, where a four-screen shared control belongs) branches on `isTimeSpan`, so all four presenting surfaces — routine-detail block sheet (duration target + block rest), exercise-config, exercise-editor defaults, and active-session duration logging — got the scrubber with zero call-site changes; the routine-settings Rest row additionally gained the `onTapValue` it never had (stepper-only until now); the rebase onto main also routed #373's new `.transition` metric onto the tape (it's a time span, so `isTimeSpan` covers it and the routine-settings Transition row gained tap-to-pick too). **Discoverability follow-up (Dave, 2026-07-16, before merge):** the tap-editable value in EVERY `MetricStepperRow` now renders as an outlined text-input (same 36 pt height + radius as the ± control beside it) instead of bare mono text — Dave, testing on device, didn't know the value was tappable at all (and so had never known the OLD wheel was there either), so the picker, and the whole tape behind it, went unfound; a non-tappable value (Sets, nudged only by ±) stays a plain readout. The value was always a `Button`; only its chrome changed, so the smoke test's `weightValue` assertions are unaffected. The 15 s steppers stay untouched — `incremented` ADDS rather than snaps, so they preserve a precise value once set (97→112), and coarse-nudge vs precise-pick is the same fine/coarse split the row grammar already had. Dead code pruned: `MetricRow`/`RepTargetRow`/`intMetricBinding` (the v1 inline rows superseded by `MetricStepperRow` + the sheets) deleted from MetricInput.swift rather than left lying about the duration UX with their embedded copy of the old wheel. `WorkoutMetric`'s duration wheel tiers remain in Kit (public API; other metrics still use the wheel path). ⚠️ **App-target gesture work — the scroll feel, per-second snap, flick inertia, and haptics are not exercisable remotely (and XCUITest can't see gesture-layer behavior anyway); needs an on-device pass** (drag precision to an exact odd second, flick across minutes, rubber-band at both ends, VoiceOver adjust, and the routine-settings rest tap). No smoke test touched the duration/rest wheels, so no UI-test changes. — The tape gives every whole second two spins away without a keyboard, keeps the app's pick-don't-type law, and fixes the UI-destroys-hand-edited-values snap; the wheel survives where its tiers are the right granularity.

**2026-07-15 — First-open reworked: a cold open always opens on the `++` mark, the splash and welcome share one moving glyph, and the Start button gained an icon + an ignition tap beat** — Follow-up tweaks to the one-screen welcome (same day, on Dave's screenshot feedback). Four connected changes, all in the fused `IntroView` (renamed from `WelcomeView`, still `PlusPlus/Views/WelcomeView.swift`) and `RootTabView`. **(1) A cold open ALWAYS opens on the mark.** Previously a first launch skipped the splash and jumped straight to the welcome content; the splash (centered `++`) only showed for returning users. Now `RootTabView` shows `IntroView` on every cold open — `introShowsWelcome` (= `!welcomeSeen`) decides whether the mark then settles into the welcome content (first launch) or just holds a beat and dissolves to Today (returning). Under `--uitest-reset` the pure-splash returning-user case is skipped (`showingIntro = welcome || !uitest`) so the smoke suite still lands on the tabs immediately; the `--uitest-welcome` test forces `welcomeSeen` false and gets its screen. **(2) The splash `++` and the welcome `++` are ONE element, moved and scaled** (Dave: "same thing, just moved and scaled… matchedGeometryEffect or something of that ilk"). A single `Text("++")` follows a `matchedGeometryEffect(id:in:properties:.position)` slot; an invisible twin inside the welcome layout reserves the destination (so there is no layout shift and the name/tagline sit consistently whether or not the mark has arrived), and a 2×2 `Color.clear` marks the splash slot at screen center. Exactly one of the two is `isSource` at a time (keyed on `atWelcome`), the real glyph is never a source. **Font can't animate**, so the size change (72→64 pt) rides `scaleEffect(welcomeScale)` while position is matched — the glyph glides up and shrinks together on a spring. **(3) The "Start building" key gained a `chevron.right`** (chosen via the Axiom `sf-symbols` skill — a plain right chevron per Dave) and was repositioned for a concentric feel: equal side/bottom insets (`edgeInset = 22`) and a larger corner radius (`keyRadius = 24`) so its corners echo the display's curve and its bottom edge sits up near where the screen starts to round, not pinned to the very bottom. **(4) Tapping it plays an "ignition" beat** (Dave: "hell yeah let's do it!" — a bare symbol bounce wasn't enough): a medium impact on tap, the cap wipes green left-to-right (the app's commit-landed grammar, `Theme.accent` scaled in from the leading edge under a rounded clip), the label morphs "Start building" → "let's go" (`contentTransition(.opacity)`), the chevron accelerates off the trailing edge, a `.success` haptic fires as the wipe lands, then the whole intro scales up + fades ("dives") into Today. The deferred fire is a stored `launchTask` cancelled on disappear, re-entrancy-guarded (`guard !launching`), and under `instant` (UI test) the whole flourish is skipped — tap just marks `welcomeSeen` and finishes so `testWelcomeFlow` still taps `welcomeStartButton` and finds the Today tab hittable with no real-seconds wait. ⚠️ **App-target only — the motion (the glyph glide/scale, the green wipe, the chevron takeoff, the dive-to-Today) is not exercisable on the CI runner and needs an on-device pass**; the identifier (`welcomeStartButton`) and the "PlusPlus" text the smoke test asserts are unchanged. — A cold open that opens on the brand mark reads as the app booting rather than dumping you onto a form; one glyph that moves beats two that pop; and the first tap is the app's first real commit, so it earns a celebratory beat in the grammar the rest of the app already speaks (green = creation, `.success` = a commit landed, zoom = navigation).

**2026-07-15 — Onboarding trimmed to one welcome screen; the Apple Health ask moved to a contextual first-workout primer that also captures per-workout calories** — Worked through the first-launch messaging with Dave and made two connected changes. **(1) `WelcomeView` collapsed from three screens to one.** The old flow was idea → mechanics tour → Health ask. The mechanics slide was pure telling — Today's setup timeline already teaches by doing — so it's gone; the screen is now just the `++` mark, name, tagline, one supporting line, and a single button that drops into Today. The multi-page machinery (TabView, page dots, "skip intro", the per-page `controlsHeight` reservation, the health-page Connect/skip) is deleted. **Copy settled (Dave, after a long riff):** NO second line — the tagline carries the positioning on its own — and the CTA is **"Start building"** (`welcomeStartButton`), which reads as entering the app and picks up the build/version-of-you thread the app leans on (the `++`/commit vocabulary). **(2) The Health ask is now a one-time primer in front of the first workout** (`HealthStartPrimer.swift`, new, in `Views/Components/`), where heart rate is actually about to matter — the standard pre-permission primer pattern (Apple WWDC 2020-10664; validated against the Axiom `axiom-health` auth skill). Its four load-bearing rules: **(a)** the "already asked?" memory is OURS (`SetupState.healthPrimerShown`) because HealthKit hides read authorization by design and we can't derive it; **(b)** both buttons proceed into the workout (a "Not now" is not a dead end — the user tapped Start to train), interactive dismissal disabled so a swipe can't eat the start; **(c)** the actual start runs in the sheet's `onDismiss`, never under the live sheet (the repo's documented dismiss-then-present-cover drop class); **(d)** Connect resolves the system sheet FIRST, then starts, so the first workout already has live HR. Every start site funnels through `HealthStartGate.begin(_:orPresent:)` — `TodayView.start`/`startEmptySession` (covers the due card, swap-in, and the Siri/widget/calendar `.plusplusStartRoutine` path), `RoutineDetailView` bottom bar, and `HistoryView` "Do it again" — so the primer covers every path once and no path double-primes.
