Under `--uitest-reset` `HealthAccess.isAvailable` is false, so the gate begins immediately: no smoke-test workout-start flow blocks on a primer. **"Not now" routes through `HealthSyncCoordinator.shared.disable()`** (the documented, Settings-reversible off switch), not a soft skip — otherwise the live `HeartRateMonitor` (which only gates on the default-ON `HealthSyncSettings.isEnabled`) would independently surface the system read sheet moments later, making "Not now" a lie. ⚠️ This is a genuine product call to confirm on device: "Not now" turns Health OFF until re-enabled in Settings' Health row, rather than letting iOS re-ask at a later workout. **Existing installs are not re-primed:** `SetupState.backfillHealthPrimerForExistingInstalls(hasWorkoutHistory:)` (called from `PlusPlusApp.init`, non-inMemory) seeds `healthPrimerShown = true` only when the store already holds a `WorkoutSession`. Keyed on prior USE, not `welcomeSeen` — `welcomeSeen` is set at "Get started" (before a fresh user's first workout) and the backfill runs every launch, so gating on it would mark the primer shown for a brand-new user who merely relaunched between onboarding and training, and the primer would never appear (swift-reviewer HIGH catch). A genuinely fresh install has zero sessions → no-ops → meets the primer at its first workout; an existing install that trained on a pre-primer build has history → not re-primed. **(3) Per-workout active energy is requested and shown** (Dave's call): `HealthAccess.readTypes` gained `activeEnergyBurned`, and the session record (`HistoryView`) shows a "N cal" line beside the HR summary, read LIVE from Health on record open (`HealthAccess.activeEnergy(from:to:)`, HKStatisticsQuery cumulativeSum) — deliberately NOT persisted, so it needs no SwiftData migration, no interchange DTO, no PLATFORM.md/completeness-test change. Trade-off: unlike stored HR, it's absent from export and won't show offline-from-Health. Full HR-parity (stored + exported) is a follow-up if Dave wants it. Absent/denied/no-Watch reads as no line, never "0 cal" (the HealthRecorder bonus-never-a-gate contract). **Health-data prioritization (the wider question Dave raised):** we deliberately request ONLY what a surface uses — heart rate + active energy + DOB — not a batch. HealthKit's ask is incremental (a later type shows only its own toggle, already-decided types never reappear), so deferring costs nothing, and a privacy-first app must not show toggles that light up nothing. The Tier-2 fitness-trend reads (resting HR, HR recovery, VO2 max, bodyweight) are captured on **#295** to ride their own trends surface with a single batched contextual ask when it ships; sport-specific power/cadence and all nutrition/vitals/mobility types are explicitly out. ⚠️ **App-target only; every HealthKit path is inert under UI test and absent on the CI runner — needs on-device validation:** the single welcome screen lands in the tabs; the first workout (from Today, routine detail, and "Do it again") shows the primer once; Connect grants and the first workout has live HR; "Not now" starts the workout with Health off and does NOT then pop the system sheet; the record shows a calorie line when a Watch was worn; an existing install updated over the top is NOT re-primed. Smoke test `testWelcomeFlow` updated for the single screen (old `welcomeContinueButton`/mechanics/health identifiers retired → `welcomeGetStartedButton`). — A mechanics slide teaches worse than the timeline does by doing, and asking for Health up front (with nowhere to use most of it) is the exact privacy-violation-feeling batch a privacy-first app must avoid; asking exactly what a surface uses, at the moment it matters, is both better UX and on-brand.

**2026-07-14 — Tray-flicker + #155 SHIPPED (build 77, #358 + #359 MERGED); a `NavigationLink(value:)` dead-tap was the last bug** — Closing the loop on the two entries below. The pre-merge TestFlight strategy earned its keep: three on-device rounds, each catching a bug CI could not. **Build 75** surfaced the shared-uuid property-default footgun (below). **Build 76** surfaced a NAV regression the uuid decoupling introduced: `TodayView` still had three `NavigationLink(value: routine)` / `NavigationLink(value: entry.routine)` sites (today card, upcoming card, carried-over card) pushing the raw `Routine` @Model after the destination was swapped to `RoutineRef.self` — so tapping a Today card to open/configure a workout did NOTHING. ⚠️ **Pushing a value with no registered `.navigationDestination(for:)` is a SILENT runtime no-op, not a compile error**, and `ui-test` is skipped on branch builds, so CI stayed green and only an on-device tap found it. Fixed to `routine.uuid.map { RoutineRef(uuid: $0) }` at all three; a whole-app sweep (manual + Axiom `swiftui-nav-auditor`) confirmed no other unregistered-push sites. `ui-interaction.md` now spells out that the uuid-keying law covers `NavigationLink(value:)`, not just `path.append`, and that the failure is silent (device pass mandatory after any routine-nav change). **Build 77** validated clean on-device (routines open their own detail, no duplicate rail rows, no tray flicker, Today cards navigate, all data intact, no reset alert). **Merge shape:** #358 (migration infra) then #359 (uuid + decoupling + the dead-tap fix) squashed to main in order, ship-together honored — #359 was rebased onto the post-#358 main (dropping the now-squashed #358 commits) to clear the expected stacked-squash conflict. Closes #155. — The pre-merge device gate is non-negotiable for this class: a data-diff and a green CI both passed while the app was, in turn, opening the wrong routine and then refusing to open any.

**2026-07-14 — The "proper" tray-flicker fix: a device-local `uuid` on the routine models, and all presentation/navigation keyed on it instead of `persistentModelID`** — The #357 door-saves fixed the flicker defensively (save a fresh model so its `persistentModelID` is permanent before it backs a presentation). This is the structural fix Dave asked for on top: `Routine`/`ExerciseGroup`/`RoutineExercise` gain a stable `uuid` and the UI keys on THAT, so the temporary→permanent id swap can never re-key an open sheet/push again (the door-saves become belt-and-suspenders). Mirrors `EquipmentLibrary.uuid` and `WorkoutSession.sessionId`; device-local, EXCLUDED from the interchange (census updated) — the repo's shared identity stays name-based (#31 territory). **Migration mechanism — lightweight + a UNIQUENESS-ENFORCING launch backfill, NOT a custom stage.** `uuid` is OPTIONAL (`UUID?`) and minted per instance in `init` — deliberately NOT via a property-level `= UUID()` default. Two migration footguns forced this, both caught by validation not by a data-diff: (1) a NON-optional UUID has no static default, so the column-add fails validation on existing rows (CI: `NSCocoaErrorDomain 1560`); (2) a `= UUID()` PROPERTY default is applied by lightweight migration as ONE SHARED CONSTANT to every existing row — the pre-merge TestFlight (build 75) showed every routine opening the same one and the rail drawing duplicate rows, because all rows shared a uuid (`ForEach(id: \.uuid)` collapsed them). Fix: defaultless optional (migrated rows → nil), `init` sets new instances, and `SeedData.backfillModelUUIDsIfNeeded` (PlusPlusApp.init) reassigns any row whose uuid is nil OR a duplicate — repairing both a clean migration and a store already stamped with the shared default. Note the export was byte-identical build-74↔75 (uuid is device-local, excluded), so the interchange diff proved data preserved but NOT identity correct — only opening the app did. ⚠️ **A frozen-V1-snapshot + custom `didMigrate` stage was tried first and ABANDONED**: nested snapshot `@Model` classes that share an entity name with the live top-level classes crash SwiftData migration with a fatal `Failed to cast model AppSchemaV1.RoutineExercise to RoutineExercise` (CI caught it; it would hit production upgrades too). The lesson for the next schema change: prefer lightweight + a launch backfill for additive fields; only reach for snapshot `VersionedSchema` classes when a change genuinely can't ride lightweight, and know the same-entity-name coexistence is a live hazard. **Decoupling scope.** Keyed on `uuid` via small route/ref value types (`ModelRefs.swift`: `RoutineRef{uuid}`, `IdentifiedUUID{id}`, `ModelContext.routine(uuid:)` resolver that FETCHES by uuid so a just-created routine resolves with no `@Query` lag): the per-exercise detail sheet + superset picker (`RoutineDetailView`), and ALL `Routine` value-navigation (`path.append(RoutineRef(...))` + `.navigationDestination(for: RoutineRef.self)` resolving by uuid) across `TodayView`/`RoutineListView`/`RoutineCatalogScreen`/`CatalogDetailViews` (incl. `PushTarget.routine(UUID)`, `createdRoutine`, `scheduleEditTarget`), plus the rail `ForEach` ids and `SupersetLanding.groupID`. `SwipeRevealRow` was made generic over `ID: Hashable`. **Deliberately LEFT on `persistentModelID`** (internal animation/list identity, not tray/screen presentation, already flicker-free via the door-saves; converting adds risk for no flicker benefit): the pending→workout zoom-transition pairing, Missed/Upcoming entry ids, the `SwapInSheet` `dueIDs` set, and swipe-open state (keeping it off `uuid` also avoids a double-optional). ⚠️ **On-device gate:** the migration lightweight-add + backfill, and the nav/zoom feel, are not exercisable remotely — needs the install-over-existing-data upgrade pass + a nav walkthrough. Kit/CLI unaffected. **Ship-together constraint** (swift-reviewer): #358 defines `AppSchemaV1 (1,0,0)` WITHOUT uuid; this change adds uuid but keeps `(1,0,0)`. Since neither has shipped, wild stores are UNVERSIONED (build 74's plain `Schema`), so the first versioned build just needs to be the WITH-uuid shape — but do NOT dispatch a TestFlight build off a #358-only main (a store stamped `1,0,0`-no-uuid would then collide with `1,0,0`-with-uuid). Merge both, then build. The upgrade opening via the primary or plan-less-fallback path (never `StoreRecovery` reset, never `SetupState.storeWasReset`) is the specific thing to confirm on device. — A presentation keyed on an id that mutates out from under it is the root bug; a stable device-local id the UI keys on removes the hazard by construction, and the migration to add it must be lightweight-safe because a validation failure on upgrade is data loss.

**2026-07-14 — Store migration policy for 1.0 (#155): a versioned schema + migration plan, and recovery that copies the store aside instead of silently wiping it** — Since build 16 (#153) an unopenable store was DESTROYED and recreated — fine while data was explicitly throwaway, but the moment sync (#23) or real usage ships it silently drops someone's training history, and the #144 entity renames are exactly the kind of change that bricked stores. This replaces the stopgap with the 1.0 policy, in two parts. **(1) A real migration plan.** New `PlusPlus/Models/AppSchema.swift`: `AppSchemaV1: VersionedSchema` (versionIdentifier 1.0.0, listing all 8 `@Model` types — it *is* today's shape, so it references the live classes with no snapshot duplication yet), `AppMigrationPlan: SchemaMigrationPlan` (schemas `[V1]`, no stages yet), and `AppSchema.latest = Schema(versionedSchema: AppSchemaV1.self)`. `PlusPlusApp.init` now opens `ModelContainer(for: AppSchema.latest, migrationPlan: AppMigrationPlan.self, …)`. Opening WITH the plan is what lets the *next* shape change migrate rather than reset the store; **when a later version changes a model, V1 gets frozen into standalone snapshot classes** (the live classes become the newer version's `models`) so each `VersionedSchema` stays a complete snapshot, not a diff (the Apple/Axiom rule). Adopting VersionedSchema V1 == the current entities is expected to map existing *unversioned* stores cleanly (CoreData matches on entity-property hashes, not the Schema.Version); a unit test (`StoreMigrationTests`) writes a store with the old plain `Schema([...])` and reopens it under V1 + plan asserting zero loss + intact relationships, which is the strongest signal a headless test can give. **(2) Recovery is copy-aside, never a silent wipe** (`PlusPlus/Models/StoreRecovery.swift`): when the container still can't open (genuine corruption, or a store the plan can't map), the raw `.sqlite`/`-shm`/`-wal` are COPIED to `Documents/RecoveredStore-<epoch>/` (Files-visible via new `UIFileSharingEnabled`/`LSSupportsOpeningDocumentsInPlace` Info.plist keys) BEFORE anything is deleted — a copy can't fail on a corrupt store and loses zero bytes — then the store is recreated and a breadcrumb (`SetupState.storeWasReset`) is set. `RootTabView` reads it once at launch and shows a calm, anti-shame alert ("PlusPlus couldn't open your saved data, so it started fresh. A copy … was saved to the Files app …"), clearing the flag on dismiss. **Deferred deliberately:** a friendlier interchange-JSON export + in-app auto-reimport — it needs a readable `ModelContext` the failure path often doesn't have (if SwiftData can't open the store, neither can `exportBundle`), it's lossy (interchange is name-keyed and excludes device fields), and it overlaps with simply fixing the migration plan; **GitHub sync is the real long-term "never lose a rep" restore** (data already lives in the user's repo). ⚠️ **Migration correctness is on-device-or-nothing** — Apple/Axiom guidance is emphatic that simulator success ≠ production safety, and this was authored in a remote Linux session with neither; the mandatory pre-ship test is install-current-build → create data → install-this-build-over-it → verify all data intact. Closes #155 (the JSON-salvage nicety can be a follow-up). — Destroy-and-recreate is losing someone's history; a versioned plan prevents the failure for ordinary changes, and copy-aside guarantees that even a genuine corruption is recoverable rather than silently erased.

**2026-07-14 — Trays/pushes stop flickering: save freshly-created models synchronously so their `persistentModelID` can't swap under an open sheet or nav push (app-wide sweep)** — Reported bug: in a routine, trays "sometimes briefly hide and reappear for no apparent reason" — the exercise-detail tray especially. Root cause is the repo's known item-keyed-presentation class (the `WorkoutSession.start` / `fullScreenCover(item:)` bug, 2026-07-07), reached by several new doors. When a model is `context.insert`ed but not saved, it holds a TEMPORARY `persistentModelID` until SwiftData's next (debounced) autosave, at which point the id swaps temporary→permanent. ANY presentation keyed on that id — `.sheet(item:)`/`.fullScreenCover(item:)` directly, an item enum whose `id` IS a model's `persistentModelID`, `.navigationDestination(item:)`, or even a value-based `path.append(model)` (a `@Model`'s `Hashable` derives from `persistentModelID`) — re-keys when the autosave fires WHILE it's open, so SwiftUI reads a NEW item and dismisses + re-presents (or re-resolves the pushed screen). The background-autosave trigger is exactly why it looks "for no apparent reason". **The specific door reported** (`RoutineDetailView`): the per-exercise detail sheet `.sheet(item: $selectedExercise)` (a `RoutineExercise`) and the superset picker whose `pickerDestination.group` id IS `group.persistentModelID`; the interactive `addExercise`/`duplicateExercise` paths inserted the new group/exercise without saving, so a just-added row was tappable while still on a temp id. **Sweep found four more** create-then-navigate sites with the same gap, all fixed the same way: `CatalogDetailViews.createRoutine` (→ `.navigationDestination(item: $createdRoutine)`), `TodayView.createRoutine`, `RoutineCatalogScreen.createBlankRoutine`, and `RoutineCatalogScreen`'s template-Add (→ `RoutineCatalog.instantiate` → `path.append`). **Fix**: `try? modelContext.save()` at the six interactive call sites, giving the new model a permanent id before it can back a presentation/push — the same rule as `WorkoutSession.start`. Deliberately NOT saving inside the shared structure-mutation/instantiate methods (`Routine.addExercise*`, `RoutineCatalog.instantiate`): those also run in import (`InterchangeMapping`) and dev/seed loops, where a per-call save would be many redundant writes; the fix belongs at the interactive door, not the shared plumbing. **Audited safe, no change** (their item id is a value/string, or they already save, or they key on a stable field): all `$wheel` sheets (`WorkoutMetric` value type), every `activeSession` cover (`WorkoutSession.start`/`startEmpty` already save synchronously), `EquipmentLibrary` create (the active pointer keys on `library.uuid`, deliberately not `persistentModelID`, per 2026-07-11), `RevealSurface` `activeTray`/`activePush` (String-enum ids), `SessionOverviewSheet` (String block key), `GitHubSyncTray` browser (URL string), `RootTabView` shareImport (deep-link value), the picker's `editingExercise`/`pendingConfig` (existing model / value type), and every cross-ref `path = .routine/.exercise` navigation (existing models from a `@Query`). Generalized the swiftdata.md rule from "`fullScreenCover(item:)`" to any item-keyed presentation (incl. `.sheet(item:)` and item enums whose `id` is a model's `persistentModelID`), plus the value-based `path.append(model)` case, with the save-at-the-interactive-call-site caveat. ⚠️ App-target-only; the flicker is an autosave-timing race not exercisable in a remote session — **needs on-device validation** (add an exercise to a routine and immediately open its detail tray + superset picker; create a routine from Today, the Routines catalog, and an exercise/template detail — confirm no dismiss/re-present or pushed-screen re-resolve in any). — A presentation keyed on an id that mutates out from under it is the bug; every freshly-created model just needed to be permanent before it became tappable/navigable.

**2026-07-14 — Follow-up polish on the carried-over work (swift-reviewer's low/latent findings)** — Three small refinements after #354's scheduling split, all behavior-preserving-ish and none blocking. (1) **`dueSince` honors "today wins".** A weekday `.due` is only ever returned when today is itself an outstanding occurrence, so `dueSince` for that case now returns `todayStart` directly instead of walking back to an older same-week lapse (which would read "due since mon" on a routine that's due *today*). Latent — `dueSince` has no production callers yet — but it's now internally consistent with the split, with a test locking it. (2) **Today's rest-day item yields to carried-over work.** `restDayItem` now also gates on `missedEntries.isEmpty`: when a CARRIED OVER lane is showing, the "rest day · start whenever" line above it read as a blind claim, so it's suppressed (the lane is the actionable surface). The finish screen's `nextOccurrenceLine` is DELIBERATELY left blind to `.missed` (documented in a comment): a completion moment shouldn't nag about a carry — that surfaces calmly on Today, per the anti-shame grammar. (3) **Missed lane stops re-deriving its due-state.** `missedRoutines: [Routine]` + a per-card `missedSince(_:)` (each re-running `dueState`/`recentCompletions`, O(sessions)) collapsed into a single `missedEntries: [MissedEntry]` that bundles the lapsed day, computed once per render. — All three are swift-reviewer findings Dave asked to clear; the first two are correctness/consistency, the third is a small render cost the missed lane had added.

**2026-07-14 — Scheduling split into due-today vs carried-miss, anchored to when a routine joined the library; Today gained a gentle "carried over" lane** — Dave hit a real confusion: a Tuesday-scheduled routine ("Nora's sample workout", just imported) showed as a green DUE card under Monday's `TODAY` marker. Two root causes, both fixed. **(1) No library-join anchor.** The Kit's weekday `dueState` walked back up to 6 days for an unmet occurrence and, finding last Tuesday unmet, called the routine due — even though it was NEVER in the library last Tuesday. `RoutineSchedule.dueState`/`dueSince`/`upcomingScheduledDays` gained an `addedOn: Date? = nil` anchor (threaded through the private walks + the `occurrenceSatisfiedEarly` recursion); scheduled days strictly before `startOfDay(addedOn)` are never counted as missed. The app passes `Routine.createdAt`, which — because a catalog routine is instantiated as a fresh `Routine` at the moment it's added to the library (`RoutineCatalog.instantiate`) — already IS the "added to your routines" moment, custom or catalog. No new field, no SwiftData migration; kept the name `createdAt` (a rename would be a risky migration for a cosmetic gain, and #155's store-migration policy is still unshipped). `createdAt` stays OUT of the interchange (device metadata, per the existing mapping note), so a library restored on a new phone anchors at restore time — no phantom pre-restore misses, which is the anti-shame-correct behavior. **(2) `.due` conflated "today" with "carried".** `DueState` split: `.due` now means TODAY is a scheduled unmet occurrence (green, one-click Start, today always wins over an older miss this week); new `.missed(since: Date)` means a PAST scheduled day (1–6 days ago, on/after `addedOn`) lapsed and today isn't itself scheduled. Rolling frequency never yields `.missed` (it floats — only `.due`/`.notDue`). Widgets/intents gate on `== .due`, so a carried miss silently stops counting as "due today" there (correct) with no exhaustive-switch breakage. **App/Today:** a new **CARRIED OVER** lane sits between today's cards and the committed history — amber (`Theme.notes`, the advisory hue already in the grammar), never green; each `missedCard` is tap-to-open (no inline Start), captioned "was tue · jul 7 · ~30 min". This also removes the missed workout from the `TODAY` date entirely (Dave: "stop showing them in today's date"). **Two more Today changes same round:** the **future/upcoming cards lost their inline Start** — one-click Start is now reserved for today's card (a future day is a calendar fact, not a call to act; upcoming cards navigate to detail where Start lives); and **committed cards gained a purple check seal** on the card itself (`checkmark.circle.fill`, `Theme.done`) so a finished workout reads as done at a glance without leaning on its rail node. Kit 269 green on Linux (added anchor + due/missed-split coverage; two carried-over tests flipped from `.due` to `.missed`). ⚠️ App-target UI (the amber lane, the killed future Start, the check seal) is not exercisable remotely — **needs on-device validation**. — `.due` meaning both "do this today" and "you didn't do this last week" is the bug; a routine can't be overdue for a day it wasn't around for, and the carried state deserves a calm lane of its own rather than masquerading as today's green work.

**2026-07-14 — GitHub sync commits at edit boundaries with semantic messages; Today pull-to-refresh syncs (or quips); connected tray gains "Sync now" and a plain status** — Four connected changes to how and when data moves to GitHub, all Dave's calls (auto-commit at boundaries / no pre-workout pull / semantic messages / plain status + a Sync-now button). (1) **Boundary commits.** Sync was foreground-only (plus on-connect, earlier this session). A new debounced, dirty-gated `GitHubSyncCoordinator.requestSync(context:units:)` now fires when an editing surface closes, so a batch of edits lands promptly instead of waiting for the next foreground. Debounced (1.5s, cancels the prior `pendingSyncTask`) so a burst of toggles coalesces into ONE commit; dirty-gated (a network-free diff of the exported local file map vs the saved base snapshot) so merely opening a routine and backing out costs nothing — pulling remote changes stays on the always-runs `sync()` (foreground, pull-to-refresh, Sync now), so the gate only asks "is there anything to push." Wired through a self-contained `.syncsProgramOnClose()` `ViewModifier` (it brings its own `modelContext` + weight unit, so it attaches anywhere): routine detail, the routine list (create/delete/reorder), both library tabs, the catalog browse screen, plus a `requestSync` in `ExerciseEditorView.save()`. Because `sync()` is bidirectional, "commit more often" and "check remote more often" (Dave's item 4) are the SAME trigger; deliberately NO pre-workout blocking pull (keeps Start instant — foreground already covers "opened the app to train"). Known gap: the routine-catalog GEAR-facet toggles aren't boundary-wired yet (caught on next foreground); the tab-level hooks + catalog browse cover the main equipment paths. swift-reviewer follow-up (all LOW): the dirty-gate's byte comparison assumes `export(import(x)) == x` for the app-side `InterchangeMapping` model round-trip — proven stable in practice (the existing foreground sync's no-op detection relies on the same property and doesn't spuriously push), but the SwiftData-model round-trip has no idempotency test yet (app-side, not Linux-exercisable); worst case is ONE self-healing spurious commit per pulled-then-re-exported file, so a model-round-trip test is a nice-to-have, not a blocker. (2) **Semantic commit messages.** `SyncEngine.commitMessage(pushing:)` now derives the subject from WHAT changed via the interchange path prefixes ("Update equipment: barbell", "Update 2 routines", "Log workout", "Sync N changes" when a pass spans areas) instead of "Sync: file-a, file-b (+n more)". Pure, path-only, unit-tested; no intent hint threaded from call sites. (3) **Today pull-to-refresh** was a placebo (it only bumped a day token; its own comment said sync would join "when #23 ships"). It now runs a real GitHub sync, but ONLY awaits — holding the spinner — when connected; disconnected there is nothing to fetch, so it skips the network entirely and rewards the gesture with a random on-brand quip (the Slack move) via a new `RefreshQuip` pool and a reusable `.toast()` component. Connected, a confirmation toast shows the friendly outcome. HealthKit is not meaningfully "refreshable" (write-on-finish + read-live), so it stays out. (4) **Connected tray.** The status line was git-jargon ("Pushed 3 · pulled 1. 2 minutes ago"); it is now a plain "Synced <relative>" (Foundation's `.relative` style pluralizes correctly on its own, so no "1 minutes ago"), and the **"Sync now" button returns** (it was dropped in #340) with an in-flight spinner. `summarize()` was rewritten to three friendly outcomes ("Updated from GitHub" / "Backed up" / "Up to date") feeding the refresh toast; the `capitalizedFirst` helper retired. Kit 262 green on Linux; swift-reviewer clean. ⚠️ App targets are macOS-CI-verified only — the live sync cadence, the toast, the quips, and the Sync-now button NEED on-device validation (edit gear/exercises/routines and confirm one semantic commit per boundary; pull-to-refresh shows the spinner + toast when connected and a quip with no spinner when not). — Foreground-only sync left edits sitting locally until the next app switch; boundary commits with readable messages make the repo a live, legible mirror, and the dead pull-to-refresh becomes either useful (a sync) or delightful (a quip).

**2026-07-13 — Connecting GitHub sync now fires the first sync immediately, instead of waiting for the next foreground** — After a successful connect, the repo's data was taking 15-30s to appear. Root cause: `GitHubSyncCoordinator.connect()` never kicks off a sync — the ONLY sync trigger is `scenePhase == .active` in `PlusPlusApp` (`onChange` at app root). But the authorize step opens GitHub in an in-app `SFSafariViewController` (a sheet in the SAME window scene, per the #343 decision), so connecting produces no background→active transition, and nothing fired the first sync. The data only landed the next time the user happened to background and return to the app. Fix: `GitHubSyncTray`'s existing `.onChange(of: sync.isConnected)` (which already dismissed the in-app browser on connect) now also kicks off the first pass — `Task { @MainActor in await sync.sync(context: modelContext, units: units) }` — reading `@Environment(\.modelContext)` (the app-root main context, since the tray is a sheet under `.modelContainer`) and `@AppStorage(WeightUnitSetting.key)`. The tray is the single surface where `connect()` is ever called (manual connect, the faulted-reconnect path, and the post-install `startAtConnect` auto-return all route through it), so this one site covers every connect completion. Safe against a race with the app-root foreground sync: `sync()` sets `activity = .syncing` synchronously before its first await and gates re-entry on `!isSyncing`, so whichever `@MainActor` Task runs first wins and the other no-ops. `onChange` only fires on a false→true transition, so opening an already-connected tray doesn't spuriously sync. Concurrency shape is a byte-for-byte match to the shipping app-root pattern (`PlusPlusApp.swift` captures the non-Sendable main context into a `Task { @MainActor in }` from a `@MainActor` `onChange` the same way). Deliberately NOT touched: the device-flow poll cadence in `GitHubDeviceFlow.pollForToken` (sleeps `interval`, GitHub's default 5s, before the first poll and +5s per `slow_down`), which adds its own ~5-15s between the user approving and the token landing — that's inherent to device flow and spec-compliant (polling faster risks a `slow_down` penalty), so it stays. swift-reviewer cleared the diff (no context-identity, Sendable, double-sync, spurious-fire, or Task-lifetime defect). ⚠️ App-target-only and the live device flow is not exercisable in a remote session — **needs on-device validation**: connect a fresh install and confirm the repo's routines/history appear within a second or two of "Connected", without backgrounding the app. — connect() completing and the data still not being there is the surprising part; the only reason it worked at all was an incidental foreground the in-app-browser flow doesn't guarantee.

**2026-07-13 — Dropped the app-wide `minimumScaleFactor`; text renders at its true, consistent size** — The #164 accessibility pass added a GLOBAL `.minimumScaleFactor(0.5)` at the app root (`PlusPlusApp.body`) as a "safety net" so fixed-height capsules/pills wouldn't clip at large Dynamic Type sizes. But `minimumScaleFactor` propagates through the ENVIRONMENT to every descendant `Text`, so any single-line label a touch too wide for its container silently shrank — **even at the default type size**, which is not what the net was for. Two visible symptoms Dave caught on build 71: (1) the Apple Health tray's "Not connected yet…" status line (`.footnote`, 13pt) rendered at roughly half size because it overflowed one line in the constrained card; (2) the Exercises-tab row subtitles (`.caption` + `.lineLimit(1)`) came out at DIFFERENT sizes depending on string length — short ones ("Shoulders · Bodyweight") at full 12pt, long ones ("Triceps · Assisted Pull-Up Machine · needs …") scaled down — so the same field read at different sizes across rows. Fix: **remove the global modifier entirely**, and put shrink-to-fit back where it belongs — LOCAL to the specific fixed-height/fixed-width controls that actually clip. An `axiom:swiftui-layout-auditor` pass enumerated the controls that had relied on the net; the ones that genuinely clip (equal-width `.frame(maxWidth:.infinity)` capsule SEGMENTS — the metric/muscle/equipment chips in `ExerciseEditorView`/`CatalogDetailViews`, the filter chips in `FilterChips`, and the compact fixed-height keys/CTAs `LibrarySwitcherKey` / "Back to now") each got their own `.minimumScaleFactor(0.6)`. Deliberately NOT added to flexible-width ROW names (exercise/routine/block names with `minHeight:`): a clean ellipsis truncation there is better accessibility than shrinking a name below 11pt, per the `axiom:accessibility-auditor`'s guidance (WCAG 1.4.4 — resize up to 200% without shrinking content). Also fixed the reveal tiles' subtitle, a hardcoded `.font(.system(size: 10))` (below the ~11pt HIG floor, no Dynamic Type scaling), → `.caption2` mono (11pt, scales, matches the footer). And the two Exercises/catalog row subtitles → `.lineLimit(2)` so the full "needs X" gear flag shows at one consistent size instead of scaling to fit one line. Broader follow-up left for a design pass (NOT done here to avoid a 205-call-site churn without on-device validation): many CTAs carry per-instance `.minimumScaleFactor(0.6)` on different base styles, so their absolute floors vary (7.8–10.2pt) at extreme Dynamic Type — the accessibility auditor recommends centralizing into 1–2 shared label modifiers with a single vetted floor. ⚠️ App-target only; not exercisable in a remote session — **needs on-device validation** at default AND at AX4/AX5 (the Health tray line reads full-size; every Exercises subtitle is the same size; no chip/segment clips at large sizes). — A global `minimumScaleFactor` trades a real default-size bug (readable text silently shrinking, the same field at different sizes) for an AX-size convenience the affected controls can provide locally; the correct granularity is per-control, and where nothing needs shrinking, text should render true and wrap/truncate rather than scale.

**2026-07-13 — Enrich the phone-side Health workout: real activity type + saved GPS route (#348)** — The phone's `HealthRecorder` wrote a BARE workout: hardcoded `.traditionalStrengthTraining`/`.indoor` (so an outdoor run logged on the phone landed in Health as indoor strength training) with no route, no metadata. Now `record(_:route:)` takes the run's GPS fixes: a non-empty route classifies the workout as `.running`/`.outdoor` and saves an `HKWorkoutRoute` (map in Health/Fitness); empty route stays strength/indoor, byte-identical to before. `RunLocationMonitor` now buffers the accepted fixes (`routeFixes`, same accuracy + no-teleport gate distance uses) and exposes `route`; `ActiveSessionView` reads it BEFORE `location.stop()` at finish and passes it in. Built the RIGHT way per Apple docs + the Axiom `axiom-health` skill: a **retrospective non-live `HKWorkoutBuilder`** (`beginCollection` → `insertRouteData` → `endCollection` → `finishWorkout` → `finishRoute(with:)` bound to the saved workout), NOT the deprecated `HKWorkout(activityType:…)` initializer (which saves an empty shell). `HKSeriesType.workoutRoute()` added to the share set (covered by the existing `NSHealthUpdateUsageDescription`; no `project.yml` change). Every step is failure-isolated (`guard success`), so Health stays a bonus never a gate — a route/auth failure drops the route and never touches the session finish. **Deliberately NOT attached: heart-rate samples** (they already exist in the store from the watch/strap; re-adding double-counts) **and energy** (the phone measures none; fabricating `activeEnergy` is wrong) — those belong to a live builder like the watch's, which is also why the phone/watch single-path double-count guard is preserved (watch imports never reach `HealthRecorder`). **Known limitations (swift-reviewer, both cosmetic/map-only):** the saved route covers the LAST contiguous outdoor segment (`stop()` clears `routeFixes`, matching the per-exercise distance re-base — this also fixes a run-then-strength session mis-classifying as a run); and a run paused then resumed elsewhere leaves one straight segment across the gap (a single `HKWorkoutRoute` is one polyline, can't encode a gap; distance already excludes it via the pause boundary). ⚠️ Every path is HealthKit/CoreLocation, inert under UI test and absent on the CI runner — **needs on-device validation** (log a phone outdoor run: confirm it lands in Fitness as a run with a route map; log a phone strength session: confirm exactly one workout, no route; confirm a watch-logged session still produces one workout). — The phone write is the surface most users see (most log on the phone); it was empty and mis-typed, and the GPS fixes we already collect for live pace were being thrown away.

**2026-07-13 — Axiom is installed by a SessionStart hook in remote sessions; the CLAUDE.md note corrected** — The `axiom@axiom-marketplace` plugin (Apple-platform skills + agents, marketplace `CharlesWiltgen/Axiom`) is declared in `.claude/settings.json` (`extraKnownMarketplaces` + `enabledPlugins`), but that declaration does NOT install it into an ephemeral remote/web container — every cloud session had been starting WITHOUT it (empty `~/.claude/plugins/installed_plugins.json`), which is why it looked unavailable and the CLAUDE.md note read as if Axiom were useless remotely. It isn't: `claude plugin install axiom@axiom-marketplace` works fine on the Linux box, and the plugin's **knowledge skills** (`axiom-health`, `axiom-swift`, `axiom-concurrency`, …) and **reasoning agents** (auditors like `security-privacy-scanner`) are plain markdown / subagents that load and help remotely — only its Xcode/Simulator-backed TOOLING is genuinely inert on Linux. `axiom-health` was used this session to validate the HealthKit sync work (it confirmed the retrospective non-live `HKWorkoutBuilder` path and the write-only `authorizationStatus` honesty). Fix: a `SessionStart` hook (`.claude/hooks/ensure-axiom.sh`) that idempotently `marketplace add`s + `install`s Axiom, gated on `$CLAUDE_CODE_REMOTE`, offline-safe (timeouts + `|| true`, never blocks session start), fast no-op once present. The post-hook container state is cached, so the install bakes in and later sessions start with it already on disk. Validated by uninstalling and re-running the hook (reinstalls in ~6s; a second run early-exits). The CLAUDE.md plugin line was rewritten to say skills/agents work remotely and how the hook installs it. ⚠️ Side note: `claude plugin uninstall` / `marketplace remove` REWRITE `.claude/settings.json` (they cleared `enabledPlugins`/`extraKnownMarketplaces` mid-test); the declarations were restored. — The plugin was silently absent in every remote session; a SessionStart bootstrap is the standard fix (mirrors the session-start-hook pattern for web dep install), and the note was actively misleading about Axiom's remote value.

**2026-07-13 — The reveal's Health tile became a real status row + config tray, promoted into SYNC** — The Health entry in `RevealSurface` was a placebo: a tile whose sub-label read "connected"/"connect" off a one-way `@AppStorage("healthAccessRequested")` flag set the moment `requestEverything` fired, regardless of what the OS actually granted, with no way to see real status or turn the integration off. It's now a status row in the **SYNC** section, sitting between GitHub and Calendar (all three are external-system sync), backed by a `HealthSyncCoordinator` (`@Observable @MainActor .shared`, mirroring the GitHub/Calendar coordinators) and a device-local `HealthSyncSettings.isEnabled` (UserDefaults, **defaults TRUE** — the app has always used Health opportunistically when granted, so this is an off-switch, not an opt-in; `object(forKey:) as? Bool ?? true` so a stored `false` is the user's choice and "never set" is on). **Honesty is the whole point:** HealthKit hides read authorization by design (an app can never learn whether its read requests were granted), so the only truthful system signal is the WRITE grant — `store.authorizationStatus(for: .workoutType())`. The row dot/word is: unavailable → gray "unavailable"; disabled → gray "off"; enabled + `.sharingAuthorized` → green "on"; enabled + `.sharingDenied` → red "denied"; enabled + `.notDetermined` → gray "connect". The write grant only ever moves through the system sheet (outside our views), so `refreshStatus()` is re-read on the surface's `onAppear` and on the tray's `scenePhase == .active`. The tray (`HealthTray`) is one "Use Apple Health" toggle (bound to enable/disable) plus a live read-out: authorized shows a green confirmation, denied shows a red note + "Open iOS Settings" (`UIApplication.openSettingsURLString` — the closest reachable deep link; HealthKit exposes no direct route to Health → Data Access), notDetermined shows a green "Connect" key that calls `requestEverything`. **Enable/disable is a real gate**, not just a label: `HealthSyncSettings.isEnabled` guards `HealthRecorder.record` (workout write) and `HeartRateMonitor.start`/`.summary` (live + summary HR reads) — turning Health off stops PlusPlus writing workouts and reading the live heart-rate stream on this iPhone. Deliberately NOT gated: `requestEverything`/`requestRead` (the enable path itself must ask), and `HealthAccess.resolvedMaxHeartRate` — the DOB→max-HR resolution is one-shot target ARITHMETIC (percent-of-max targets → bpm bands shown on device and pushed to the watch plan), not the live stream the toggle advertises stopping; gating it would silently recompute a user's configured HR targets against the fallback max the moment they disabled Health, and the watch (reading live HR through its own store) would zone-color against the wrong ceiling. Scope is this iPhone only: a watch-run workout keeps its own `HKWorkoutSession` write + HR read (the tray copy says so). The old flag, `connectHealth()`, and the `revealHealthTile` id are gone; the tiles grid drops to three (Data, What's new, About). No smoke test referenced the tile. NOT exercisable in a remote session (HealthKit is inert under `--uitest-reset` and absent on the Linux CI runner) — **needs on-device validation**: the row's dot/word reflect real grant state, the toggle gates writes/reads, and a denied grant routes to Settings. — A placebo status indicator is worse than none; the row now tells the truth HealthKit will actually confirm, and disable finally means something.

**2026-07-12 — Live outdoor-run pace, shown as target · actual beside heart rate (phone + watch)** — Heart rate was already live throughout an active workout on both platforms (header pill + set/rest lines), but pace was a hand-dialed number with no GPS anywhere. Added live GPS pace + distance for OUTDOOR runs, framed (with HR) as optional targets showing target · live actual, the actual accenting when it's meeting the target (pace improves DOWN so actual ≤ target; distance UP so actual ≥ target). **Kit:** `MetricProfile.isOutdoor` (additive `Bool`, `decodeIfPresent ?? false`, defaulted trailing init param — zero SwiftData migration; ⚠️ read only off a DECODED profile, since the `(metrics:distanceUnit:)` initializer resets it to false and reconstructed profiles like `secondaryMetricsList`/the watch `targetText` don't carry it); `DistanceUnit.paceReferenceMeters` (mile 1609.344 / km 1000 / 500 m) + `value(fromMeters:)`; and `LivePaceMeter` — a pure, Linux-tested value type that ingests MONOTONIC cumulative-distance samples and yields **current pace** over a trailing 20 s window (nil below `minSpan` 8 s, below `minSpeed` 0.4 m/s → "—" when stopped, or outside `DistanceUnit.paceRange` → GPS-spike clamp) and a **moving-time average** (Δt gated on speed + pause boundaries, so a red light doesn't inflate it). `WatchSync.Step.isOutdoor` + `PlanRoutine.isOutdoorRun` (every step outdoor — one `HKWorkoutSession` is one activity type). **Phone:** new `RunLocationMonitor` (`@Observable`, `CLLocationManager`, mirrors `HeartRateMonitor`'s generation-guard/`--uitest-reset`-inert discipline) runs BACKGROUND location (`allowsBackgroundLocationUpdates` + `UIBackgroundModes:[location]` + `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription`) so a pocketed, screen-off run keeps tracking — the standard running-app pattern (Dave chose this over foreground-only). It rejects fixes with accuracy > 30 m, accumulates distance between good fixes → the meter, and publishes current pace + distance. `ActiveSessionView` engages it only while the current exercise's decoded profile `isOutdoor`, keeps ONE session across a contiguous outdoor stretch (`onChange(of: activeLog?.order)`; `start()` is idempotent so distance doesn't reset per round), pauses GPS with the workout clock, and auto-fills a set's logged distance/pace actuals from the meter on completion (only a single-round piece, only when not already edited). New `LivePaceLabel`/`LiveDistanceLabel` sit beside `LiveHeartRateLabel` in the header + set + rest (this also gives the phone rest screen live HR, which it lacked). **Watch:** `WatchWorkoutController.start(outdoorRun:unit:)` configures the `HKWorkoutSession` as `.running`/`.outdoor`, collects `distanceWalkingRunning` (HealthKit's fused GPS+motion distance, better than raw `CLLocation`) into a `LivePaceMeter`, and requests `CLLocationManager` when-in-use auth (the workout consumes the fixes; we hold the grant). `WorkoutRunView` shows a `paceLine` (target·actual) on set + rest. **`isOutdoor` deliberately NOT in the interchange** (v1): the DTO carries `metrics`+`distanceUnit` only, built-ins re-resolve outdoor from the seed catalog on any recipient, and there's no user-facing outdoor toggle yet (census note added to `InterchangeMapping.swift`). **Deferred:** `HKWorkoutRouteBuilder`/route map, persisting average pace onto the finish stamp/history, an editor "Outdoor (GPS)" toggle + carrying the flag through the interchange, cycling live-speed. Kit 261 + CLI 26 green on Linux; **the app/watch targets and every GPS/CoreLocation path are NOT exercisable in a remote session — needs on-device validation** (outdoor run on iPhone locked/pocketed and on Apple Watch: pace tracks reality, distance accumulates, pace drops to "—" when stopped, shows through walk/rest, permission prompts once). — HR was essentially already done; live pace was the real gap. Framing all three cardio metrics as target·actual unifies them under the grammar HR already used, and GPS supplies the missing live actual.

**2026-07-12 — GitHub connect-flow tweaks (#343): sliding steps, in-app browser except Install, "connected" trigger text** — Three follow-ups to #340's one-tray redesign. (1) The wizard's step change now animates as a horizontal SLIDE rather than an instant swap (the reported failure was double-tapping "Done? Continue" through a step you didn't notice change). Built with the repo's existing `SwapInSheet` idiom — `switch step` inside a `ZStack(alignment: .topLeading)` so the outgoing/incoming steps OVERLAP, `.clipped()`, direction from an `advancing` flag, `Theme.Anim.selection` spring. The first cut applied the transition to a `.id(step)`-keyed view inside a VStack, which laid the two stages as vertical siblings mid-transition and briefly doubled the panel height (shoving the error note) — the ZStack overlap is why SwapInSheet uses it. (2) The Authorize step's "Open GitHub" and the create-repo fallback open in an in-app `SFSafariViewController` (new-in-#340 `SafariView`), auto-dismissed via `.onChange(of: sync.isConnected)` once the poll lands. But **Install stays EXTERNAL** (`UIApplication.open`): `SFSafariViewController` does not hand a universal link back to the app, so an in-app install would forfeit the post-install auto-return (`plusplus.fit/github/connected` → app); external keeps both the AASA and custom-scheme return paths. Authorize has no such dependency (the app polls in the background), so it's in-app. (3) The reveal's GitHub trigger shows the trailing status word again: green "connected" / red "disconnected" / gray none (Dave preferred the connected confirmation). **Token note:** the "connection expired minutes after connecting" report was NOT a bug — the GitHub App has "Expire user authorization tokens" OFF (confirmed with Dave), which is the correct config for a serverless device-flow app that holds no client secret and so cannot refresh; the message came from a forgotten manual disconnect. — Slides make the step change legible; the in-app browser stays everywhere it doesn't cost a deep-link return; "connected" is a useful confirmation.

**2026-07-12 — GitHub sync collapsed to one tray with an explicit connect wizard, and a persisted fault state for the trigger** — The reveal's GitHub sync used to be two surfaces: a light `SyncTray` (status + one button) that *pushed* a separate full-screen `GitHubConnectScreen`. Both are gone, replaced by a single `GitHubSyncTray` (new file) that carries the whole story; `GitHubConnectScreen.swift` deleted, `SyncTray` struct removed from `RevealSurface`, and the `RevealSurface.Push.connect` push case retired (only `.equipment` remains). The tray, when not connected, is a three-step wizard showing **exactly one enabled primary at a time**: **Create repo in GitHub** → **Install on GitHub** → **Connect this app** (the authorize/device-flow step), each non-terminal step advanced by a quiet **Done? Continue** button, with a `STEP n OF 3` bar + a **Back** control for orientation. Connected, the tray shows only a read-only connected line (repo · last synced) + **Disconnect** — the manual **Sync now** button was dropped (foreground sync still runs once per `.active` in `PlusPlusApp`). "Create repo" tries the GitHub app first via `UIApplication.open(https://github.com/new, universalLinksOnly: true)` and, if the completion reports it didn't open (app absent or doesn't claim `/new`), falls back to `https://github.new` in an in-app `SFSafariViewController` (new `SafariView` wrapper). **Trigger row** (`RevealSurface.syncRow`) is now `‹status circle› ‹GitHub mark› GitHub`: green when live (no trailing word), gray when never connected, red + "disconnected" when a connect attempt failed or a live connection expired/broke. The GitHub row and the Calendar row both dropped the redundant "sync" word and now sit under a shared `SYNC` section header (`syncSection`). That gray-vs-red split needs memory an expired token can't provide (auth-failure clears the token + coordinate, so a relaunch looks identical to a fresh install), so `GitHubSyncCoordinator` gained a `faulted` flag persisted in `GitHubSyncSettings.connectionFaulted` (UserDefaults): set on a genuinely failed `connect()` (declined/expired/network) or a sync auth-failure, but NOT on a `BootstrapError` (repo not installed yet is an unfinished setup, not a break — and it must not force the next open onto the authorize step), cleared on a clean connect or a **deliberate** disconnect (a manual disconnect is clean → gray, not a breakage). The trigger's red state is additionally gated on `connection == .disconnected`, so an unconfigured build never paints red from a stale flag. A faulted state (and the post-install auto-return, `startAtConnect`) both open the tray already on the authorize step, since the repo + App install already exist by then; only the redirect auto-starts the device flow. Copy per Dave's handoff (subtitle "Keep your data in sync with a GitHub repo", the three-paragraph description incl. the machine-rebellion line), no em dashes. UI-test identifiers renamed (`createRepoButton`/`installGitHubButton`/`connectGitHubButton`/`disconnectGitHubButton`/`continueStepButton`; no smoke test referenced the old `revealConnect`/`revealDisconnect`). Step-3 wording ("Connect this app" / "Authorize on GitHub to link this iPhone to your repo") chosen by Dave. — One surface reads better than a tray-pushes-screen hop; the wizard makes the two unavoidable GitHub trips (install on the repo, authorize this device) legible instead of two buttons with no order; the fault flag is the minimum state needed to tell "never set this up" from "it broke, reconnect".

**2026-07-12 — The ++ key opens a slide-to-reveal drawer, not a pushed AppMenuScreen** — The top-left ++ on every root header used to push a per-tab `AppMenuScreen` (→ `SettingsScreen`) onto that tab's `NavigationStack`. It now toggles a `RevealController` (an `@Observable @MainActor` in the environment) that a `RevealContainer` reads to slide the whole `TabView` right + scale it down (translate 0.72W, scale→0.86, corners→34, drop shadow + dim fade-in; the surface parallaxes in from the left and fades up), uncovering an app-level `RevealSurface` beneath — the Claude-drawer model. The container wraps the app ABOVE the NavigationStacks (in `RootTabView.body`) so it moves the native Liquid-Glass tab bar as one layer; the bar transforms because SwiftUI applies the layer transform to the hosted UIKit view (verified only in CI/on-device). `AppMenuKey` dropped its `action:` param (reads `@Environment(RevealController.self)` and toggles); `showingAppMenu` + the `AppMenuScreen` pushes were retired from Today/Routines/both catalog tabs, and `CatalogTabHeader` lost `onMenu`. **Settings is folded into the surface**: appearance/units/GitHub-sync-row/calendar-sync-row inline, the active `EquipmentLibrary` promoted to a hero card (name · items, and the downstream cascade "N exercises · N routines"), and the rarer things as tiles → bottom-sheet trays (Data, Health, What's new, About) plus the library/sync/calendar trays. `AppMenuScreen.swift` + `SettingsView.swift` deleted (`InterchangeDocument` + `WhatsNew` moved into `RevealSurface.swift`); export/import/health/GitHub-connect/calendar-sync plumbing preserved verbatim, not simplified — the sync tray pushes the real `GitHubConnectScreen`, the calendar tray drives the real `CalendarSyncCoordinator`, and "Choose your gear" still opens `CatalogBrowseScreen(setupMode:)`. Trays are native `.sheet`s (cornerRadius 22, drag indicator, `Theme.surface`), matching the app's existing tray grammar rather than hand-rolling the mock's bottom sheet. **Deliberately deferred:** edge-drag-to-OPEN (a left-edge grab would fight `.fullWidthSwipeBack()`/the interactive pop on pushed screens, and this remote session can't validate gestures) — open is tapping ++, close is tap-or-drag on the peeking app. **Copy-law fixes vs the mock:** library-row third field is "N routines" not "N due today" (the "due" ban, Dave's call), em dashes removed from the tray descriptions, and the dropped "Home Screen & Siri" blurb stays dropped (Dave's call). — Replaces the two-level pushed menu with one app-level surface; equipment is promoted because gear decides which exercises exist → which routines run. Design handoff: `About_view_transition_design.zip`.

**2026-02-19 — Use XcodeGen for project generation** — Declarative YAML (`project.yml`) is far cleaner for source control than Xcode's binary `.pbxproj`. The `.xcodeproj` is gitignored and regenerated from `project.yml` via `xcodegen generate`.

**2026-02-19 — Equipment as SwiftData model, not enum** — "Machine" is too broad; users who have a leg press don't necessarily have a lat pulldown. Specific equipment items enable filtering by what users actually own. Exercise→Equipment is to-many (Bench Press needs [Barbell, Bench]).

**2026-02-19 — ExerciseGroup as superset container** — Every exercise lives in a group, even solo ones. A group with >1 exercise is a superset. This avoids a separate "superset" concept and makes the data model uniform.

**2026-02-19 — Filter state as @Observable class** — `ExerciseFilterState` is a plain `@Observable` class, not a SwiftData model. Takes an array parameter instead of running queries — keeps filter logic pure and testable without a ModelContainer.

**2026-02-19 — Order management via `order: Int` + reindex helpers** — SwiftData relationships are unordered. Every ordered collection uses an `order: Int` property with `sortedX` computed properties and `reindexX()` methods called after every mutation. Sorted properties filter `isDeleted` objects.

**2026-02-20 — Dark mode default with user toggle** — `@AppStorage("appearance")` defaults to `.dark`. Applied via `.preferredColorScheme()` at app root.

**2026-02-20 — System semantic colors over custom color scales** — Use Apple's semantic colors (`.primary`, `.secondary`, `.label`, `.systemBackground`, etc.) for all UI chrome. They handle dark mode, Increase Contrast accessibility, Liquid Glass (iOS 26), and future OS changes automatically. Use built-in `Color.indigo` for brand accent. Custom color scales (Radix, etc.) fight the platform on iOS.

**2026-07-05 — Keyboard-free metric input (stepper + wheel picker)** — The `.number`-formatted TextFields had janky cursor behavior, and gym data entry shouldn't need a keyboard at all. `WorkoutMetric` (enum in `MetricInput.swift`) owns all value semantics — step size, wheel granularity (2.5 lb for weight so microplates are reachable), range, default-from-nil, formatting — as pure, tested logic; `MetricRow` renders it. Stepping an empty value lands on a sensible default (45 lb / 10 reps / 30 sec) instead of zero.

**2026-07-05 — Group actions via header menu, not EditButton** — With exercises as rows inside per-group Sections, `onMove`/`onDelete` on a ForEach of Sections doesn't produce usable edit controls. Groups are reordered/deleted via an ellipsis menu in each section header (Move Up / Move Down / Delete); individual exercises use swipe-to-delete, and deleting a group's last exercise deletes the group.

**2026-07-05 — Work tracked as GitHub issues, board synced via auto-add** — Remote Claude sessions can create/close issues but cannot touch the GitHub Projects board directly (no Projects v2 API in the toolset). The project board's "Auto-add to project" workflow ingests repo issues automatically; issue state drives board state.

**2026-07-05 — GitHub Actions macOS CI as the remote-session verification path** — Remote Claude sessions run on Linux: no Xcode, no Simulator, and ~~the sandbox network policy blocks installing a Swift toolchain (download.swift.org and Docker Hub's CDN are unreachable)~~ **2026-07-10 update: no longer true** — download.swift.org is reachable from cloud sessions; `scripts/install-swift.sh` installs Swift 6.1 in ~2–3 min and the PlusPlusKit + PlusPlusCLI suites (incl. DocsConformanceTests) run locally. Run them before pushing Kit/CLI changes; CI remains the only verifier for the app targets. Dave can also add the script to the cloud environment's setup script (results are cached across sessions). `.github/workflows/ci.yml` runs `xcodegen generate` + `xcodebuild test` on a `macos-26` runner for pushes to `main` and `claude/**` (plus manual dispatch). This verifies compilation and the unit test suite; it does NOT replace interactive Simulator validation (UI automation + screenshots), which still requires a local Mac session. Note: macOS runner minutes bill at 10x on private repos — keep triggers narrow. A shared `PlusPlus` scheme is defined in `project.yml` because `xcodebuild test` requires one.

**2026-07-05 — PT program as v1 acceptance scenario** — The user's shoulder-PT prescription (band work, external rotations, rep ranges like 3×15–20, form notes, a reference video link) is the concrete bar for v1: issues #7 (custom exercises + notes/video) and #8 (rep/set ranges) exist because the current model can't represent it.

**2026-07-05 — Sessions snapshot, never reference-only** — `WorkoutSession`/`SetLog` copy the workout name, exercise name/type, and targets at start time; the `workout`/`exercise` references are conveniences that may go stale. History must survive template edits and deletions. Tested explicitly.

**2026-07-05 — Superset execution order is strict rotation** — A group with exercises [A, B] and 3 sets expands to A1 B1 A2 B2 A3 B3 at session start (one flat, pre-ordered SetLog list). The execution UI just walks `nextPendingLog`; it holds no ordering logic of its own.

**2026-07-05 — Rest timer is date-based, not tick-based** — The countdown stores an end `Date` and renders via `TimelineView`; backgrounding or suspension can't drift it. Fixed 90s default with +15s/skip for v1.

**2026-07-05 — UI smoke tests + screenshot artifacts as the remote validation layer** — With no Mac available for days, XCUITests on the CI simulator exercise the real flows and export screenshots reviewable from any browser. Gated to `workflow_dispatch` + main pushes to control 10x macOS minute billing; dispatch the workflow on a branch (`actions_run_trigger` / the Actions UI) to run them pre-merge. First hands-on Mac session still owns #1.

**2026-07-05 — Watch sync will be WatchConnectivity, not CloudKit (planned)** — Full plan lives in issue #6 comments: Codable plan/result payloads (`updateApplicationContext` for template pushes, `transferUserInfo` for finished sessions), no SwiftData on the wrist for v1, HKWorkoutSession for runtime. CloudKit rejected for v1: iCloud dependency, opaque debugging, network-at-the-gym requirement.

**2026-07-05 — Developer platform: repo-as-backend, format-as-contract (see docs/PLATFORM.md)** — First niche is developers; training data lives as versioned JSON, eventually synced to a private GitHub repo the user owns (GitHub App + device flow, no PlusPlus server). The interchange format (schema v1, deterministic serialization for clean diffs) is the API contract for app export/import, repo sync, the CLI, and agents. Phases tracked in issues #20–#25.

**2026-07-05 — Sync is a pure three-way merge in the Kit** — `SyncPlanner.plan(local:remote:base:)` decides writes/pulls/conflicts per template file; `FileLayout` owns all repo paths and append-only session placement. Transports (GitHub API in the app for #23, disk in the CLI) stay thin adapters. Deletions deferred: a remotely-present, locally-absent file is adopted, never deleted.

**2026-07-05 — CLI is Swift, shells out to git, never authenticates** — Swift over Go because the contract (deterministic codec, validator) already lives tested in PlusPlusKit; a second implementation would drift byte-level. Conformance fixtures in PlusPlusKitTests/Fixtures are the language-neutral spec for future ports. The CLI operates on a clone; git is transport and auth; the app (#23) is the only surface with GitHub auth.

**2026-07-05 — PlusPlusKit package holds everything platform-pure** — MuscleGroup/ExerciseType, WorkoutMetric, RepTarget, and the interchange DTOs/codec/validator live in a local SwiftPM package with no SwiftUI/SwiftData. The `kit-test` CI job runs its tests on Linux (1x minutes); if it fails, someone leaked an Apple-only dependency into the shared core. SwiftData models, mapping (InterchangeMapping), and views stay in the app.

**2026-07-06 — Session v2: cursor navigation, weight carry-forward, auto-timers** — The session model gains `cursorOrder`: `currentLog` is the cursor's log when pending, else the first pending. `jump(to:redo:)` powers Do now / Redo / Skip-to from the overview sheet (redo reopens a completed log keeping its actuals as prefill); `complete(_:)` prefills actuals, carries an edited weight forward to the remaining pending sets of the same exercise, and advances the cursor (wrapping). Timed sets run a date-based AUTO TIMER (pause stores remaining; auto-logs at zero with haptic + a `TimerNotification` for backgrounded expiry; "log now" logs elapsed). Tested in SessionNavigationTests.

**2026-07-06 — v2 "quiet-terminal" design system; dark-only** — Dave's Claude Design prototype v2 (design handoff in issues #59–#67) supersedes the 2026-02-20 system-semantic-colors decision: a fixed GitHub-dark palette (`Theme` in `PlusPlus/Theme/Theme.swift`), green accent (#3fb950/#238636) replacing indigo, monospace for data/numbers, and no light mode (appearance toggle removed). Screens must draw colors from `Theme`, never ad-hoc literals. Accessibility trade-offs (Increase Contrast, dynamic type on fixed layouts) go on the #1 Mac checklist.

**2026-07-06 — Weight numbers are unit-agnostic; the unit is a declaration, not a conversion** — `WeightUnit` (lb/kg) in the Kit owns per-unit semantics (step 5/2.5, wheel 2.5/1.25, empty-bar default 45/20); `WorkoutMetric`'s weight paths take a `weightUnit:` param defaulting to `.lb`. The app setting (`@AppStorage("weightUnit")`, Settings segmented control) changes labels/stepping/defaults only — stored numbers never convert (225 stays 225). Bundles carry an optional `units` field (absent = lb, so old files stay valid); import adopts a bundle's declared unit; CLI stats honor it. The per-file repo layout stays lb-implied until a real kg repo needs a meta file.

**2026-07-06 — Renames are new exercises; identity IS the name** — Decided on #32's option 3: no stable IDs, no rename manifest. Renaming an exercise starts a fresh identity — history and "last time" stay with the old name; sync sees a new file next to the old. The editor warns on a real rename (`ExerciseDraft.isRename`, case-only changes exempt since slug and match are unchanged). Documented in docs/PLATFORM.md. Revisit stable IDs only if this chafes in practice.

**2026-07-06 — iPhone-only for v1** — `TARGETED_DEVICE_FAMILY = 1` (issue #41). Nobody had ever seen the app on iPad and nobody rests a 13" iPad on a squat rack; it still runs letterboxed there. Revisit post-v1 only if real demand shows up.

**2026-07-06 — Rest-end notification: scheduled always, presented only when backgrounded** — Extends the date-based rest timer: `RestNotifier` schedules one local notification (stable identifier, so each rest replaces the last) at rest start, reschedules on +15 s, cancels on skip/finish/discard/natural expiry. Foreground presentation is suppressed by the delegate (the ticking RestView is already on screen) rather than by conditional scheduling — no race with backgrounding. Permission is requested at first workout start, not app launch. Fully disabled under `--uitest-reset` so the permission dialog never eats a smoke test's tap. Felt behavior (sound while locked) still needs the #1 Mac pass.

**2026-07-06 — MCP server is a CLI subcommand with one heavily-fenced mutating tool** — `plusplus mcp` hand-rolls stdio JSON-RPC (~100 lines; no third-party MCP SDK, keeping the Linux build dependency-free). Read tools return interchange DTOs / the `--json` reports verbatim — no bespoke shapes to keep in sync. `propose_program_change` is the only write: `program/**.json` paths only, clean work tree required, must lint or it's fully rolled back, commits to a fresh branch, never pushes (the CLI still never authenticates — review/push/PR is the caller's job, and the repo's lint Action recipe is the second gate).

**2026-07-06 — Sync engine is transport-blind; sessions bypass the merge entirely** — `SyncEngine` (Kit) runs one sync pass — load base → fetch remote → `SyncPlanner` → resolve conflicts (keep-mine / take-theirs / postpone) → push → save the converged base — against two tiny protocols: `RepoStore` (the GitHub adapter in the app, a fake in tests) and `SyncBaseStore` (base-snapshot persistence, answering where "base" lives: the store owned by the app, a dictionary in tests). Postponed conflicts keep their old base entry so they re-conflict next pass. Finished sessions never enter the merge: `pushSession` is append-only via `FileLayout.sessionPlacement`, idempotent on retry, and composes its own "Log: …" commit message. What remains for #23 is UI + the GitHub `RepoStore` adapter + device-flow auth.

**2026-07-06 — Duration spans to a full hour; m:ss display above a minute** — Dogfooding the real program (#29) hit the old 900 s cap with "20–30 min spin bike". `WorkoutMetric.duration` now ranges 5–3600 with a tiered wheel (5 s steps to 2 min, 15 s to 10 min, whole minutes beyond) so the picker stays usable; values ≥ 60 s render as m:ss ("25:00") with no unit suffix. The interchange validator stays permissive (duration > 0) — the format doesn't encode UI limits.

**2026-07-06 — Rail direct manipulation is a custom gesture layer; List is out of the detail view** — Issue #78 (Dave's design): two separate long-press interactions — drag a row body to rearrange, drag a rail dot's ring edge to manage superset membership (full-width blue highlight while active, so state reads around the thumb). `List` was rejected a third and final time: its drag machinery can't express grouped semantics (2026-02 Sections attempt, 2026-07-05 header-menu retreat), gives no live preview, and has an unfixable drop ambiguity at group boundaries. The detail view now uses ScrollView + rows positioned absolutely by `RailLayout`; all geometry/semantics (drop slots, ring spans, clamps) are pure `RailArrangement` logic in PlusPlusKit (Linux-tested), and commits compose the existing Workout mutations plus `placeSolo`/`reorderExercise`/directional `splitExercise`. Division of labor kills ambiguity: gaps between groups always mean "land solo", in-ring positions exist only for the dragged row's own group, joining a ring is exclusively the ring gesture. Swipe actions are a small custom `SwipeRevealRow` (List-only feature otherwise). Gesture feel is unvalidated remotely — on the #1 checklist.

**2026-07-05 — Rep ranges shift, sets stay scalar** — `reps`/`repsUpper` express "15–20"; the stepper shifts the whole range to preserve the prescribed span. Set ranges ("2–3×10") deliberately collapse to one number — the range's meaning ("stop when cooked") lives with the user, not the model.

**2026-07-06 — TestFlight via unsigned archive + cloud signing on CI (#55)** — `testflight.yml` archives with `CODE_SIGNING_ALLOWED=NO` and lets `xcodebuild -exportArchive` do ALL signing via cloud signing with an ASC API key (which must be **Admin** role — App Manager gets "Cloud signing permission error"). Injecting a signing identity at archive time fails ("conflicting provisioning settings"); dev-profile signing fails on runners (no registered device). Build number = workflow run number; placeholder ++ icons + `ITSAppUsesNonExemptEncryption: NO` satisfy validation, and the watch target needs its own icon or the upload rejects.

**2026-07-07 — Dynamic Type text styles, capped at xxLarge (#82/#98)** — All `.system(size:)` fixed sizes became text styles (`.body`, `.footnote`, etc., keeping design/weight); display numerals ≥32 pt stay fixed. Rail geometry scales via `@ScaledMetric(relativeTo: .body)` row height threaded into the Kit's `RailMetrics`. Root caps at `.xxLarge` because the fixed v2 layouts break beyond it — full accessibility sizes are a #1-checklist item, not a regression.

**2026-07-07 — Adaptive palette + appearance setting (#97; amends the dark-only call in the v2 decision)** — `Theme` colors became `Color(light:dark:)` dynamic providers (UIColor trait resolvers, so previews and sheets resolve correctly); a GitHub-light palette mirrors the dark one. `AppAppearance` (system/dark/light, default **system**) drives `.preferredColorScheme` from Settings. Stored numbers and the design language are unchanged — light mode is the same quiet terminal, inverted.

**2026-07-07 — Equipment stays to-many; the editor makes it legible (#86)** — Dave's "multi-equipment feels weird" feedback was a UI problem, not a model problem: Bench Press genuinely needs [Barbell, Bench]. The editor presents equipment as removable REQUIRES chips with a caption spelling out the semantics ("needs all of these; filtering by what you own uses it") instead of an unexplained multi-select.

**2026-07-07 — Shared v2 controls live in `Views/Components/` (#85/#88/#91)** — Once a control appears in a second view it moves to `Views/Components/` rather than being redefined or imported across screens: `SearchField` (one search affordance app-wide), `SwipeRevealRow` + `SwipeActionButton` (one swipe affordance — reveal-then-tap, uppercase mono labels; native `.swipeActions` is out), `SheetHeader`/`SheetSectionLabel`/`SheetActionButton`/`MetricStepperRow`, `SegmentedTabs`. XcodeGen's `sources: [PlusPlus]` picks the directory up automatically.

**2026-07-07 — Scroll starvation was gesture claiming, not layout (#99)** — The detail-view bug where the exercise list couldn't scroll had two layers: offset-positioned rows gave the ScrollView no real content height (#92, necessary but insufficient), and `.gesture(LongPressGesture().sequenced(DragGesture()))` on rows claimed every touch before the ScrollView's pan could run. Long-press-initiated row gestures must use `.simultaneousGesture`; the handlers already ignore events until the long-press fires, and `scrollDisabled` during an active drag prevents fighting.

**2026-07-07 — Cadence is a Kit enum; due-state is pure; surfacing waits for design (#83)** — `WorkoutSchedule`: `.weekdays(Set<Int>)` (Calendar weekday numbers) or `.frequency(times:perDays:)` anchored to the last completion (rational slots — "3× per 7 days" is due when `daysSince × times ≥ perDays` — so it doesn't drift to every-3-days). `dueState(lastCompleted:today:calendar:)` takes the clock as a parameter. Stored app-local as additive `Workout.scheduleData` JSON; NOT in the interchange format until something consumes it. The editor lives in workout settings; how "due" renders on Home belongs to the #96 design.

**2026-07-07 — Today ⊕ History + "diff" handed to Claude Design; #96 on hold** — Dave's framing: Today's workout is just a pending history entry, and a per-exercise "diff" against last time should show how you're improving (incrementing — ++ing). This collapses the Today/History tabs into one timeline and is the app's identity moment, so it gets real design exploration (prompt delivered 2026-07-07) instead of a first-pass implementation. Nav restructure/onboarding (#96) and cadence surfacing ride on the handoff.

**2026-07-07 (night) — v3 "ink × increment green" palette; green is data, never chrome** — The Claude Design v3 handoff replaced the GitHub palette with warm ink/cream neutrals; full-chroma green survives only on data (deltas, net chips, committed nodes, next-due values, the ++ glyph). New `primaryFill`/`onPrimary` tokens carry every filled control; `accentButton`/`onAccent` died. Superset blue desaturated (3B6FB0/7FA3D0, Dave's pick) to recede behind the green.

**2026-07-07 (night) — Four bottom tabs; History and the FAB die** — RootTabView with a custom quiet-terminal bar (Canvas commit-node/cards/list/dumbbell icons): Today · Workouts · Exercises · Equipment. Creation is contextual per tab header +; settings lives on Today; LibraryView split into the two catalog tabs. Tab switching is a `switch`, so per-tab navigation state resets on switch — accepted for v3.

**2026-07-07 (night) — Today ⊕ History shipped: the timeline IS the app** — Pending (due) workouts render as dashed cards with per-exercise diffs against last performance; committed sessions sit below on the same rail. `WorkoutDiff` (Kit, pure): weight wins over reps in the summary, never-performed = new, regressions neutral (anti-shame), net chip sums positive movement only. The diff PRIOR is one real set — the top completed set's weight with THAT set's reps (mixing max-weight with last-set reps described sets that never happened).

**2026-07-07 (night) — Carried-over weekday due-ness; occurrences never stack** — A missed Thursday keeps the workout due through Friday ("due since thu") and a late completion satisfies that occurrence; the next scheduled day supersedes rather than stacks. `dueSince` feeds captions; `shortLabel` ("mon/thu", "2×/7d") is the shared pill vocabulary. Editor tabs are Off / Days / Pace with Monday-first 38 pt circles, accent-tinted selection (due-ness is data), and occupancy dots for other workouts' days.

**2026-07-07 (night) — Onboarding: equipment access IS the Equipment tab list** — Two skippable beats (preset cards + chips → Equipment.inLibrary; starter push/pull split composed slot-by-slot from owned built-ins). Ownership filters the catalog everywhere per Dave's call: hide + "show all" escape hatch + "needs X" cues; curated library rows are never hidden, only flagged. Custom-equipment deletion strips references first (the relationship has no inverse).

**2026-07-07 (night) — Watch v1 is WatchConnectivity with a frozen-plan run view; no HealthKit** — Kit `WatchSync` payloads (plan pre-expanded in rotation order; ISO 8601 deterministic JSON). Phone pushes via updateApplicationContext on launch/backgrounding; results return via transferUserInfo and import SYNCHRONOUSLY inside the delegate callback (WCSession acks on return — deferred work can permanently drop a delivered workout). The wrist freezes its step list at first render so mid-session plan pushes can't corrupt a live workout; partial sessions ship on early exit or unexpected pop; a watch-local notification carries "rest over" through suspension (no HKWorkoutSession until #90 un-defers).

**2026-07-07 (night) — Rail gestures live on a UIKit UILongPressGestureRecognizer** — Third strike on the detail scroll bug: SwiftUI's LongPressGesture starves UIScrollView's pan in ANY composition (sequenced, simultaneous, either order). A zero-size probe attaches one UIKit recognizer to the enclosing UIScrollView — the primitive system drag-to-reorder uses — reporting rail-content coordinates; geometry routes ring (x < 37) vs drag, bounded to actual row extents (RailLayout.exercise(at:) clamps to nearest BY DESIGN, so callers must bound y). Regression-tested by a 16-row seeded workout in the UI suite.

**2026-07-07 (night) — Overnight adversarial bug hunt: 3 agents, ~20 verified findings, fixed same night** — Highest-severity: staging an empty-but-scheduled workout committed a permanent 0-set session and satisfied the schedule; the diff prior described nonexistent sets; watch results could be dropped after the WCSession ack; a hold anywhere in the detail viewport hijacked the nearest row. Pattern worth keeping: hunt on fresh code with parallel reviewers told to VERIFY against the actual code before reporting, then fix in the same PRs that introduced the surface.

**2026-07-07 (day) — Native Liquid Glass TabView replaces the custom bar; HIG type/contrast/target pass (#130)** — Dave's build-10/11 feedback: the v3 custom bottom bar died in favor of the system `TabView` (`Tab(_:systemImage:value:)`) — system hit targets, accessibility, and scroll-edge treatment for free; the quiet-terminal identity lives in the content, not the chrome. Same pass bumped small text a tier toward HIG minimums, fixed `textFaint` contrast, standardized 44 pt targets (header +, day circles), and added tray headroom.

**2026-07-07 (day) — Set screen redesigned around the values (#131)** — The active-exercise screen felt empty and Log set sat dangerously close to the steppers. Weight/reps are now two big card columns center-stage (44 pt mono values opening the wheel, 56 pt −/+ buttons); Log set stands alone in a bottom dock with 28 pt of clearance.

**2026-07-07 (day) — Onboarding is the timeline: setup steps as gated commits (#132, supersedes the #125 cover and #129's land-on-Workouts)** — The Claude Design setup-as-timeline handoff: no onboarding screen at all. A fresh install lands on Today, where three setup steps render as timeline entries stacked bottom-up like commits — equipment (1 of 3), first workout (2 of 3, gated), schedule (3 of 3, gated) — ready steps as dashed pending cards with a CTA, gated steps dimmed with "needs X first", done steps as committed-style cards (green node, `date · summary`, edit ›). The scaffold yields to real history at the first logged session. Only equipment stores a flag (`SetupState`, UserDefaults) — its done-ness can't be derived; workouts and schedules are derived live, so the steps self-heal (delete your last workout and the step reopens). The equipment picker and starter-split seeder are standalone sheets shared with Settings.

**2026-07-07 (eve) — SwipeRevealRow hit-testing + session identity save (#134)** — Two tap bugs, one lesson each: `opacity(0)` does NOT remove a view from hit testing (hidden swipe actions now `allowsHitTesting(false)` and `.plain`-styled — List routes row taps into default-styled buttons); and `fullScreenCover(item:)` keys on `persistentModelID`, which CHANGES at the first save of a fresh model — `WorkoutSession.start` saves synchronously so a live session never re-presents. Same PR: per-equipment `weightStep` (Kit `stepOverride` param; smallest override among an exercise's gear wins) and the SF Symbols sweep (no pictographic glyphs in strings; typography like Δ − → stays).
