**2026-07-07 (eve) — Catalog is a graph; built-ins editable except name (#136/#137/#139)** — Exercises/Equipment tabs push real detail screens (cross-links: equipment ⇢ exercises ⇢ routines; creation at every dead end); sheets survive only for create/edit forms — a rule that then made the catalog browser a pushed page too (Dave's call): CatalogBrowseScreen lists the WHOLE catalog with membership Toggles (nothing vanishes on add), All/In-library/Not filter, the picker's muscle/equipment filter sheets reused. Built-ins open in the full editor with the name locked (identity IS the name, #32) and revert-to-default backed by a SeedData definitions table.

**2026-07-07 (eve) — Routines rename, no schema bump (#144)** — Dave: templates are ROUTINES, performed things are WORKOUTS. Renamed everywhere (code, interchange keys `workouts`→`routines` and `workoutName`→`routineName`, FileLayout `program/routines`, fixtures, UI); kept WorkoutSession/SetLog/WorkoutMetric/"Workout Complete"/"Start workout". Schema stayed v1 — zero external users made it the free window. Entity renames reset local stores (accepted; data was throwaway).

**2026-07-07 (eve) — Share links carry the routine inside the URL fragment (#145, PLG #141-A)** — `RoutineShareLink` (Kit): `{share:1, units?, routine: RoutineDTO, exercises: [ExerciseDTO]}` → sorted-keys JSON → base64url behind a "0" encoding tag on `https://plusplus.fit/r#…`. Fragments never reach servers — privacy by construction — and sorted keys make identical routines produce identical links. The static viewer renders client-side; `plusplus://r#…` opens ShareImportSheet, which imports via the normal interchange policies. Explicit Info.plist now (URL types can't be INFOPLIST_KEY settings) with CFBundleVersion still `$(CURRENT_PROJECT_VERSION)` for TestFlight numbering. Universal links deferred until the associated-domains entitlement + real team ID.

**2026-07-07 (eve) — plusplus.fit hosts on Vercel** — Domain already lives in Dave's Vercel account; static + preview deploys + serverless headroom beat migrating elsewhere. `/r` viewer + `/privacy` shipped; GitHub Pages workflow retired; Dave's one-time dashboard import connects the repo.

**2026-07-07 (late eve) — Org transfer + open source: AGPL-3.0 app, MIT Kit/CLI (#154)** — Both repos moved to the `plusplusinc` org and went public (old URLs redirect). Dave's licensing call: the app under AGPL-3.0 (contribution-friendly, structurally hostile to rebranded App Store clones), PlusPlusKit + PlusPlusCLI + the conformance fixtures under MIT (the contract is meant to be adopted without copyleft obligations). A full-history secrets scan ran clean before the flip. Free public-repo Actions minutes obsolete the 10x macOS-billing caution.

**2026-07-07 (late eve) — Store recovery: destroy-and-recreate on unopenable stores (#153, build 16)** — Build 15 crash-looped for update-in-place installs (the #144 entity renames made pre-15 stores unreadable and init `fatalError`'d). The app now deletes the store files (+ -shm/-wal) and recreates on open failure, clearing the stale setup flag; the setup timeline self-heals. Beta-appropriate — data is explicitly throwaway until sync ships; the 1.0 migration policy is #155. In-memory (`--uitest-reset`) failures still fatalError: a test store that can't open is a bug, not a recovery case.

**2026-07-07 (late eve) — Platform batch 1: Live Activity, widgets, App Intents (#147 → PR #152, build 17)** — The rest countdown is a Live Activity (Dynamic Island compact/expanded/minimal + Lock Screen banner), date-based like the in-app timer and driven from RestNotifier's existing lifecycle moments so the island and the rest-over notification can never disagree. New `PlusPlusWidgets` extension target + `PlusPlusShared/` sources; widgets can't see SwiftData, so the app writes a tiny `WidgetSnapshot` to the App Group (`group.com.davidcole.plusplus`) on launch/backgrounding — the same moments the watch plan pushes. Widgets: Due today + Streak (12-week mini contribution row). App Intents: StartRoutineIntent/DueTodayIntent/OpenTodayIntent with shortcut phrases; `RoutineEntity` keys on the name (identity IS the name, #32). Extension gotcha: an empty `CFBundleVersion` makes the simulator refuse the .appex — `CURRENT_PROJECT_VERSION: 1` in project.yml, overridden by TestFlight's run number. Display-only island for now (#157 adds controls); snapshot freshness is #159.

**2026-07-07 (late eve) — Branch protection: required checks on main; ci.yml runs on every push** — A repository ruleset gates merges on `test` + `kit-test` + `cli-test` passing (squash-only). Cancelled required checks must be re-run before merge. The docs-only `paths-ignore` in ci.yml died: a docs-only push produces no runs, the ruleset waits for checks that never come, and a green `workflow_dispatch` run on the identical SHA did not satisfy it in practice — free public-repo minutes make always-run the simple correct answer. The Claude GitHub App needed installing on the plusplusinc org for API merges to work at all.

**2026-07-08 — Entitlements require a signed archive; self-signed embedding + portal capabilities (#90 fallout, builds 18–22)** — The unsigned-archive pipeline (#55) shipped NO capability entitlements: `CODE_SIGNING_ALLOWED=NO` skips the entitlements phase, so the archive carries no `.xcent` and the export's cloud signing requests nothing — silently fine for entitlement-free builds 1–16, silently broken for build 17's App Group, loudly broken (90701) once the watch's `WKBackgroundModes: workout-processing` DEMANDED healthkit in the signature. Portal capabilities alone didn't fix it (build 20: profiles carried healthkit, the request still didn't). Ad-hoc archive signing is refused for iOS/watchOS SDKs (build 19). What works (build 22): after archiving unsigned, re-sign the three bundles inside the archive with a **throwaway self-signed identity** via the codesign CLI (`-macalg sha1 -keypbe/-certpbe PBE-SHA1-3DES` on the p12 — macOS's importer can't read OpenSSL 3 defaults), embedding each target's xcodegen-generated entitlements; the export's re-sign reads those as its request and the App Store profiles (capabilities enabled in the portal by Dave) satisfy it. New capability = enable it on the App ID in the portal + entitlements file in project.yml; the workflow needs nothing new. TestFlight distribution never depended on any of this — App Store profiles carry no device list.

**2026-07-08 — No obligation vocabulary: "due" is banned from every user-facing surface (#172)** — Dave's call, sharper than a rename: a routine's presence on Today IS the statement, so nothing needs to say "due" (or any replacement). Card captions died outright, the Today header lost its "N due" tally, the *Due today* widget became **Today** (`kind` and struct names unchanged — renaming orphans installed widgets/shortcuts), Siri answers "Today: Push Day", the rest-day line shows plain calendar info ("next wed — Push Day"), and snapshot captions carry the schedule's own `shortLabel`. "Due since X" was also an anti-shame violation — that whole caption class is gone. Kit API names (`dueState`, `dueSince`) stay internal. The general rule for future copy: presence and position communicate; obligation words don't get written.

**2026-07-08 — Selection blue #62b6de: green is data, blue is UI state (#176, direction set)** — Dave picked the Claude Design blue (#62b6de, or tuned variants) as the selected/interactive color, resolving the pill-state inconsistency (white fills vs green fills) by giving each hue one job: full-chroma green stays data-only (v3 rule), blue carries selection and interactive state. Implementation rides the Design v4 handoff (per-scheme variants, text-on-blue contrast, distance from the desaturated superset blue). Companion rule, also Dave's: **the app must always feel fast and responsive to input** — selection transitions are snappy (~0.15 s), never default-slow, never absent.

**2026-07-08 — Design v4 implemented in one overnight pass (PRs #188/#190/#191/#192/#193)** — Tokens: `selected` #1A7FA8/#62B6DE + tint (12%/16%) + ring (55%); `info` retired ("new" = data green); every selectable speaks tint+content+ring with 0.15 s ease-out and selection haptics. Trays: title upper-left + primaryFill commit capsule (SSC table); pickers get the ✕ variant. Routine settings and app settings became pushed pages; text entry stays in trays (notes, rename). The superset rail: solid spine, return loop at x=3 drawn in border at rest (collapsed it's just an order map), selection-blue full-row highlight + punched SUPERSET legend only while the ring gesture is live — outside a live gesture the app has exactly one blue; SUPER swipe died. Onboarding equipment rides the real catalog (setupMode: preset strip + pinned Done + populate offer); the catalog top got the 44 pt density pass (ownership toggle moved into the equipment filter tray, list-end escape hatch). TipKit replaced ambient captions, never configured under UI test (since #270 TipKit is superset-only — see that decision).

**2026-07-08 — Routines rename in place; the "renames are new identities" law stays exercise-only (#189)** — Routine identity is the SwiftData reference (sessions link directly; name matching is only the broken-reference fallback), so editing `routine.name` keeps schedule anchoring and history — past sessions deliberately keep their snapshot name. Duplicate names are blocked case-insensitively. Accepted edges: Siri shortcuts pinned to the old name re-pick; an in-flight watch session imports under the old name; the future sync repo sees a new file (policy when #23 is real). Exercises are unchanged: their names ARE the history join key.

**2026-07-08 — Fresh installs seed the catalog, not the library (#185); built-in equipment self-heals (#186)** — Built-in exercises seed `inLibrary = false`; population is the user's optional call at the end of equipment setup ("Add N exercises your equipment supports?" / "Start empty"), and anything used joins the library on its own (starter seeder already did). Existing stores untouched. Separately, Dave's store surfaced Bench Press as bodyweight though the seeder is provably correct — the loss path couldn't be reproduced (seeder, name-matched import, identity-scoped deletion, editor draft all ruled out), so a one-shot UserDefaults-keyed repair restores empty-equipment built-ins from the canonical definitions table, with regression tests locking the requirements. If it recurs post-repair, there's a live repro to chase.

**2026-07-08 (late) — Exercise defaults bump from routine edits (#187)** — Exercise carries optional defaultWeight/defaultReps/defaultRepsUpper/defaultDurationSeconds; fresh routine entries prefill from them; editing targets in the planning sheet writes back (the latest prescription anywhere IS the default — Dave's call). Editor gains a DEFAULTS stepper card with Clear. Interchange fields are additive; schema stays v1.

**2026-07-08 (late) — Widgets compute, snapshots don't assert (#159)** — WidgetSnapshot carries every schedulable routine's encoded RoutineSchedule + lastCompleted; the widget extension links PlusPlusKit and computes due-ness per timeline entry (now + 7 calendar midnights), the streak rolls forward to the entry date (stale snapshots can't overstate), Siri computes at ask time. Frozen `due` list retained solely as the pre-#159 fallback.

**2026-07-08 (late) — Island rest controls run in the app's process (#157)** — +15s/Skip are LiveActivityIntents in PlusPlusShared (both targets see the type; the system executes in the app process) posting .plusplusAdjustRest; ActiveSessionView routes to the same extendRest/endRest as the on-screen buttons. Critical pairing: scheduleRestEnd no longer tears down the activity (update is background-legal, request is foreground-only — the swift-reviewer agent caught +15s destroying its own island pre-merge).

**2026-07-08 (late) — Docs are verified claims, not prose (Dave's ask)** — three parallel doc audits fixed every stale claim (watch "stub", test counts, private-repo PAT instructions, PLATFORM.md phase status and commit-message examples); PLATFORM.md's JSON examples are now EXECUTABLE (DocsConformanceTests in the CLI target decodes + validates them on Linux CI — it caught its first drift within an hour); a docs-drift PostToolUse hook names the owning doc when contract files change; the standing rule lives in CONTRIBUTING.md.

**2026-07-08 (late) — Committed .claude/ dev setup (Dave's ask)** — skills (ci-status / pr-flow / testflight), agents (swift-reviewer with the repo's proven bug classes — paid for itself on its first run; doc-verifier), the docs-drift hook. .gitignore keeps only settings.local.json out.

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Screens that commit edits on exit must also commit in `onDisappear`** — The full-width swipe-back (#198) pops entirely in UIKit: SwiftUI's `onBack` closures never run, so RoutineSettingsScreen's swipe exit silently discarded an uncommitted rename (swift-reviewer catch). The rule: any screen whose back-chevron commits state duplicates that commit in `onDisappear`, idempotent and guarded against the deleted-model race. Companion: Save buttons disable on invalid drafts instead of silently reverting.

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Library search is a bottom Liquid Glass dock; every list under a search field scroll-dismisses (#213/#214)** — Dave's Messages-pattern ask, which also fixed a real trap: the header search had no cancel affordance and the keyboard covered the tab bar. `SearchDock` (Components) is a glass capsule + the tab's create action in a `glassEffect` circle that morphs + → ✕ while focused (✕ unfocuses and clears); it rides `safeAreaInset(edge: .bottom)` so rows scroll under the glass and the dock rides above the keyboard, drops focus `onDisappear` so pushes can't strand the keyboard, and carries `librarySearchField` (not `searchField` — the pushed catalog browser has its own). The catalog browser and picker keep top fields (reachable exits; setupMode's Done bar owns the browser's bottom edge).

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Platform polish batch (#216): motion carries meaning, one mechanism each** — Selection SLIDES (SegmentedTabs' blue fill is one `matchedGeometryEffect` object); data ROLLS (`contentTransition(.numericText)` on every steppable value, directional where the raw number is at hand); completion THUDS differently (medium impact per logged set, `.success` only at the finish — the whole-path invariant took a second pass because the duration auto-timer had its own `.success`); navigation ZOOMS (`navigationTransition(.zoom)` from routine/pending/committed cards into their screens, `persistentModelID`-keyed, silent fallback when no source is on screen). Skipped deliberately: chip-slide across flow-layout rows (diagonal glide reads as glitch), `tabBarMinimizeBehavior` (uncoordinated next to the fixed dock), scroll-in entrance effects (decoration).

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Today rail grammar: green ring = actionable, grey = inert/gated, purple = done (Dave's call)** — Completes the GitHub mapping #201 started: hollow green ring for a ready workout or ready setup step (open PR), neutral grey ring for the rest-day item (new `.inert` node — it previously shared the ready look), fainter ring for gated steps (draft), filled purple for committed (merged). Ready stays HOLLOW: filled is done's shape.

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Orphaned sessions are salvaged, never stranded** — A `WorkoutSession` with `endedAt == nil` that isn't presented is invisible to every query, unsatisfies the schedule, and had no recovery path (mid-workout crash always; possibly a zoom drag-dismiss the exit dialog never sees — device check pending). TodayView salvages on cover dismissal and on appear: finish it when sets were logged, delete it when empty (swift-reviewer catch on the zoom PR; closes a pre-existing hole).

**2026-07-08 (afternoon) — Routine creation auto-suffixes duplicate names** — #189's case-insensitive uniqueness now holds at creation too (`Routine.uniqueName`): a colliding name gets " 2"/" 3" instead of a block, because creation happens in an alert with nowhere to surface validation. A duplicate pair would have jammed settings-rename for both and made Siri/session name-matching ambiguous.

**2026-07-08 (evening) — Equipment catalog is comprehensive and generic; inclusion = "can gate an exercise" (#222)** — A research sweep of Rogue/Rep/Titan home catalogs and Hammer Strength/Life Fitness/Precor-class commercial lines took the catalog 40 → 100 generic types (no brand names). The rule that decides membership: an item qualifies only if some exercise can genuinely REQUIRE it (Dip Belt in; straps/chalk/collars out), and near-synonyms fold into one type (functional trainer → Cable Machine, prowler → Sled, buffalo bar → Cambered Squat Bar). Judgment-call inclusions: Weightlifting Chains (the band precedent) and Slant Board (travels with Tibialis Bar). Newcomers reach existing stores catalog-only and un-owned via the #95 top-up.

**2026-07-08 (evening) — Routine catalog: static templates, three authored attributes, facet chips (#223)** — 40 browsable templates behind the Routines tab + (the library-tab grammar: adding starts from a catalog; blank creation is its first row — the New Routine alert moved there from the header). Templates are static `RoutineTemplate` definitions, NOT seeded Routine rows (those would pollute the user's list and schedule queries); Add instantiates through the existing structure mutations + `Routine.uniqueName`, applies template targets over exercise defaults, joins referenced exercises to the library, and pushes into the new routine. Only Focus (split vocabulary), Effort (Light/Moderate/Intense — names the session, never the user), and Style (Strength/Build/Conditioning/Recovery) are authored; time, equipment, and muscles DERIVE from content so they can't lie. Filtering is four single-select chips with anchored Menus, live AND filtering, active values in solid selection blue, leading ✕ to clear — deliberately no Filters-sheet-with-Apply (at ~40 in-memory items that's the Save button of filtering); GEAR filters by ownership fit (My equipment / No equipment), not gear lists; sort (Featured/Name/Time) rides the toolbar. Full research + tradeoffs recorded on #223. Schedule is deliberately NOT auto-applied on add — a suggestion may render as copy, but obligations never appear on Today unchosen. `RoutineCatalogTests` pins every exercise reference to SeedData so content can't drift.

**2026-07-09 — Parallel feature branches replace the serialized single-branch flow (Dave's authorization)** — The one-designated-branch rule was a session-harness default, never a repo decision, and it serialized every unit of work behind the previous PR's CI (held commits, stashed diffs, "wait for merge before starting"). Dave, on learning this: "That sounds terrible. I authorize you to make however many branches you need, and parallelize work." New shape (pr-flow skill rewritten): one `claude/<slug>` branch per unit of work off fresh main, PRs open and run CI concurrently, the later-merging branch rebases mechanically on same-file overlap, force-with-lease only on own branches, `subscribe_pr_activity` per PR. ci.yml already triggered on `claude/**`, so nothing CI-side changed.

**2026-07-09 — Swipe stays custom everywhere; the native experiment reversed same-day (#231)** — Dave picked native List swipes, then on learning the rail view can't use List (so the app would MIX native and custom swipe feels) reversed: "Do non native and just get it working right." The thrice-reported snap-back was root-caused, not fudged: SwipeRevealRow's onEnded read the few-point rightward lift-drift of a relaxing finger as close-intent via predictedEndTranslation, overriding onChanged's live commit — fixed with a momentum floor (|momentum| > 36 required to override the live position). One swipe affordance app-wide again; the honest labels stayed (a custom's removal is DELETE, a built-in's is REMOVE).

**2026-07-09 — Search is an expanding toolbar button, catalogs only (#233/#234)** — Dave's build-31 call: the library tabs (short, curated) lost search entirely; catalog surfaces get a top-right circular magnifier expanding in place to field + ✕ (trailing slot, so it can cover the inline title but never the back chevron — his constraint, by construction). Drilled-in screens carry inline titles sized with the back button. The SearchDock died. Focus is requested in the field's own onAppear via a one-shot flag — a focus request made before the view exists is silently dropped, and an unconditional onAppear re-summons the keyboard on pop-back.

**2026-07-09 — Equipment ownership is opt-in; the reset chose honesty over grandfathering (#232, PR #245)** — An all-owned default meant the ownership filter said nothing. The whole catalog now seeds out of the library (ownership rides the same `populateLibrary` smoke-test shortcut as exercises); both library tabs explain themselves when empty and CTA into the catalog; onboarding toggles gear ON. Existing stores got a keyed one-shot reset (Dave: "Reset mine too") that un-owns built-ins, never touches custom gear, and clears the setup flag (the flag described the curation the reset erased). Companion law from the review: **the picker never ownership-hides** — every picker row is a library/custom row and curated rows are flagged, never hidden (#113); the hide would have read as data loss post-reset.

**2026-07-09 — Scratch workouts: sessions without routines are first-class (#239, PR #247)** — "Start empty workout" on the rest-day card and swap-in sheet creates a routine-less WorkoutSession ("Scratch workout"); an empty stage (which never auto-finishes — 0-set commits are the empty-staging bug class) grows solo blocks from the picker, also reachable mid-session from the overview sheet (stacked, so no dismiss-then-present drop). Finished sessions refuse appends — the duration auto-timer can finish a session under an open picker. At the finish, "Save as routine" materializes what was PERFORMED (set counts as done, targets from each block's last completed log), joins exercises to the library, uniques the name, and relinks + renames the session so the run becomes the routine's first performance. Ad-hoc sessions satisfy no schedule; abandoned empties ride the orphan salvage.

**2026-07-09 — FTUE audit (#246): three agent walk-throughs, quick wins shipped, structural fixes as parallel PRs** — Dave's before-bed mandate ("find the rough edges… evaluate tradeoffs, pick, and execute autonomously"). Findings + plan live on #246; the quick wins (PR #248): exits are equivalent (swipe-back carries the populate offer), the curation tip stays out of setup, zero-owned populate copy, caption dedup, and OWNED as equipment's one word ("library" stays exercises-only). Deferred with issues: #249 bodyweight "— lb" column, #250 schedule-step multi-routine, #251 equipment-picker grouping, #252 smaller follow-ups. Decision recorded: **no return-visit celebration is deliberate** — yesterday's purple node under today's green ring IS the acknowledgment (#172/anti-shame).

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Value navigation destinations register at stack roots, never on pushed screens (#262)** — Build 33's catalog triangle: `navigationDestination(for: RoutineTemplate.self)` lived inside RoutineCatalogScreen, itself pushed via `navigationDestination(isPresented:)` — template taps hit SwiftUI's missing-destination placeholder while `path.append(routine)` from the same screen worked fine (Routine.self was registered at the root). Every value destination now lives at its owning NavigationStack's root; `isPresented:` destinations on pushed screens remain fine (SettingsScreen precedent).

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Swipe snap-back root-caused: row content carries NO tap affordance; SwipeRevealRow owns activation (#263)** — Third user report; the two prior fixes had hardened real but secondary paths inside the drag. The actual closer: row content was a Button, the reveal drag rides `simultaneousGesture` (deliberately non-cancelling so the List pan coexists), and a Button fires on touch-up-inside regardless of drag distance — the card moves WITH the finger, so the touch never leaves bounds — and every consumer's tap handler treated tap-while-open as close. The finger-lift ending each reveal closed the row it had just opened. Fix v1 (slop-based tap ButtonStyle) was REJECTED by its own new regression test on CI: the offset chases the finger, so movement relative to the row is ~zero — no slop heuristic can engage. Fix v2 (shipped): content has no Buttons or onTapGestures; SwipeRevealRow takes `onTap` and composes it with the drag in an `ExclusiveGesture` — once the drag activates (16 pt), the tap is structurally impossible; tap-while-open closes inside the component. Proven by a red→green pair: a probe branch (main's code + the test) failed at "the revealed action must be tappable" — the device bug at the exact assertion — and the fix branch passed it. Contract documented on the component; the rail rows' bare onTapGestures (same latent class) were converted too. Dave's build-34 field report matched the prediction exactly (rail rows fine, Button rows snapping).

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Today rail nodes are rings, never filled (#264)** — Dave's call: every circle on the left rail is stroke-only; done became a purple RING (the hue carries done-ness, the fill no longer does). Scoped to the Today timeline; widget streak squares and the finished checkmark unchanged.

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Membership is a visible action; menus are destructive-only (#265/#268)** — "Add to my exercises/equipment" renders as a green action row on catalog detail when a built-in isn't in the library (adjacent above the create rows — different intents, and routine use auto-joins anyway); the row disappearing on tap is the confirmation. The … menus keep only Remove/Delete and hide when they'd be empty.

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Today's corners: ++ is the app page, top-right starts workouts (#266/#269)** — The ++ glyph is a circle button pushing AppMenuScreen (Settings — moved from top-right, About with version+build, What's new per-build highlights curated at each TestFlight dispatch, links, feedback); the top-right is a play button opening the start tray (any routine / empty workout / create), retitled "Start a workout". Grammar note, deliberate: the play button is GREEN — starting mints a session, a pending history entry being created (the v3 framing), so it rides the creation grammar.

**2026-07-09 (eve) — One workout, one occurrence; the week ahead scrolls in above Today (#267/#271, Dave's rulings)** — Today opens anchored at today; the next 7 days' scheduled routines render above as FULL cards with Start but visually secondary (condensed, date caption, compact Start, inert grey ring); past the week a cadence summary; overscroll refreshes. Schedule semantics: a genuine EARLY completion banks the next upcoming occurrence (it won't re-appear on its day), but a late make-up discharges ONLY the missed occurrence — never both (Dave rejected two-for-one consumption when review surfaced it). The Kit gained `previousCompleted: Date?` (defaulted; nil callers keep prior behavior) so the banking predicate can tell an early extra session from a make-up; app, widgets (additive snapshot field, old snapshots conservative), and Siri thread the two most recent completions. Captions gain the date when the next occurrence sits beyond the week ("next thu · jul 23").

**2026-07-09 (eve) — TipKit is reserved for the superset introduction; both old tips died (#270, Dave's call after a HIG audit)** — Audit against Apple's offering-help guidance: CatalogCurationTip died without replacement (REMOVE/DELETE labels carry it); PaceAnchorTip became a PERMANENT generic footnote in the Pace editor (the semantics matter at every configuration, not once). Two new one-shot tips (`Tips.MaxDisplayCount(1)`, daily cadence configured): the loop tip (names a rendered superset) and the creation tip (sheet path first, gesture second — HIG prefers describable paths over gesture prose). Every hand-creation path invalidates BOTH tips; a ring eject invalidates the creation tip (mechanic proven). Structural law from review: the tip gate lives on a 1 pt overlay strip — conditional content must never wrap the rail ScrollView (identity churn mid-gesture). 8 catalog templates already contain superset blocks, so the loop appears organically.

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Merge-on-green is a tight poll, not a batched check-in (Dave's ask)** — GitHub webhooks deliver CI failures but never successes, so "ready to merge" is invisible without polling; batching polls into ~30-min check-ins left green PRs sitting (Dave: "how can we make sure you monitor your PRs and merge as soon as they're ready?"). Protocol: while ANY owned PR has pending checks, poll on a ~270 s cycle and merge in the same breath as the green result. Companion trap, repeated twice tonight: pushing or dispatching on a branch CANCELS its in-flight push run via the concurrency group, and the ruleset accepts only push-triggered runs — never push to a branch whose proof run you're waiting on; re-run the cancelled push run rather than dispatching a new one.

**2026-07-09 (eve) — Axiom plugin installed (Dave's ask)** — `axiom@axiom-marketplace` (user scope): Apple-development skills/agents for future sessions; its bundled simulator/profiling tools need macOS and stay inert here. Its UserPromptSubmit hooks keyword-match aggressively (fired on PR-review notifications); treat matches as advisory and skip when no real question of that domain is live. ~~⚠️ User-scope installs do NOT survive remote-session containers~~ **2026-07-10: committed at project scope** (Dave's ask) — `.claude/settings.json` declares the marketplace (`extraKnownMarketplaces`: github `CharlesWiltgen/Axiom`) and enables `axiom@axiom-marketplace`, so every session on this repo (remote containers included) loads it at startup; no per-session reinstall. Unpinned — tracks the marketplace's default branch. First LOCAL session on a new machine may show a one-time plugin trust prompt.

**2026-07-10 — Quiet Arcade: the design refresh is press mechanics + a rebalanced triad (#281/#282/#283, Dave's handoff)** — The 13-screen HTML handoff keeps ink × increment green and adds: (1) **RaisedKey grammar** — every button that commits or navigates is an opaque cap depressing 3 pt (quiet keys 2 pt) onto a FIXED base plate, 0.06 s ease-out (`RaisedKeyStyle`/`QuietKey`/`StartFlashButton`/`BlockBar` in Components/RaisedKey.swift); flat stays flat (chips, toggles, segments, rows) — the state flip is their feedback. Caps must be OPAQUE or the plate shows through. (2) **Selected blue** `#1668D2`/`#5CA8F5`, chroma-matched to accent/done; `Theme.selected` is RETIRED as a text/link color — every escape hatch is a quiet key. (3) **Warm charcoal dark** (`#201F1D` family) instead of near-black; the site mirrors it; the watch keeps system black (OLED convention beats fidelity at wrist size — WatchTheme mirrors the dark tokens instead). (4) **Blocks over bars**: week block bar on Today/Complete (Kit `expectedSessionsPerWeek`, purple = landed), set progress and rest recharge in accent. (5) **One-shot flourishes**: Start flashes accent + "let's go ▸" ~0.85 s (gated off under `--uitest-reset` — it delays the action), Log set pops a rising mono "+1". (6) Rest extension is **+30s everywhere** (in-app + island; `RestAdjustment.addThirty`). Judgment calls: no "Delete all data…" (mock showed one; a wipe doesn't ride a visual refresh); finish screen keeps the honest timeline line over the mock's repo path (#246 stands).

**2026-07-10 — Flexible metrics: a curated vocabulary + per-exercise profiles; intervals fall out of the block model (Dave's ask)** — The metric space grew from weight/reps/duration to a FIXED 14-metric vocabulary (adds distance, pace, speed, incline, resistance, power, cadence, calories, assistance, height, RPE) — each case's semantics (step, wheel, range, format, **improvement direction**: pace and assistance improve DOWN; machine settings are neutral and never diff) live tested in the Kit. Users pick which metrics an exercise tracks (`MetricProfile`); they never invent metrics — that keeps every surface (diffs, watch, interchange, CLI lint) honest about what a number means. Storage is fully additive, ZERO migration: the big three keep their columns (every existing surface untouched); new metrics ride one Kit-coded `[metric: value]` Data bag per row; `Exercise.metricsData == nil` resolves through the seed catalog's per-name profile table (existing stores get rich cardio profiles instantly), then legacy `exerciseType`. `exerciseType` stays stored and consistent (`tracksReps → weightReps`) for old readers. Equipment carries a *suggested* profile (rower → distance/pace/damper); custom gear declares its own via EXERCISE CONFIG chips, which also decides whether weight-step config shows; new custom exercises prefill from their gear and latch on first touch of the TRACKED VALUES chips. **Execution driver**: the highest-priority WORK metric (reps > distance > calories > duration) *with a target* drives the set screen — reps log, duration auto-times, distance/calories show a target card + manual log — so the same rower runs 4×500m in one routine and a 20:00 steady piece in another purely by which target is set. **Intervals are not a new structure**: an interval block = rounds (sets) + a work target + `ExerciseGroup.restSecondsOverride` (amends the "per-workout rest only" decision — intervals are the proof it was deferred against); the existing expansion/auto-timer/rest engine runs the loop, and cardio sets read "ROUND N OF M". Carry-forward generalized to loads + machine settings (re-dial the damper once, remaining rounds follow); work metrics never carry. Catalog: bodyweight movements dropped the dead weight row ([reps]); assisted machines track `assistance` (legacy weight column read as the last-time fallback); carries gained distance; Box Jump gained height; Running/Walking/Cycling joined equipment-free; distance is unit-declared per exercise (m/km/mi — declaration, never conversion; pace references ride it: /500m, /km, /mi). Interchange adds `metrics`/`distanceUnit`/`extraDefaults`/`extraTargets`/`extraActuals`/group `restSeconds`/set `restSecondsOverride` (schema v1, additive; the validator enforces the vocabulary — catching a hand-typed "resistence" is what lint is for). Deliberately NOT shipped (issues filed): AMRAP (#298), EMOM slot semantics (#299), per-set target variation / pyramids (#300 — SetLog's per-set targets mean the session model is already shaped for it), drop sets (#301), count-up stopwatch + derived pace (#302).

**2026-07-10 (morning) — Quiet Arcade round 2: Dave's build-42 walkthrough (#286)** — (1) The "native Liquid Glass toolbar chrome" judgment call was OVERRULED: custom key chrome everywhere — `pushedScreenChrome(title:subtitle:search:onBack:trailing:)` (Components/PushedHeader.swift) hides the system bar and renders a `safeAreaInset` header (raised back key, screen-centered title/mono subtitle, trailing keys, in-header expanding search); GlassBackButton + ExpandingSearchButton died; the #198 full-width swipe-back is unaffected (its pan drives the nav controller, not the bar). (2) Travel is **4 pt standard / 3 pt quiet** (watch 3 pt, site 4px) — a point over the mock, Dave's feel call. (3) Swipe actions are SOLID full-height color blocks (mock 02): DELETE white-on-destructive, DUPE primaryFill/onPrimary. (4) **The +1 beat**: `completeCurrentSet` commits data immediately but the set screen LINGERS ~0.75 s (`lingeringLog`, same view identity so the burst animates; rest countdown anchored at log time; duration sets and `--uitest-reset` skip the beat; the deferred finish checks `session.isDeleted`). (5) Faithfulness sweep: rest keys 1:1.4, amber "needs <gear>" on exercise lists, weight card's green "last N · +Δ" + reps' plain-ink "target X–Y" annotations (the old target/last header line survives only on duration sets), session-record facts as the chrome subtitle.

**2026-07-10 (midday) — A pushed screen that appends to the path must itself be a path entry (#291/#293, Dave's build-44 walkthrough)** — The routine catalog was pushed via `navigationDestination(isPresented:)` while its template taps and blank creation `path.append`ed onto the same stack: SwiftUI treats the path as authoritative, so the appended value REPLACED the boolean-presented catalog (no push transition) and back double-popped past it. The catalog is now a `RoutineCatalogDestination` path marker registered at both stack roots (the #262 root-registration rule composes). The ordering law this generalizes: boolean/item destinations are fine ON TOP of value pushes (nothing appends beneath them — the AppMenu→Settings chain, the equipment catalogs); value appends BENEATH a live boolean destination are the bug. Companion: `path.append` is not idempotent like the old booleans — root-only affordances guard on `path.isEmpty`, the catalog's template rows carry a one-shot flag reset in `onAppear` (the `addTemplateButton` double-fire class). Same round: the ++ key (AppMenuKey) on every root header, and **native toggles stay** — the handoff's Fidelity rule names them platform-native-wins, the press grammar keeps flat controls flat (a toggle is a state flip, not a committing key), and a custom switch costs VoiceOver/Switch Control for zero design gain.

**2026-07-10 (afternoon) — Heart rate rendered everywhere it exists; cardio zone/bpm targets; a three-screen welcome precedes the tabs (#294, Dave's ask)** — The #90 batch already RECORDED heart rate (the wrist's live builder streams it into the saved workout) but displayed nothing and never told the phone. Now: (1) **Watch** — the builder's delegate publishes live/avg/max bpm; the run view shows the live number (accent while inside the step's band, plain otherwise; recovery bpm on the rest screen) and the summary rides home in the result payload (additive WatchSync optionals — payloads without the keys decode both directions, tested). (2) **Phone** — `HeartRateMonitor` (Health/HeartRateService.swift) runs an anchored Health query from session start (a worn watch or paired chest strap feeds it); the session header wears a live "♥ bpm" capsule that renders NOTHING when the newest sample is >3 min old (none beats stale); at finish a statistics query stamps avg/max onto WorkoutSession, and the session record BACKFILLS on open if samples synced late. Displays: Workout Complete line, Today committed-card subtitle ("· 132 bpm"), session record header line. (3) **Targets** — Kit `HeartRateTarget` = zone(1–5) or explicit bpm range, hand-written stable Codable ({"kind":"zone","zone":2}); zones resolve against max HR (Health date of birth → 220−age, fallback 185); the prescription lives on RoutineExercise as a JSON blob (the scheduleData pattern), bumps exercise defaults (#187 law), snapshots onto SetLogs, and ships to the watch RESOLVED to bpm — the wrist never learns max HR. Targets are guidance: no per-set HR actuals, and out-of-band renders plain ink, never a warning (anti-shame). (4) **Welcome flow** — the one deliberate exception to "the timeline IS the onboarding" (#132): three escapable screens (the idea / how it works / the Health ask) overlay the tabs on first launch, once per install — existing installs see it once post-update BY DESIGN; that's where the Health grant lives, and notifications keep their contextual first-rest ask (#246). `--uitest-reset` skips it, `--uitest-welcome` opts the new smoke test in (which asserts tab-bar HITTABILITY for dismissal — the tabs exist under the overlay throughout). Settings gains an APPLE HEALTH connect row (the "not now" recovery path). HR stays OUT of interchange v1 until something consumes it (the scheduleData rule).

**2026-07-10 (evening) — Welcome-flow refinement: the tagline carries the wink (Dave's build-46 walkthrough)** — Three calls on the #294 welcome screens. (1) **Git kitsch toned down** (Dave: "it's cool and valuable but we don't need to harp on it so much"): the tagline ("hackable… incrementing yourself") is the ONE brand wink; the idea screen's "every workout you finish is a commit / progress is the diff" became Dave's positioning line "Privacy-first and customizable to the core. Own your data, and your results.", "Today **stages** what's ready" → "shows", "your schedule is a timeline" → "what's next on top, history below", and the diff row went benefit-first — "See your progress on every set" / "last time's numbers are right there; green means you went up" ("Every set diffs against last time" and "the point is the increment" both read as cringe, Dave's call). (2) **The mechanics rows wear real SF Symbols** (dumbbell.fill / calendar / chart.line.uptrend.xyaxis) — the monospaced text glyphs (+ ▸ Δ) read as noise, the Δ as nothing (Dave: "I don't understand at all"). (3) **The control area reserves the two-key height on every page** (primary cap 50 + 4 travel + 10 gap + quiet cap 44 + 3 travel = 111 pt, top-aligned) so the dots and the primary key sit at identical positions across all three screens instead of jumping up when "Not now" appears on the Health ask. **2026-07-11 — Equipment language is availability, not ownership (equipment-language audit)** — "Owned"/"you own" excluded the many people who train in commercial or hotel gyms without owning the rack. Swept the user-facing copy to "have / have access to" (the Today setup step and the exercise-catalog escape hatch already used it; the routine catalog and pickers still said "own"): the catalog membership facet unified to **LIBRARY** ("In library" / "Not in library") across exercises AND equipment; the escape hatches read "gear you don't have"; the gear-check tray "mark what you have"; the welcome/What's-New lines "equipment you have". DELIBERATELY KEPT: "My equipment" and "YOUR GEAR ✓" (possessive-of-selection, not purchase — a gym member says "my gym"), and the data-ownership brand pillar ("Own your data", "a repo you own") — a different sense of own. Internal symbols renamed where the CONCEPT changed (`showUnowned`→`showUnavailable`, `ownedEquipmentNames`→availability helpers, `missingEquipment(for:available:)`) since they now mean "not in the active library", not "not owned". No-em-dash rule applied to every touched string.

**2026-07-11 — Equipment libraries: gear is per-location, one active at a time, and in the sync contract (equipment-language audit, follow-on)** — Dave trains at home but travels; at hotels he wants a curated bodyweight-or-limited set, not "own everything" or "own nothing". So availability moved from a single `Equipment.inLibrary` flag to membership in a named **`EquipmentLibrary`** (Home, Hotel…), exactly one ACTIVE at a time; every availability read in the app (catalog filters, "needs X" cues, template gear verdicts, the populate offer, Settings summary) resolves through the active one. **Model**: `EquipmentLibrary` (name, order, `uuid`, many-to-many `equipment` with explicit inverse `Equipment.libraries` — the every-relationship-declares-its-inverse law; `uuid` not persistentModelID because that re-keys at first save). Libraries SHARE `Equipment` records, so weight steps and suggested metric profiles travel between locations for free. **Active pointer** is device-local (`@AppStorage`/UserDefaults `activeEquipmentLibraryID`) and deliberately NOT in the interchange — which library is "with you" is a property of the device's whereabouts, and two devices syncing one repo may legitimately differ; a stale/missing pointer falls back to the first library by order (never writes the pointer, so parallel test suites can't fight). **Migration** (`SeedData.ensureEquipmentLibrary`): content-keyed on zero libraries (not UserDefaults), folds the legacy `inLibrary` built-ins + all customs (customs were always available pre-libraries) into a default "Home"; runs AFTER the #232 ownership reset so it snapshots the post-reset flags. `Equipment.inLibrary` is frozen for store compatibility, no live read. **Switcher UX**: a medium-detent **tray** off the Equipment tab header (left of +), showing each library with its gear as chips (ViewThatFits: show-what-fits then "+n") — tapping a row switches and the tab list re-renders behind the tray, which is how the app-wide scope is made legible; rename/delete in a per-row … menu (delete hidden at one library); "New library…" starts EMPTY by design (a curated short list, no copy-all). The routine catalog's GEAR facet names the active library once >1 exists (a lit HOME/HOTEL chip IS the state) with a "Switch library…" menu footer; the template verdict reads "HOME ✓". **Flag-don't-hide** holds (#113): the Routines/Exercises tabs still list everything, but unavailable gear renders in notes amber (routine-card pills, "needs X" subtitles) — your bench-press routine is still yours at the hotel, just marked not-here; only the CATALOGS filter. **New-phone completeness**: added `equipment` (gear records with config) and `equipmentLibraries` to the interchange (both additive/optional, absent = predates them → readers leave state alone; per-file `program/equipment/` and `program/equipment-libraries/`; validator + Kit tests + PLATFORM.md), so a clone-and-import restores WHAT you have and HOW it's configured. Import = replace-or-create by name; unknown gear names become customs; a pre-libraries bundle's created gear joins the active library so old files import with old meaning. The equipment catalog now lists customs too (a custom belongs to specific libraries, so the catalog is where you add one to another). Also fixed `scripts/install-swift.sh` (sourcing /etc/os-release clobbered its `VERSION` var → malformed URL).
**2026-07-11 — Stretches + mobility ride existing primitives, not a new session-phase model (Dave's ask: "finish with stretching, sometimes at the start after a warmup")** — 26 curated stretches join the built-in catalog with ZERO new schema, enum, or migration — the flexible-metrics design (#304) already carried everything they need. A static stretch is a timed HOLD: `ExerciseType.duration` → the `.durationOnly` profile → the set screen runs it as an auto-timer, exactly like Plank/Wall Sit. A dynamic mobility drill (arm circles, leg swings, inchworm) is rep-based: default type → `.repsOnly` (no dead-weight row). Each stretch carries its TARGET muscle group so it lives in the same equipment⇢exercise⇢routine graph and turns up in the library search dock — hip openers (figure-four, pigeon, butterfly) cluster under glutes, neck rides shoulders, forearm/biceps under biceps, mirroring how the catalog already files adduction/neck/grip work (there is no adductor or "mobility" group, and inventing one would fight the muscle graph). All bodyweight, so they reach every install and add no gear (and `everyEquipmentGatesAnExercise` needs nothing new). The user's two stated moments get two ready-made routines under the existing `.recovery` style, single-set-per-block because mobility is a sequence not volume: **Dynamic Warm-Up** (8 drills to open up before lifting) and **Full Body Stretch** ("the way to finish a session", 9 holds head to toe). All content reaches existing stores through the #95 top-up seeder untouched-curation path, catalog-only and un-owned. Rejected as premature abstraction (the workflow doesn't need it — routines already sequence exercises via ordered blocks): a session-PHASE model (warmup/main/cooldown as structure, which would touch the rail UI, execution, watch, and interchange) and a stretch/movement-KIND dimension on Exercise. Per-side holds stay unmodeled (the timer is the whole set; both sides fit inside it). Existing strength templates were left alone — new standalone bookends rather than appended blocks that would shift every estimate and its test.

**2026-07-10 (evening) — Today details round (Dave's build-45 walkthrough): the start tray is a two-stage menu; every workout surface offers a path INTO configuration or repetition** — Five calls from Dave's screenshots. (1) **The start tray never lists routines at top level**: a routine row directly under the tray title read as part of the title, not an option. Stage one offers the WAYS to start — "Choose a routine" (drills into stage two) and "start empty workout" — and stage two is the picker (rows + New routine creation, which moved INTO the picker; the swap footnote renders only when something is scheduled today, since on a rest day there is no swap to explain). Stages slide like a push (0.15 s ease-out, the one motion rule) while the sheet grows its detent (`presentationDetents(_:selection:)` — .height(280) menu ↔ .medium picker); a back key appears in the picker header. (2) **Upcoming (week-ahead) cards navigate**: the whole card is a NavigationLink to routine detail (committed-card grammar — tap the card, chevron trailing) so an upcoming workout is configurable before it starts; the compact Start stays as an inner Button that wins its own frame. Nested-control hit-testing is finger-only territory — on the Mac checklist. (3) **Session records offer "Do it again"**: a StartFlashButton dock on SessionDetailView (the routine-detail Start grammar); the candidate is the session's own routine when alive and non-empty, else a name match — hidden entirely when nothing startable, because a key that no-ops is worse than none. The start state is LOCAL to the record screen (the routine-detail pattern), and that's load-bearing: a first cut routed through TodayView.start(), parking the flash's deferred fire on a surviving screen — a pop mid-flash could drop the cover with `activeSession` stuck non-nil, wedging every future start AND the orphan salvage (swift-reviewer catch). Local state dies with the pop; the started session rides the salvage. Rule to carry forward: **a flash-deferred start's state must live on the screen that flashes.** (4) **The rest-day card carries ONE action**: "Start a workout" (play.fill — the swap-arrows icon was pre-#266 framing; this button STARTS something). The empty-workout quiet key left the card (the tray owns both paths now); the schedule offer sits below the action as the footnote it is. The no-candidates branch keeps direct creation + the quiet empty key — a tray with an empty picker would be a dead end (#208). (5) **The superset tip is inline, not a popover**: the balloon anchored to the rail's top strip read as randomly placed and covered the first rows; a TipView between header and rail displaces content instead. Creation copy names ONE describable path ("Tap an exercise and choose Superset with the one above or below.") — the #270 HIG call taken all the way; the ring gesture stays a discovered mechanic (using it still retires the tip). The #270 identity law is unchanged: the tip gate stays a SIBLING of the rail ScrollView, never a wrapper.

**2026-07-11 — Today layout: the date rides the rail, the estimate leaves the card's top row, the timeline opens harder on today (Dave's ask)** — Three tweaks to the Today surface. (1) **The date left the header**: the header's mono caption dropped "sat, jul 11" and now carries only the setup progress or the week tally (nil → the line hides entirely when there's neither). The date moved onto the timeline as a `todayMarker` — a spine-only divider ("TODAY" section label + "sat · jul 11" in the timeline's own weekday·date grammar, matching the upcoming cards' caption), rendered as the first row below the opening anchor so it sits ON today's item and is exactly what the scroll lands on. Parallel to the "BEYOND THIS WEEK" block by construction: a divider that names a moment, no node. (2) **The estimate left the pending card's top row**: the name now owns that row alongside Configure; "~15 min" pairs with the gear line on the go/no-go meta row (equipment left, estimate right with `layoutPriority(1)` so a long gear list truncates before the time does) — both are "can I do this now?" facts, so they read as one. Options weighed and dropped: folding it into the muscles line (semantically it's not what-it-hits), a dedicated third meta row (too much vertical weight), and a Start-button subtitle (StartFlashButton swaps its label mid-flash — a subtitle fights that). (3) **The opening scroll now seats today at the top even on a short timeline**: the #267 anchor only bites when there's scroll room, so a fresh install (one due card, no history) couldn't push the week ahead off-screen. The below-anchor region gained `.frame(minHeight: viewport.size.height)` fed by a GeometryReader wrapping the ScrollView, so today's region is a screen tall (a `@State` + `onGeometryChange` reports height a beat late, after `onAppear`'s scrollTo has already fired against short content — the GeometryReader binds it in the same layout). Belt-and-braces for the ordering the reviewer flagged: the opening `onAppear` scroll is GATED on `viewport.size.height > 0`, and a one-shot `onChange(of: viewport.size.height)` fires the anchor if the height resolves a beat late — so change #3 can't silently no-op if the min-height grows after appear (`hasAnchoredToday` keeps it one-shot, so a later rotation/keyboard height change never yanks a moved scroll). Taller timelines make the min-height a no-op. Net: you always open on TODAY · today's date, and reaching the week ahead is a deliberate scroll up.

**2026-07-11 — Today pending card: the Configure capsule dies for a trailing chevron; the whole meta region navigates (Dave's ask)** — The pending (today's-workout) card dropped its bordered "Configure" capsule in favor of a plain trailing `chevron.right` in the top row, and the entire region above the Start button became the navigation target — one `NavigationLink(value: routine)` wrapping name+chevron / muscles / gear+estimate / diff, `.contentShape(Rectangle())` so gaps are tappable too. This adopts the committed-card grammar the upcoming cards already speak (tap the card, chevron trailing): the pending card was the last Today surface still gating its detail behind a discrete button. Start keeps its own frame below the link, so exactly one affordance fires per tap (the finger-only Start-vs-navigate contract #306 flagged — verify on device). No zoom conflict: the `Routine.self` destination pushes RoutineDetailView with a plain transition, while the card's `matchedTransitionSource(routine.persistentModelID)` still feeds only the Start→live-workout zoom on the fullScreenCover. The `configureRoutineButton` accessibility id moved onto the NavigationLink (still the "open the routine to configure it" affordance; no test leaned on it).

**2026-07-11 — Closing a workout's recap goes home and converts the card to done (Dave's ask)** — The "Workout Complete" recap's Continue button now posts `.plusplusWorkoutFinished` (object = the session's `PersistentIdentifier`) before dismissing. Two listeners act on it: RootTabView switches to the Today tab, and TodayView pops its NavigationPath to root and plays a staged conversion on the just-finished committed card. The notification (not a direct `dismiss` + local state) is the mechanism because a session cover is presented from THREE screens (Today's pending card, a pushed RoutineDetailView, HistoryView) — routing through a broadcast lands the user on Today and animates the right card regardless of origin, and Today is the initial tab so its `.onReceive` is always live even when another tab presented the cover. The animation reads as a sequence, not a pop: the session commits (endedAt) during the +1 beat while the cover is still up, so the committed card already exists behind it; on close the card's rail node is forced to actionable **green** (the pending color) at a hair-smaller scale, then after a 0.35 s lead (letting the cover finish pulling away) a spring turns the node **purple** (`Theme.committedFill`/done) and pops a one-shot `checkmark.circle.fill` seal over it, then it settles — echoing the recap's own purple checkmark. Green→purple IS the "convert to done" beat (the rail's own grammar: green = actionable now, purple = landed); the checkmark is a momentary stamp, not a resting fill (nodes are stroke-only rings at rest, the build-33 law). `TimelineItem` gained two defaulted params (`strokeOverride`, `showCheckmark`) so the other node states are untouched. **Timing is a deliberate exception to the 0.15 s selection/nav motion law** — a completion flourish (0.35 s lead → 0.4 s spring → 0.8 s hold → 0.2 s settle), the same "completion" beat category as the recap's bouncing checkmark and the finish `.success` haptic; the app's fast-feel rule governs selection/data/navigation, not this. The staged Task guards `justCompletedID == id` after each sleep so a second finish supersedes cleanly. The teleport-to-Today is **unconditional** across all three presenters because the ask is "closing the recap sends you to Today" full stop — finishing from the Routines tab lands you on Today too. ⚠️ Needs Mac validation: the RoutineDetail/History covers dismiss against a tab already switched underneath them (no zoom transition on those two), so check for dismiss jank on real hardware. Smoke test `testExecuteWorkoutAndSeeHistory` — which starts from a routine detail in the Routines tab — now asserts the recap-close lands on **Today** (the Today-only `startTrayButton` appears) instead of manually backing out and hopping tabs: the auto-landing is the new contract.

**2026-07-11 — Today card borders: today = solid green, upcoming = dashed grey; the dash now means "not yet", not "pending" (Dave's ask)** — Two swaps on the Today timeline. The pending (today's-workout) card traded its dashed `borderStrong` stroke for a **solid green** (`Theme.accent`, 1.5 pt) border — the same actionable-green its rail node ring already speaks, so the one card you're meant to DO now reads as such at the card level too. The week-ahead `futureCard` traded its solid thin `border` for a **dashed grey** stroke (`Theme.border`, `dash: [4,3]`). Net effect: the dash inverted meaning on the card border — it used to mark "pending/staged today", now it marks "future/not-yet", while solid-green marks "do this now". This is consistent with, not a contradiction of, the rail-spine grammar (RailGlyph's "dash = pending, only on Today" is about the SPINE glyph, untouched here; the node RINGS — green=actionable, grey=inert, purple=done — are also untouched). Card-border dash and spine dash are different elements; only the former moved.

**2026-07-11 — Recap navigation drops its zoom to match routine-detail's plain push (Dave's ask)** — Tapping a committed card opened the session record with a `.zoom` navigation transition (paired `matchedTransitionSource` on the card + `.navigationTransition(.zoom)` on the `SessionRecordDestination`), while tapping a pending/upcoming card into RoutineDetailView used the standard slide push. Dave noticed the two felt different and preferred the plain push, so the recap's zoom pieces were removed — both navigations now push identically. The `zoomNamespace` stays (it still drives the pending-card→live-workout and activeSession-cover zooms); only the committed→record hop lost its zoom. The completion-conversion node flourish (green→purple on recap-close) is unaffected — it never depended on the navigation transition.

**2026-07-11 — Routine-detail workload facts leave the chrome subtitle for the body header (Dave's cramped-heading ask)** — The pushed routine-detail chrome centered its title with a mono subtitle ("~15 min · 5 exercises · 18 sets") beneath it. Because the chrome carries TWO trailing keys (share + settings), `PushedScreenChrome` pads the centered title 100 pt each side to keep a long name from truncating under a key cap — which left the subtitle column ~190 pt on a standard phone and crushed it to "~15 min · 5 exercise…". Options weighed: (A) move the workload facts to the body header at full width [chosen]; (B) collapse share+settings into one "…" overflow to free chrome width — rejected because share is a primary one-tap affordance (#145) and it only treats the symptom; (C) left-align the chrome title — rejected as a global grammar break across every pushed screen; (D) shorten the subtitle to fit — rejected as papering over the cause. **Chosen (A):** the chrome now carries the title alone (matching RoutineSettingsScreen), and the workload facts became the body header's top line above the existing cadence line (schedule · rest), full-width and truncation-proof. Cost: the facts scroll away with the body instead of pinning — acceptable, they're arrival-glance info and the cadence line already lived there with the same property. Reverses the build-42 "counts live in the chrome (mock 07)" placement, which the cramping had made untenable.

**2026-07-11 — Configure-before-you-do-it + a pause-aware, staged-start workout clock (Dave's ask)** — Four related gaps in the live-session flow closed together. (1) **Configure an exercise before adding it.** Picking an exercise for a session used to drop in three sets with default targets and jump straight to logging — no chance to set the set count or targets. Now a session pick opens an `ExerciseConfigSheet` (set count stepper + per-metric rows, the same grammar as the routine planning sheet `ExerciseDetailSheet.metricsCard`) stacked on the picker; "Add to workout" commits, Cancel adds nothing. Backed by a SwiftUI-free `@Observable SessionExerciseConfig` (sets + a `target/setTarget` bag prefilled from the exercise's defaults, mirroring `RoutineExercise`) so it's unit testable. `ExercisePickerView` gained an `onConfigured:` path (session adds) beside the plain `onSelect:` (routine building configures via its own detail sheet, so it skips the step); `appendExercise` split into a `config:` overload plus the old `sets:` convenience (existing callers/tests untouched, prefill identical → tapping straight through Add reproduces the old three-set block). The in-session `SessionExerciseSheet` (reached from the tray) gained a **Sets** stepper too, via `WorkoutSession.resizePendingBlock` — adds/trims PENDING sets contiguously, never touching completed or the live set (floor = completed + live), shifting later blocks' `order` and re-pinning the cursor. (2) **Pauseable workout.** (3) **Live elapsed in the session tray.** (4) **Ad-hoc timer starts only when the first exercise starts.** All three are one mechanism: the session's elapsed time moved from a single `startedAt` anchor to a **pause-aware clock** — `runStartedAt` (nil until the timer engages), `segmentStartedAt` (nil while paused/staged/finished), `accumulatedSeconds` (banked running time). `elapsed(at:)` sums banked + live segment, excluding staging and paused stretches; `startClock`/`pauseClock` engage/resume and bank; `finish` banks the final segment so `duration` counts active time only. A **routine** session engages the clock at `start(from:)` (you tapped Start); an **ad-hoc** session leaves it disengaged through the empty stage + picker + config sheet and engages it when the first set screen appears (`engageClockIfNeeded` on the logging view's `onAppear`) — so the header reads "ready" and the tray "not started" while you assemble, and the clock begins at the first exercise. A **Pause** key (header, shown only while running under the logging flow — never mid-rest) banks and holds; a full **Paused** screen with Resume replaces the logging/rest flow so no set logs while held. The session tray's elapsed, previously computed once at open and frozen, now ticks in a `TimelineView` and speaks the same "· paused"/"not started" states. Legacy compatibility: `elapsed(at:)` falls back to `endedAt - startedAt` when the clock never engaged, so historical records (and interchange imports, which carry only `startedAt`/`endedAt`) keep their durations; the three clock fields are device/runtime state and deliberately NOT in the interchange (like the active-library pointer). Health's workout window and HR summary anchor on `effectiveStart` (the clock's start, not the session's creation). Rejected as premature: a separate pre-workout staging/build screen (the correction confirmed the tray already covers multi-exercise assembly; config-at-add-time + the staged clock deliver "configure as you go" without it). ⚠️ Needs Mac validation: pause/resume feel and the Paused screen; a duration auto-timer set resets its countdown if paused mid-set (the card tears down); the config sheet stacked on the picker dismissing both cleanly on Add; the clock engaging at exactly the first set screen.

**2026-07-11 — Live mirror foundation: interchangeable phone/watch workouts on a CRDT-lite op log, phone-as-record + mobile custody; whole-session Live Activity; phone rest notifications removed (#322, Dave's ask "do the whole thing")** — The watch and phone were independent workout surfaces (phone pushes the plan; watch ships one finished `SessionResult` back) with no live/in-progress channel. #322 lays the foundation for a workout you can drive from either device and pick up on the other. **Device model (Dave's calls, this thread):** the watch app STAYS a dependent companion (`WKCompanionAppBundleIdentifier`, no `WKRunsIndependentlyOfCompanionApp`), so the iPhone is the durable system of record. Authority is split deliberately — *durable record* = phone (SwiftData), but *custody* (who is authoring / sole-holder right now) is MOBILE: either device can ORIGINATE a session and be its sole author while the other is absent (a run with the phone left behind). Because there is one human, custody is handed off, never split, so a per-field **last-writer-wins** register beats a real CRDT — the one asymmetry (phone wins wall-clock ties) falls straight out of "phone is the record". Full reasoning trail is this session's conversation; the short version lives here. **Core (`PlusPlusKit/LiveSession.swift`, Linux-tested, 13 tests):** an in-progress workout is an append-only log of `Op`s (`started` carrying the plan · `logSet` · `reopen` · `restStarted`/`restEnded` · `cursor` · `finished` · `discarded`), each idempotent by `opId` and stamped `(at, origin, seq)`. The reduced `State` is per-field LWW registers keyed by that stamp (phone > watch on ties) plus a grow-only `applied` set, so `apply(op)` and `merge(state)` are both commutative + idempotent — both devices converge regardless of delivery order, duplicates, or which one was offline (the property the tests pin: order-independence, LWW ties, criss-cross merge, custody handoff, buffered-before-`started`). A shared `sessionId` (minted by whichever device starts, carried in `started`) is the missing identity the old `(name, startedAt±1s)` dedupe never had. **Phone (`PlusPlus/Watch/LiveMirror.swift`):** SwiftData stays the sole record — ops are ONLY the wire format, no parallel reducer. Each mutation emits an op; inbound watch ops project onto SwiftData through a `nonisolated` context-agnostic `project(_:into:)` so the durable transfer path applies them synchronously on the WCSession delegate queue (the A4 "acks on return" rule) while the live path runs on main; a `.started` for an unseen session materializes it IN-PROGRESS so "leave phone behind, come back" resumes rather than imports-as-finished. **Transport:** symmetric both directions — `sendMessage` when reachable, else the durable `transferUserInfo` FIFO queue (never lost, arrives on next contact); the plan's single `applicationContext` slot stays uncontended. **Watch (`WatchLiveSession.swift`):** a reducer-backed working copy that emits wrist ops, folds in phone ops, and **journals the reduced state to `UserDefaults` after every change** — a phone-absent run survives a watch relaunch because the wrist is the only holder until contact. `WorkoutRunView` emits started/log/rest/finish alongside its existing local execution (additive, not a rewrite). **Live Activity (`WorkoutActivityController` + `WorkoutActivityAttributes`, #322):** ONE activity spans the whole session — `.working` (exercise · set N/M · count-up elapsed from `sessionStart`) swapping to `.resting` (countdown to `restEnd` + controls). One activity for the session means rest is an in-place `update`, so the island's own +30s can't tear it down (the pre-#322 rest-only teardown bug). Date-based throughout so the island renders both timers without the app awake; drives from ActiveSessionView's lifecycle. **Notifications:** the phone's `RestNotifier` local notifications (rest + duration-timer) and their permission prompt are DELETED — the rest-over cue is now watch haptics + the Live Activity countdown (Dave: "we shouldn't use notifications for that, just watch haptics"). Interim gap, closed as the mirror completes: a **phone-only** workout (no watch) gets a visible island countdown but no buzz. **Deliberately deferred (this is a foundation, not the finished feature — validate on device, then iterate):** (a) the watch SCREEN live-reflecting phone-authored edits — `WorkoutRunView` still renders from its own `@State`, so phone→watch convergence is in the data/journal but not yet on the wrist UI; (b) both-devices-open JOIN of the same `sessionId` (today two simultaneous opens originate two sessions); (c) jump/redo `cursor`/`reopen` op emission from the phone overview (the reducer supports them; the phone doesn't emit them yet). **Migration:** `WorkoutSession.sessionId: UUID = UUID()` is a lightweight-migration add; existing finished rows take an inert default (history never mirrors). ⚠️ Needs Mac/2-device validation across the board — all of it was written from a remote Linux session (compiles + Kit tests + CI; no device). This is the intended output of the "do the whole thing, I'll tell you if it's broken" mandate: maximal correctness in the Linux-testable core, thin device adapters CI compile-checks.

**2026-07-11 — Three routine-deletion / routine-card bugs (Dave's report)** — (1) **Delete confirm floated anchored to nothing.** RoutineSettingsScreen's delete confirm was a `.confirmationDialog` fired from the "…" header menu; on this pushed screen it adapted to a popover that floated near the tab bar pointing at nothing (same failure class as #204's floating catalog offer). Swapped to a centered `.alert` — same buttons/message, presents predictably centered — matching the custom exercise-delete confirm already in CatalogDetailViews. (2) **Deleting from routine detail stranded you on the deleted routine's detail (and risked a crash).** RoutineSettingsScreen sits ON TOP of RoutineDetailView (pushed via `navigationDestination(isPresented:)`), so a delete has TWO stack levels to unwind. The old `onDelete` set `showingRoutineSettings = false` AND called `dismiss()` in one transaction; the two competing stack mutations raced to a single pop, leaving the detail (now backing a deleted `@Bindable`) on screen. First attempt deferred `dismiss()` + delete across nested `Task { @MainActor }` hops — but a Task hop yields to the next main-actor turn, it does NOT await the ~0.3 s pop animation, so the delete could still fire while the outgoing detail is mounted and re-render `body` against a dead model (`routine.groups`/`.sortedGroups` fault). Final fix follows the standing deleted-model-race law instead of relying on timing: `RoutineDetailView.body` now guards on `routine.isDeleted` (renders `Color.clear` once dead, so `body` never faults regardless of animation), and a `body`-level `onChange(of: routine.isDeleted)` pops the detail off the stack in reaction to the delete. `onDelete` just pops settings + defers the delete one turn (so the settings pop commits first) — the detail's own pop is driven by the deletion, not a second pop racing the settings pop in the same transaction. The guard+onChange live on the `Group` wrapping the branch so they survive the switch to `Color.clear`. Detail is reachable from three parents (list/catalog/Today) with different push mechanisms, so the fix stays internal to `RoutineDetailView` rather than threading a path binding; the onChange auto-pop is also correct universal behavior (a detail whose routine is deleted anywhere should leave). The TodayView caller is unaffected (settings pushes directly from the Today root there — one level, already correct; that root holds no `@Bindable` to the routine). (3) **Routine card truncated its workload facts.** RoutineCard put the name and "~30 min · 5 exercises · 6 sets" on one baseline-aligned row with the facts at `layoutPriority(-1)`, so a long name crushed the facts to "~30 min · 5 e…". Moved the facts to their own full-width line below the name+chevron row (guarded on non-empty so empty routines still claim no workout) — the same fix the routine-detail chrome took in build-48 (2026-07-11 entry above). Card grows from three text lines to four when populated; acceptable for a truncation-proof read. Also renamed the routine catalog's pushed-screen heading from "Catalog" to "Routine catalog", matching its siblings "Exercise catalog"/"Equipment catalog" (LibraryView `CatalogBrowseScreen`). Remote session: no Simulator; relies on CI compile + the reasoning above (navigation UX unverified on device).

**2026-07-11 — GitHub sync adapter + auth + app wiring: the whole remotely-buildable half of #23 (Dave's ask "everything we need to get GitHub sync working")** — The sync ENGINE (`FileLayout`/`SyncPlanner`/`SyncEngine` + the `RepoStore`/`SyncBaseStore` protocols) had shipped months earlier; what remained was the transport, the auth, and the app glue. All of it that doesn't need the (unregistered) GitHub App now exists. **Kit (Linux-tested, 226 total):** an `HTTPClient` protocol boundary (production `URLSessionHTTPClient`, tests inject a scripted fake) chosen over `URLProtocol` stubbing because swift-corelibs-foundation's custom-protocol support is unreliable on Linux — this is what keeps every byte of GitHub logic (paths, headers, SHA concurrency, device-flow polling) covered off-device. `GitHubRepoStore` implements `RepoStore` over the **Git Data API**, not the Contents API: `fetchAll` via one recursive `git/trees` call + a `git/blobs` fetch per file (filtered to the `program/` + `history/` prefixes, so a user's README/CLAUDE.md/skills are never fetched, planned against, or clobbered), and `write` as ONE commit — blobs → tree (layered on the head tree via `base_tree`) → commit → **non-forced ref update**, where the 422 on a non-fast-forward IS the optimistic-concurrency guard (surfaced as `.conflict` for the caller to refetch+replan). Contents-API-per-file was rejected because `SyncEngine` batches a pass into a single commit; git-data is the only way to honor that. `GitHubDeviceFlow` does the "enter this code at github.com/login/device" dance (no client secret, no webview) with the poll loop pure over an injected `sleep` so pending/slow-down/expiry all test without a clock. `GitHubAccount` is the bootstrap trio (whoami / repo-exists / create-private-repo). `InterchangeFiles` reverses `templateFiles` — decoding pulled repo files back into an `ExportBundle` for import — and is Linux-tested too rather than living untested app-side. **App (CI-compiled; no Simulator/Keychain remotely):** `KeychainTokenStore` (token as a generic-password Keychain item, `AfterFirstUnlock` so a background foreground-sync can read it), `ApplicationSupportBaseStore` (the base snapshot as backup-excluded JSON — it's a rebuildable cache), and `GitHubSyncCoordinator` (`@Observable`, a `static let shared` so the connect screen / Settings / app-root all address one instance; durable state lives in Keychain+UserDefaults so a fresh instance agrees anyway). The coordinator runs connect (device flow) → bootstrap (adopt-or-create a private `workouts` repo) → foreground `sync`. **Key sync-design call:** the `local` map passed to `SyncEngine.sync` is templates **plus finished sessions** (built via `templateFiles` + `sessionPlacement`), not templates-only — so a session already on the remote reads as `unchanged` instead of being re-pulled every foreground pass, an offline-finished session gets pushed on the next sync (the "queued offline" behavior for free), and cross-device session pull converges through the same three-way merge. Conflicts default to `.postpone` (never clobber, never auto-pick) — the interactive keep-mine/take-theirs sheet is a deliberate follow-up, as is a commit-per-session `pushSession` at finish time (foreground sync currently folds session pushes into the sync commit). Surfaced by `GitHubConnectScreen` off Settings › SYNC (was a coming-soon alert); app foregrounds trigger a sync (no-op unless connected). **Client ID:** read from Info.plist `GitHubAppClientID` ← `GITHUB_APP_CLIENT_ID` build setting (project.yml), empty until the owner registers the App — the connect screen says "not set up" rather than calling GitHub with a blank id; not a secret (device flow needs none), so it's committed. **Owner-gated remainder** (can't be done from a Linux session): register the GitHub App + drop in the client ID, then a two-device Mac validation pass — full walkthrough in `docs/recipes/github-app-setup.md`. This is the "everything you can without the client ID" half of the mandate: maximal correctness in the Linux-testable Kit, thin app adapters CI compile-checks.

**2026-07-11 — Template sync conflicts auto-merge field-by-field (local-wins), no interactive prompt (Dave's ask "any way we could avoid conflicts?")** — The first sync cut deferred a keep-mine/take-theirs UI and defaulted both-sides-changed template files to `.postpone` (never clobber, but the file just re-surfaces). Dave asked whether conflicts could be avoided outright. **`TemplateMerge` (PlusPlusKit, Linux-tested, 6 tests)** does a field-level three-way merge: it decodes the both-changed file's base/local/remote, and for each field of the inner DTO (a routine's `name`/`restSeconds`/`notes`/`groups`, etc.) applies `SyncPlanner`'s three-way logic ONE level down — a field changed on only one side takes that side, so editing rest on the phone and notes in the repo both apply with no conflict. Only a genuine same-field-both-changed collision needs a tiebreak, and it resolves **local-wins** — consistent with PLATFORM principle 3 (the app's store is live truth) and the #322 live-mirror LWW philosophy ("one human, custody handed off not split"), and non-destructive because git history preserves the overwritten value. **Why local-wins and not real timestamp-LWW:** the interchange format carries no per-field `updatedAt` and must not (it would noise every clean diff — the whole value prop), and the app tracks no local edit times, so there's no wall clock to compare; "local wins" is the honest deterministic rule given "phone is live truth." **Implementation notes:** the merge is generic over JSON (merge the inner object's top-level keys, arrays like `groups` compared as whole values) so all four template kinds (routine/exercise/equipment/library) share one code path with no per-DTO boilerplate; output is canonicalized through `InterchangeCodec` (decode→encode) so bytes match app output and the next sync sees no spurious diff. **SyncEngine integration:** a merged file is pushed (if it differs from remote) AND handed back as a pull (if it differs from local), converging base to the merged bytes; `keep-mine/take-theirs/postpone` survives only as the fallback when a file is undecodable/unknown-shape (the existing conflict tests still exercise it — their non-JSON fixtures can't merge). Net: template conflicts effectively cease to exist, and the interactive resolution sheet never needs building. The array-level coarseness (a `groups[]` edited on both sides takes one whole side, not a per-group merge) is an accepted limit — per-element structural array merge is a future refinement if it ever chafes, which for a single user it won't.
