**2026-07-11 — Sync bootstrap discovers the repo from the App installation, doesn't guess a name (Dave registered plusplus-sync, installed it on `plusplus-data`)** — The first cut hardcoded a repo name (`workouts`) and had bootstrap create-or-adopt it. Two problems surfaced during registration: the App is **Contents-only** (least privilege), which can't create a repo (`POST /user/repos` needs Administration → 403); and forcing a fixed name is a bad constraint (Dave named his `plusplus-data`). Fix: bootstrap calls `GitHubAccount.installedRepositories()` — `GET /user/installations` (the device-flow token is app-scoped, so this lists only THIS App's installations) then `/user/installations/{id}/repositories` — and adopts whichever repo the App is installed on, at its real default branch, preferring a previously-synced one across reconnects. Benefits: any repo name works, and the app can only ever target a repo the App actually has access to (can't 404 against an uninstalled repo). Empty result = "install PlusPlus Sync on a private repo, then reconnect" (the user pre-creates + installs, since Contents-only can't create). `GitHubAccount.createRoutineRepository`/`repository(owner:name:)` stay as tested Kit APIs but are no longer on the app path. Client ID `Iv23liHj9WxBHXjrVYJM` (not a secret) is committed in project.yml's `GITHUB_APP_CLIENT_ID`.

**2026-07-11 — Import validator no longer false-rejects a partial-exercise bundle (Dave's export→uninstall→import round-trip failed)** — Dave exported, reinstalled, and re-imported; import died with "unresolved exercise reference (not in bundle; must exist in the target library)" for every routine exercise. Root cause: `InterchangeValidator` assumed *bundle declares any exercises ⇒ bundle is exhaustive* — if `bundle.exercises` was non-empty, every routine reference had to be among them. But the **export policy** ships only ANNOTATED built-ins + customs; unannotated built-ins a routine references are omitted (they ship with the app). Dave's bundle declared exactly one exercise (`Running`, an annotated built-in) while the routine referenced five unannotated built-ins (Goblet Squat, …) → non-empty exercises → false "unresolved." The pure Kit validator fundamentally can't know the app's built-in library, so guessing from the bundle is unsound. Fix: reference-existence is now **opt-in** — `validate(_:knownExerciseNames:)` checks a reference against `bundle ∪ knownExerciseNames` only when the caller supplies that set; `nil` (default) skips the check. The app importer calls `validate(bundle)` (nil) — it already resolves references against the live seeded store and gracefully SKIPS any that don't (`importBundle` continue-on-unresolved), so blocking the whole import on a reference the validator merely couldn't see was pure false-negative-avoidance gone wrong. The CLI/MCP lint paths also go lenient (they were false-positiving on the same partial repos; a built-in-aware strict lint is a future add). Tests that assert the error now pass `knownExerciseNames: []` (strict), plus a new regression test: a one-exercise bundle whose routine references omitted built-ins validates clean with nil, clean with a knowing library, and flags only under an empty (strict) library. Kit 233 / CLI 26 green on Linux. Unblocks restoring data on a fresh install; unrelated to the GitHub-sync connect bug being chased in the same build.

**2026-07-11 — Retry transient network errors in the GitHub HTTP client (Dave's device: "network error -1005" mid-connect)** — With the diagnostics from the prior entry, the real connect failure named itself: `URLError.networkConnectionLost` (-1005). Classic cause: device flow sends the user to Safari to authorize, and the FIRST request after the app returns from background reuses a keep-alive connection iOS has already torn down → connection lost. Not a real connectivity problem — a stale-socket race. Fix: `RetryingHTTPClient` (PlusPlusKit, Linux-tested, 4 tests) wraps any `HTTPClient` and retries transient failures with a short backoff (0.4/0.8 s) — thrown `URLError`s in the transient set (networkConnectionLost, timedOut, cannotConnect/FindHost, dnsLookupFailed, notConnectedToInternet) and 502/503/504 responses; 4xx and real 500s pass through untouched. The retry gets a fresh connection and the user never sees the spurious error. `GitHubSyncCoordinator`'s default client is now `RetryingHTTPClient(wrapping: URLSessionHTTPClient())`. Pure over an injected `sleep` so the backoff tests without a clock.

**2026-07-11 — Export = your library: exercise `inLibrary` membership travels (Dave: "I had a bunch of exercises but my export only had one")** — Dave accepted the equipment-driven populate offer (`SeedData.populateLibraryFromEquipment` sets `inLibrary = true` on built-ins whose gear you have), adopting a couple dozen exercises into his library — but his export contained exactly one exercise (`Running`, the only one he'd hand-customized). Root cause: the export filter was `!isBuiltIn || notes/videoURL/defaults/metrics` — it exported customs + *edited* built-ins and **ignored `inLibrary` entirely**. So an adopted-but-unedited built-in (the whole populated library) was invisible to export; the manual export/import backup silently dropped the user's curation, and equipment library membership traveled while exercise membership didn't. Decided per #328 (the ownership thesis: the repo should be self-contained for what's *yours*, and `inLibrary` is exactly "yours"). Fix: export predicate gains `|| inLibrary` (customs + in-library + edited built-ins); a new additive `ExerciseDTO.inLibrary: Bool?` carries membership, **written only when `false`** (the exception: an exported exercise NOT in the library, e.g. a removed custom) so the common in-library case stays byte-clean and every pre-`inLibrary` file (absent) reads as in-library; import restores `exercise.inLibrary = dto.inLibrary ?? true`. Un-adopted catalog built-ins still stay out (they ship with the app and resolve on import) — the boundary is "did you adopt it," which is the same signal the app already draws. Needed the explicit DTO field (not a "present ⇒ inLibrary" shortcut) because a routine can reference a non-library exercise (adding an exercise to a routine doesn't adopt it), and customs must export unconditionally (no catalog fallback). Kit 238 / CLI 26 green; app round-trip test added (adopted built-in exports + restores, catalog-only does not). Closes #328.

**2026-07-11 — Sync connect diagnostics + in-app install step (Dave's on-device report: "GitHub said connected, PlusPlus said something went wrong")** — First real device run: device flow authorized on GitHub ("you're all set"), but the app showed the generic "Something went wrong. Try again." — which is `describe`'s catch-all, meaning the thrown error wasn't one we message specifically (so NOT the empty-installations case, which has its own copy). The friendly-copy layer was hiding the actual cause (Keychain write? a non-2xx on `/user/installations`? a `URLError`?), un-diagnosable without device logs. Fix (no behavior change, just visibility): `connect()`/`sync()` catches now `Logger.error(String(reflecting:))` the real error, and `describe` surfaces concrete detail instead of a blanket string — HTTP status for `AccountError.http`/`StoreError.http`, `URLError` code, `KeychainError` OSStatus, and a last-resort `"Couldn't connect: \(error)"`. So the next run names the culprit. Also closed the UX gap Dave flagged ("is installing the App required? how would they know?"): yes, required (sync targets whichever repo the App is installed on), but it was only implied by copy. Added an explicit **"Install on GitHub"** button (`GitHubSyncSettings.installURL` → the App's `installations/new` repo-picker) as **Step 1** on the connect screen, with **Connect GitHub** relabeled **Step 2** — installation is now a visible step, not a hidden prerequisite. Follow-up to the merged #326; needs another device build to read the surfaced error.

**2026-07-11 — "Beyond this week" reads as a recurring rhythm, not a duplicate day (Dave's report)** — The Today timeline's `beyondThisWeekBlock` cadence summary rendered each scheduled routine as `shortLabel · name` ("sat · Dumbbell Full Body"). Sitting directly beside the concrete dated `futureCard` for that same routine ("Dumbbell Full Body / sat · jul 18"), it read as the exact same data stacked twice — the summary's *terse day token* is indistinguishable from a single occurrence. Fix: a new `RoutineSchedule.recurrenceLabel` (Kit, pure, 1 test covering all modes) phrases the **ongoing pattern** distinctly from one occurrence, and the block uses it instead of `shortLabel`. Fixed weekdays lead with "every" so the recurrence is explicit — "every sat", "every mon/thu" (mirrors Dave's own "it's every Saturday"); a rolling frequency reads as a rate that never names a weekday — "weekly", "daily", "3×/wk", "2×/day", "every 2d", falling back to "N×/Md". That rate-vs-weekday split is itself the cue that tells the two scheduling styles apart at a glance, which was Dave's second ask (specific days vs a looser cadence). `recurrenceLabel` is deliberately separate from `shortLabel` — the latter stays the terse chip/pill token used on cards, detail headers, widgets, and the week block. Also swapped the block's em-dash separator for "·" (the no-em-dash copy rule, 2026-07-10) and refreshed the doc comment's stale example. Remote session: Kit suite green locally (203 tests); the TodayView copy swap is CI-compile-verified, layout unverified on device (single faint mono caption line, `lineLimit(1)`, unchanged).

**2026-07-11 — Interchange completeness audit: five content fields that silently dropped on export/restore, plus a mechanism so it can't recur (Dave: "make sure all data that should be in an export will be … and figure out how to avoid new stuff getting missed")** — Following the `inLibrary` miss (#328), a full sweep of the SwiftData models against the mapping found more fields that never reached a DTO, so a new-phone GitHub-sync restore lost them: (1) **routine `schedule`** — the whole recurrence (weekdays / frequency) was absent, so a restored routine came back unscheduled; (2) **heart-rate targets** at all three layers — `Exercise.defaultHeartRateTargetData`, `RoutineExercise.heartRateTargetData`, `SetLog.targetHeartRateData` — the entire cardio-prescription feature round-tripped to nothing; (3) **session heart-rate summary** — `averageHeartRate` / `maxHeartRate`; (4) **per-set metric-profile snapshot** — `SetLog.metricsData`, so a restored history set derived its profile from `exerciseType` and could mis-render a flexible-metrics set; (5) **session active duration** — `WorkoutSession.accumulatedSeconds` (running-clock time, excluding pauses/staging), so a restored session's `duration` fell back to the wall-clock span. All five are now mapped via new additive-optional DTO fields (`RoutineDTO.schedule`, `ExerciseDTO.defaultHeartRateTarget`, `EntryDTO.heartRateTarget`, `SessionDTO.{activeSeconds,averageHeartRate,maxHeartRate}`, `SetDTO.{targetHeartRate,metrics}`), each **omitted when it carries no signal** so pre-existing files stay byte-identical and older readers keep working. The HR blobs have no model accessor on `Exercise`/`SetLog`, so the mapping decodes/encodes their stored `HeartRateTarget` JSON directly (`decodeHeartRate`/`encodeHeartRate`). **The mechanism** (Dave's second ask): a single authoritative `INTERCHANGE FIELD CENSUS` doc-comment atop `InterchangeMapping.swift` gives every stored property of every synced model exactly one disposition — EXPORTED or EXCLUDED-with-reason (device state like `sessionId`, the live clock's `runStartedAt`/`segmentStartedAt`/`cursorOrder`, `order`/`createdAt` ordering metadata, the dead legacy `Equipment.inLibrary`); a new completeness test `fullGraphRoundTripPreservesEveryContentField` populates every exported field with a distinctive value and asserts it survives export → encode → decode → import into a fresh store, so an unmapped future field fails loudly instead of vanishing; and the `docs-drift` hook now fires on `PlusPlus/Models/` edits with the "map it, assert it, or mark it EXCLUDED" reminder. **Schema-change policy** (Dave's third ask), now written into docs/PLATFORM.md § "Schema evolution": additive optional fields never bump `schemaVersion` (absent must decode to the pre-field default, writer omits in the default case → two-way compatible + deterministic); only breaking changes (remove/rename/retype a field, make one required, change a default's meaning) bump it, and the codec already rejects any document above the version it understands (`unsupportedSchemaVersion`, covered by the future-version fixture). Kit 239 / CLI 26 green on Linux; the app-side completeness + membership tests verify in macOS CI (SwiftData is Apple-only). PLATFORM.md's example bundle gained representative `schedule` / heart-rate / session-summary values.

**2026-07-12 — First sync is a RESTORE, not a merge (Dave: reinstall wiped my equipment library)** — Dave synced a populated library to the repo, deleted the app, reinstalled, reconnected, and synced — and the sync EMPTIED his "Home" library on the repo (10 gear → `[]`). Root cause: a fresh install has no sync base (Application Support was wiped with the app), so the first pass ran the normal three-way merge. The fresh seed's local `home.json` (an empty "Home" library, #185) collided with the repo's populated one; with no base entry, `TemplateMerge.mergedFields` couldn't tell the seed's empty `equipment` array from a deliberate edit and hit "both changed → local wins" — the empty array won and overwrote the repo (SyncEngine conflict → TemplateMerge, local-wins per the #322 last-writer philosophy). The merge's own premise (git history preserves the overwritten value) meant Dave's data was recoverable from the prior commit, but the app had destroyed the backup it was supposed to restore FROM. Fix: `SyncEngine.sync` now detects `base.isEmpty && !remote.isEmpty` (first sync on this install against a populated repo) and takes a `restore` path instead of a merge — adopt every remote file (returned as pulls the app imports), push only local files the repo doesn't have (real work made before connecting; a fresh reinstall has none), and never overwrite a remote file. Once the base is saved the next pass is a normal merge. This makes the primary use case (new-phone / reinstall restore) safe by construction: a fresh install cannot wipe the repo it's restoring from. The alternative (local-wins on a base-absent collision) is only ever right when local is real user data, which a fresh seed is not. Kit 240 green on Linux (new test: first sync into a populated repo restores it, pushes only local-only files, commits nothing over the library). docs/PLATFORM.md sync-semantics updated. Recovery for Dave: the 10 gear are in the commit before the wiping sync.

**2026-07-12 — Calendar sync: scheduled workouts on the user's own calendar, one tap to start (#333, Dave: "a workout is more likely to get done if it shows up at a specific time on the user's own calendar")** — Opt-in feature that writes each fixed-weekday routine into the user's calendar as a recurring event whose URL deep-links back to start that exact workout. **Apple + Google through one path, no dependency:** iOS has no "sync to Google Calendar" client API, but EventKit writes to the device calendar database, and any account the user added in iOS Settings (iCloud, Google, Exchange) surfaces there as a writable source — so a Google-primary user is covered by the same code, and we never run a server, hold an OAuth token, or add a third-party package (matches the share-link "nothing leaves the device" philosophy). **A dedicated "++ Workouts" calendar** (created in the user's default source so it still syncs up to their account) is the load-bearing choice: removal is one `removeCalendar` that takes every event with it, the reconcile only ever reads/writes inside our own calendar so it can never disturb the user's real events, and the user gets a native off-switch (hide/delete it in their calendar app). **One idempotent `reconcile`, not per-edit hooks** — this repo's rules file is full of missed-mutation-path bugs, so we don't chase individual edits: `reconcile` computes the desired event set from `WorkoutCalendarPlan` and diffs it against a device-local `routineName → {eventIdentifier, fingerprint}` map, so routine-deleted / rescheduled / retimed / unscheduled / switched-to-frequency / feature-toggled-off all fall out of the same add-update-remove diff, and running it on **every foreground and background** (background so a just-made schedule edit is present before the user switches to their calendar app; foreground so external changes and any missed edit self-heal) means no orphans. **Full calendar access, not write-only** — write-only (the minimal iOS 17 prompt) can only *create* events; updating and removing them, which managed sync requires, needs `requestFullAccessToEvents`. That's an Info.plist usage string only (`NSCalendarsFullAccessUsageDescription`) — **no entitlement, no App ID / portal change**, so shipping is unchanged. **The deep link reuses everything that already exists:** identity is the routine name (#32, same as Siri), so `plusplus://start/<name>` and `https://plusplus.fit/start/<name>` route through the existing `.plusplusStartRoutine` → `TodayView.start(routine)` pathway; associated domains (`applinks:plusplus.fit`) were already live so only the site AASA gains a `/start/*` component + a not-installed fallback page. **v1 scope:** fixed-weekday schedules only (frequency "3×/7d" floats against the last completion and has no fixed recurrence rule — deferred to a rolling-horizon follow-up; it's simply absent from the desired set, so switching a routine to frequency removes its event); global time-of-day (default 07:00, per-routine deferred); duration = the routine's own estimate floored to 30 min; neutral titles ("++ Push Day") and no alarms (a block the user opted into is not a nag — the no-obligation/anti-shame law). Pure logic (`WorkoutCalendarLink` build/parse, `WorkoutCalendarPlan` eligibility + fingerprint) lives in Kit with 11 Linux tests; the EventKit glue (`CalendarSyncCoordinator`) + device-local state (`CalendarSyncSettings`) + Settings UI are app-side. Known follow-ups: frequency-mode sync, per-routine time-of-day, an `.ics` fallback for Google-only-in-the-Google-app users, and that iOS doesn't auto-delete the calendar on uninstall (clearly named so the user can remove it; noted in the settings caption). Kit green on Linux; app targets verify in macOS CI (EventKit is Apple-only).

**2026-07-12 — Superset creation gets a landing moment, and the resting loop earns a (quiet) color (Dave: "hard to feel the connection between the selection rectangle and the little path it leaves; give the loop some color")** — Two linked gaps in the ring-drag superset flow. (1) **No handoff on release.** During the drag the rail shows a full-width vivid-blue selection field (ringHighlight, `Theme.selected`); on release `commitRing` mutates the model and the field just vanishes as the `RailGlyph` loop appears — nothing tied the two, so the loop read as unrelated chrome. (2) **The resting loop was colorless.** v4 §1a drew it in `Theme.border` ("collapsed it's just an order map"), which is why it didn't register as the residue of that blue selection. Fix, three parts on the same landing (gated on `commitRing`'s existing "membership grew" branch, `span.absorbAfter/absorbBefore > 0`, so ejects/reorders are unaffected): **(a) a resting color** — new `Theme.supersetLoop = selected.opacity(0.5)`, the selection hue dialed down; the loop + chevrons now carry it while the spine + node dots stay neutral (`border`/`borderStrong`) — the grouping mark is blue, the order map isn't. Amends the "exactly one blue at rest" law to "one *vivid* blue". **(b) a collapse** — `supersetLandingOverlay` fades the selection field and shrinks it left into the rail column (`scaleEffect(x:anchor:.leading)` over 0.42 s) so the "big" visibly drains into the "little". **(c) a bloom** — `RailGlyph.flash` (1→0 over the same 0.42 s) mixes the loop ink from `supersetLoop` up to full `selected` and back, so the loop ignites in the field's own colour as the field lands on it, plus a single `.impact(weight: .medium)` snap (distinct from the light per-slot drag ticks; `.success` stays reserved for the purple finish). **On matchedGeometryEffect** (Dave asked): rejected deliberately — the "little one" is a `Canvas`-drawn path with no matchable frame, and the morph fires mid-relayout (the commit mutates the model, re-laying the whole rail), where matched geometry across a conditional removal inside a ScrollView drops frames; a self-owned scaleEffect+flash driven by one `progress` value gives the same big→little read deterministically, which matters because it can't be seen in a remote (Linux) session. Colour choice (muted blue over purple/neutral) went with the selection hue because it maximally connects the two elements and a routine rail is a *plan*, not history — purple ("done") would misread there. Landing keyed by the surviving group's `persistentModelID` so it survives the commit's reindex. App-target change: no Kit/CLI tests; feel + exact collapse landing point need on-device validation (CI compile-verifies; the Simulator is unavailable remotely).

**2026-07-12 — Empty-workout key: "build as you go" + a `plus.square.dashed` glyph (Dave: "sounds kinda sad as is")** — The no-plan start affordance (#239) read "start empty workout" as a bare monospaced quiet key. "Empty" undersold the feature — the path is walk in, log, and keep the result as a routine at the finish if it earned it — so the copy is now **"build as you go"** (action-forward, names what actually happens; no obligation vocab). It also gained a leading SF Symbol, `plus.square.dashed` (a blank canvas you add to), differentiating it from its sibling "Choose a routine" (the Routines-tab `square.stack`). `QuietKey` gained an optional `systemImage` that rides at the leading edge in the same quiet ink (`textSecondary`) — icon stays monochrome, not green, so the key keeps the quiet grammar rather than borrowing the creation hue. Both instances updated: the rest-day card's escape hatch (via `QuietKey`, shown only when no startable routine exists) and the swap-in tray's "two ways to start" menu (a hand-rolled quiet button, icon added inline). Accessibility identifiers unchanged (`startEmptyWorkoutButton` / `swapInStartEmpty`) so the UI smoke flows still key off them. Copy/layout only; CI-compile-verified, on-device layout unverified (remote session).

**2026-07-12 — Motion tempo becomes `Theme.Anim` tokens; selection slides on a snappy spring, not a decelerating ease-out (Dave: "changing the selected segmented control item feels sluggish/muddy")** — The "one motion rule" (0.15 s ease-out, #176/#216) lived only as prose in app-surfaces.md while `.easeOut(duration: 0.15)` was copy-pasted ~30 times across the app, with no shared constant. Two problems, one fix. (1) **The muddy feel.** `SegmentedTabs`' pill slides between segments via `matchedGeometryEffect`; under `.easeOut(0.15)` the pill leaps then *crawls* the final stretch into place — ease-**out** decelerates to zero velocity, and that asymptotic tail on a large sliding object is exactly what reads as sluggish. Springs front-load velocity (immediate response to the tap) and settle organically, which is why iOS's own selection UI uses them. (2) **No single dial.** A tempo change meant editing every call site. Fix: a `Theme.Anim` token enum — `selection` = `.snappy(duration: 0.25, extraBounce: 0)` (a spring, **no** overshoot: a bouncing segmented pill reads toy-like and could visually clip the padded track), `standard` = `.easeOut(duration: 0.15)` (unchanged — data rolls, opacity, search expansion), `press` = `.easeOut(duration: 0.06)` (RaisedKey). Every inline `.easeOut(0.15)`/`0.06` now references a token (the "draw from Theme, never ad-hoc literals" law extended from colour to motion); the `standard`/`press` migrations are behaviour-preserving, so the **only** felt change is selection. Routed to `selection`: the segmented pill, the selected metric/muscle/HR-target/equipment chips, filter-facet chips, and the schedule day circles (each already paired with `.sensoryFeedback(.selection)` — that pairing was the classifier). Left literal deliberately: the flourish exceptions that were never part of the fast-feel rule (splash 0.35 s fade, superset landing bloom 0.42 s, the green→purple completion beat's `spring`/0.2 s, paging 0.2 s, drag 0.16 s, swipe reveal 0.18 s, the rest-timer pause `.default`). Amends app-surfaces.md's motion line. Nominal spring duration (0.25 s) is *longer* than the old 0.15 s but perceptually snappier — the pill reaches ~90 % in ~0.15 s with no dead crawl; the well-known "springs feel faster than their duration" effect. ⚠️ App-target UI change, feel is subjective and the Simulator is unavailable remotely: CI compile-verifies, but the exact spring value wants Dave's on-device eyeball — it's a one-line retune in `Theme.Anim.selection` if 0.25 s / zero-bounce isn't quite right.

**2026-07-12 — Superset landing v2: opaque gray rest + the four-phase Snap (Dave's design handoff, "not quite right")** — Dave shipped a high-fidelity HTML/Canvas prototype revising the #334 landing, fixing two things. (1) **The resting loop had a color-variation artifact.** `supersetLoop = selected.opacity(0.5)` is a SEMI-TRANSPARENT stroke, so wherever the `RailGlyph` Canvas sub-paths overlap (the quarter-curve/line joins under round caps, each chevron drawn over the line) the alpha COMPOUNDED (~0.5 → ~0.7) and those spots read darker. Fix: stroke the settled loop in an **opaque** color (`Theme.supersetLoop = #7C786F`, a warm gray) — opaque ink doesn't composite with itself, so overlaps are uniform regardless of draw order. This also **reverses the #334 color decision**: blue is now the MOMENT OF CREATING (selection field + snap line + spark); gray is the bound unit AT REST (a step more prominent than the neutral spine, quieter than any blue). (2) **The create→static handoff was two disjoint eased overlays** (a scaleEffect-collapsing field + a separately-blooming loop) that didn't read as one motion — replaced by a single continuous sequence off ONE linear clock (`supersetLanding.progress` 0→1 over 1.30 s, `.linear` so the per-phase easings live in the views), four phases: **A Reshape** (260 ms, ease-out) the selection field's top/bottom/left edges + left corners settle onto the loop-to-be, right edge HELD at full width; **B Snap** (320 ms, `1-(1-p)^2.2`) the right edge sweeps left in its one and only move, deflating into the loop line (no mid-way seam — that was the old two-motion problem), fill fading, right corners 12→4; **C Pulse** (420 ms) a soft additive `plusLighter` spark travels bottom→top along the ACTUAL loop path (curved into both end nodes via `pulsePoint`), revealing + briefly flaring each chevron as it passes; **D Fade** (300 ms) only after the spark lands, the whole loop crossfades blue→gray. Ungroup stays instant. **SwiftUI mechanics:** the field is an `UnevenRoundedRectangle` (per-corner radii) in an `Animatable` view; the spark is a `Canvas` radial gradient in an `Animatable` view; the loop line + chevron reveal + blue→gray fade live per-row in `RailGlyph` (already `Animatable`). All read the same `progress` @State, so one `withAnimation(.linear)` drives every piece in lockstep (each `Animatable` view interpolates its own `animatableData` off the shared clock — no `TimelineView`/`Date`). Timing constants + `pulsePoint` centralized in `SupersetRailGeometry`. The medium-impact "snap" haptic moved from t=0 to the B→C hand-off (~580 ms, the deflate) via a delayed `Task`, guarded by a `landingSeq` token so a superseded run's clock/completion/haptic all bow out. `RailGlyph.flash` (the #334 channel) is gone; the FX overlay replaces `supersetLandingOverlay`. **matchedGeometryEffect** stays rejected for the same reasons as #334 (the loop is a Canvas path with no matchable frame; the morph fires mid-relayout). Deliberate deviation from the handoff, flagged for Dave: the field renders as an OVERLAY (above row text) matching the existing `ringHighlight`, not slotted behind the text per the handoff's isolate-layer note — doing the latter needs a `RailGlyph`↔text z-split that the shipping live-drag highlight doesn't do either; low visual risk (the tint is faint, the motion brief). App-target change, no Kit/CLI tests; the whole animation (feel, exact pixel landing of the field edges/spark) needs on-device validation — CI only compile-verifies and the Simulator is unavailable in a remote session.

**2026-07-15 — Operator (on-device AI agent) PR 1 of 3: the change vocabulary + deterministic engine, no UI, no model yet (Dave's feature: an agent chat on the reveal surface that can answer questions about your data and do library work for you, including bulk edits like "make all stretches duration-based")** — Operator will be a chat agent powered EXCLUSIVELY by the iOS 26 Foundation Models framework (~3B on-device model, 4,096-token context, zero server), opening from a hero card on the reveal surface into a tray (Dave, plan review: the keyboard can't fit the drawer's sub-surface layout, and sheets get keyboard avoidance + full width free; an in-place takeover was designed and rejected). Design decisions settled with Dave up front: tiered safety (small reversible edits apply immediately with an inline Undo; bulk/destructive changes stage a preview card and touch NOTHING until Apply); v1 scope = read-only data Q&A + library writes/bulk edits + outcome navigation (the engine steers the main surface to what it touched; no general "go to X" commands, no history edits); one rolling persisted thread with honestly-explained limited scroll-back; entry always visible with per-reason unavailability explainers; dry pithy terminal persona in sentence case; grounded-only knowledge (answers from the user's data + catalog, deflects open-ended fitness advice — a 3B model hallucinates confidently); contextual suggestion chips picked deterministically from app state. **The governing law (from #165's framing): the model proposes, the app disposes.** The model only ever fills a structured `ChangeSpec` via @Generable constrained decoding; everything that touches data is deterministic app code. **This PR ships the deterministic half.** Kit (Linux-tested): `ChangeSpec`/`ChangeFilter`/`ChangeValues`/`TrackMode` (one flat vocabulary covering create/update/delete across routine/exercise/superset/library, with filter+transform bulk selection), model-leniency normalization (create-superset reads as the update that forms one; a create's name in `targets` is adopted), terse model-readable validation issues, weekday-name parsing (hand-mapped, no locale), `ChangeTierPolicy` (delete of a persistent entity ALWAYS previews; >3 affected previews; a tracking conversion auto-applies only for one entry-free exercise; a superset "delete" is dissolution — structural, so it rides the count rules), `ChangePreviewSummary` formatting, and `OperatorThreadPolicy` (store cap 120 / visible cap 60 / recycle at 70% of contextSize / ~3 chars-per-token estimation). The @Generable mirror (`ChangeArgs`) deliberately CANNOT live in Kit — the FoundationModels macro doesn't build on Linux — so PR 2 adds a thin app-side mirror + one mapping function, and the entire engine stays Linux-testable. App side: `ChangeEngine` (validate → resolve → tier → stage/apply; case-insensitive exact-then-unique-substring name matching with AMBIGUOUS/Closest digests instead of guesses; previews carry the SPEC and re-resolve at Apply-tap time so nothing stale-pointer-mutates; all-or-nothing applies via `context.rollback()` on any mid-apply error; synchronous save; a post-apply hook seam for the widget-snapshot/watch-push/calendar-reconcile trio so tests observe invocations without singletons), `OperatorDataService` (find_items/get_stats digests, one entity per line — digest text re-enters the 4k window so every line earns its tokens; streak counts consecutive weeks and an empty CURRENT week holds rather than breaks, anti-shame), and `OperatorDestination` (+ a `.plusplusOperatorShow` notification for PR 3's outcome navigation). **Undo is depth-1 and in-memory by design** (persisting inverses across launches invites stale-ref corruption): creates invert by deleting (IDs captured AFTER the save — a pre-save `persistentModelID` is the temporary one and dies at the swap); field updates invert from before-image snapshots; structural routine edits snapshot the whole group tree as a `RoutineDTO` and rebuild INTO THE SAME `Routine` model so its `uuid` (presentation identity) survives (group/entry uuids DO re-key — accepted, only the routine's identity is promised); deletes invert by recreating from interchange DTOs PLUS the device-local identity the DTO census-excludes (routine `uuid` + `createdAt` so nav and the #354 due-ness anchor survive; a library's `uuid` + active-pointer state — deleting the active library re-points the pointer like the tray does, and its undo points it back). A recreate skipped because a same-name item now exists is NAMED in the receipt ("Undone, except …"), never papered over. **One deliberate deviation from UI semantics:** the UI's custom-exercise delete is a bare `modelContext.delete` that leaves ghost entries (`entry.exercise == nil`) in routines; the engine removes those entries too (previewed, structure-snapshotted for undo) — bulk deletes would otherwise strew ghosts. Built-in "deletes" set `inLibrary = false` (the catalog keeps them), mirroring the UI's remove-from-library. Digest/preview vocabulary reuses the app's existing dialects rather than inventing new ones: schedules render through `RoutineSchedule.shortLabel` (the one chip/pill vocabulary) and the streak stat feeds end-date-bucketed weekly counts into `WidgetSnapshot.streak(fromWeeklyCounts:)` (THE shared streak rule), so Operator's numbers and words always match the widget and every card. Tests: 29 new Kit tests (validation matrix incl. filter-applicability — an inapplicable filter criterion is rejected, never silently widened to select everything; tier table; formatting; thread policy) + 27 app tests against throwaway on-disk containers, 19 engine + 8 data service (every apply class round-tripped through undo, the stretch bulk end-to-end with entry cascade, tier gating proving a staged delete touches nothing, ambiguity/closest digests including superset members, the last-library guard, uuid/createdAt identity restore on delete-undo, the honest partial undo). PR 2 = model boundary + tools + controller + tray UI + reveal-surface hero; PR 3 = outcome navigation + polish. Kit suite green locally (299); app tests verify in macOS CI.

**2026-07-15 — Operator PR 3 of 3: outcome navigation (engine-driven, model-blind) + polish** — Dave's amendment made concrete: when an applied change touches an entity, the MAIN surface steers to it BEHIND the still-open drawer, so closing the drawer (or the receipt's now-live View key, which re-posts and closes tray + drawer) lands on the result. The mechanism is the `.plusplusStartRoutine` pattern: `postReceipt` posts `.plusplusOperatorShow` with the change's first `OperatorDestination`; RootTabView switches tabs; RoutineListView resolves `.routine(uuid)` with a path reset + `RoutineRef` push (registered at the stack root, the #262/#291 laws — and uuid-keyed, so a just-created routine resolves with no query lag). Exercises/equipment stay tab-level in v1 (no uuid nav pathway exists for them; extending ModelRefs is a separate decision). The model has NO navigation primitives — navigation is a deterministic post-apply effect, exactly like the widget/watch/calendar hooks. Polish: decorative status dots hidden from VoiceOver; a controller test asserts the destination post. ⚠️ The receipt-View → tray-dismiss → drawer-close → pushed-detail chain is squarely in the silent-dead-tap class (build 76): it MUST get an on-device tap in the validation pass.

**2026-07-15 — Operator PR 2 of 3: the Foundation Models boundary, the four tools, the chat tray, and the reveal-surface hero (outcome navigation landed in PR 3)** — The user-facing half of Operator, on the PR 1 engine. **The model boundary is a protocol** (`OperatorModel`: isResponding/contextSize/prewarm/send-as-cumulative-text-stream/recycle) with `FoundationOperatorModel` as the only type in the app touching a real `LanguageModelSession` — Foundation Models does not exist on Linux CI and is unavailable on CI simulators, so every controller behavior (turn serialization, streaming assembly, error→copy mapping, context recycling, card flows) is proven against a `ScriptedOperatorModel` in tests, plus an `availabilityProvider` seam because CI simulators always read unavailable. **26-cycle API surface deliberately** (CI pins Xcode 26): errors are `LanguageModelSession.GenerationError` (the one-enum spelling; the 27 split migrates when the floor rises), tools return their `Output` directly (no ToolOutput wrapper), sessions rebuild via plain `init(tools:instructions:)`. **Session recycling carries context in the PROMPT channel, not synthetic transcript entries and not instructions**: entry construction is under-documented on the 26 SDK, and the carryover contains user-derived names (routine names, topics) which the injection rule keeps out of instructions — so a recycle rebuilds a fresh session and the controller prepends one bracketed `[earlier: …]` line (deterministic, app-built: last 3 receipt summaries + last topic, ~60 tokens, no model summarization call) to the next prompt. Proactive recycle at 70% of `contextSize` (chars/3 estimate, `OperatorThreadPolicy`); reactive on `exceededContextWindowSize` with ONE retry. The visible thread is untouched by recycling — store and session are independent by design. **The four tools are `@MainActor final class`es** (their work IS ModelContext work; an actor-isolated async method satisfies the protocol's async `call`, and the immutable `name`/`description` lets stay nonisolated-readable): find_items/get_stats (terse digests from the PR 1 data service — digest text re-enters the window), propose_change (the `@Generable ChangeArgs` mirror → `toSpec()` → engine; the return string only steers narration, the cards are the record; wrong string fields come back as INVALID digests the model can self-correct from), and ask_user (NON-blocking: the options card renders, the turn ends, the tap arrives as the next user message — a held tool continuation would wedge `isResponding` across a dismissed tray or killed app). **Surface**: the reveal surface's hero slot is now the Operator card (availability dot + status word: ready shows no word, off/downloading/unavailable explain in-tray with a Settings deep-link for the opt-in case; sub-line = last reply snippet else the tagline); the ACTIVE LIBRARY card demoted to a `statusRow` under a LIBRARY header (its Switch button died — switching lives in the tray it opens); Operator opens as a `.large` tray through the surface's existing sheet mechanism (Dave, plan review: the keyboard can't fit the drawer sub-surface; sheets bring native keyboard avoidance and full width). The controller is created LAZILY (first drawer open or hero tap, never at app init) and prewarms the session when the drawer opens with the model ready. **View context**: an app-level `ViewContext` (`@Observable`, injected beside the RevealController) carries one compact line ("routines/Push Day"); screens report via an appear-only `.operatorContext(_:)` modifier (tab roots report nil, so pops and tab switches clear a stale detail line), and each turn's prompt starts with one bracketed context+date line (~15 tokens). Contextual chips are hand-authored templates chosen deterministically from (tab, detail, has-history) — no model call. **Thread**: one JSON file in Application Support (`OperatorThreadStore`, atomic, capped at the policy's 120, corrupt-file → empty thread), deliberately NOT SwiftData (no migration/census surface) and NOT backup-excluded (a conversation is user state, not a cache); the transcript renders the last 60 with the honest scroll-back notice above. Receipt "View" posts `.plusplusOperatorShow` already, but nothing listens yet — outcome navigation is PR 3 by design. Post-apply hooks wired live (watch plan push + widget snapshot + calendar reconcile, the PlusPlusApp trio). ⚠️ Real 3B tool-dispatch quality, streaming latency, guardrail behavior on fitness vocabulary, and every availability state are on-device validation (the plan's checklist) — CI proves everything up to the model boundary, nothing behind it. See the PR 1 entry below for the engine's laws.

**2026-07-12 — Calendar sync identity is the TITLE, not the identifier (#346, Dave on-device: "changed the time and it made a second calendar; disable only removed one, orphaning the first")** — First on-device run of calendar sync (#333) surfaced a duplicate-calendar bug. Root cause is **documented EventKit behavior we relied on wrongly**: `EKCalendar.calendarIdentifier` is not durable — Apple's own docs say *"A full sync with the calendar will lose this identifier. You should have a plan for dealing with a calendar whose identifier is no longer fetch-able by caching its other properties."* When the "++ Workouts" calendar synced up to Dave's iCloud/Google account, the stored identifier stopped resolving. The v1 reconcile misread the non-resolving id as *the user deleted the calendar* (`store.calendar(withIdentifier:) == nil` → `disableAndRemove`), turned the feature off, and cleared the id; a subsequent enable then created a SECOND calendar at the new time. And because the code remembered only ONE identifier at a time, disable could only remove the last-created one — orphaning the first (Dave's exact asymmetry: the single-slot pointer, not the drift, is what orphaned specifically the older calendar). **Fix does what the doc prescribes — cache another property (the title) and key off it:** (1) `ourCalendars()` resolves by title ("++ Workouts"), drift-proof; (2) `resolvedCalendar`/`canonicalCalendar` picks one canonical calendar, CONSOLIDATES strays (deletes the extras), re-points the stored id, and clears the event cache when the calendar set changed so the survivor rebuilds from the current schedule — this auto-cleans the orphan already on affected devices; (3) user-deletion is now detected by *no ++ Workouts calendar existing at all* (passive pass only; the enable path rebuilds), so identifier drift no longer false-triggers the auto-off; (4) events are matched by scanning the calendar and reading the routine name from each event's `url` (`existingManagedEvents`), since event identifiers drift with the same sync — the stored `managedEvents` map is now just a fingerprint cache for change-detection, not the source of truth; (5) `disableAndRemove` removes EVERY "++ Workouts" calendar, so nothing can orphan. No Kit change (pure link/plan logic already covers the URL round-trip the event-scan match depends on); app-side EventKit glue, so CI compile-verifies and it needs an on-device re-check (enable → change time → confirm ONE calendar; disable → confirm ALL gone; delete the calendar in Calendar.app → confirm the feature turns off and doesn't resurrect).

**2026-07-16 — Operator field round 1: digests carry the payload, deltas beat replaces, and the model delivers instead of offering (Dave's first on-device conversation, build 84)** — Dave's very first exchange ("What equipment do I have?") exposed three compounding gaps. (1) The library digest was count-only ("Home · 3 items · active"), so the model could never say WHICH gear — it stalled in an offer loop ("want to check them out?" three times), then fished a WRONG answer out of exercise search (barbell curl/dumbbell shrug/kettlebell swing presented as the library's contents). Law from this: **a digest must carry the payload, not a pointer to it** — a count the model can't expand is worse than no line, because a small model fills the hole with the nearest-shaped wrong thing. `findItems(.library)` lines now name the members (alphabetized, capped at 10 + "+N more"). (2) The only membership edit was `values.equipment` REPLACE — for "add a jump rope" a 3B model that omits the existing members silently wipes them, and the update tiered applyNow. `ChangeValues` gains `addEquipment`/`removeEquipment` deltas (libraries only, validated; combining replace + delta is rejected as a contradiction), receipts speak the resolved catalog casing, and the existing LibrarySnapshot inverse covers undo unchanged. A replace on update now ALWAYS previews (`replacesMembership` in the tier policy — a whole-list restatement is a delete in disguise) and the preview card names the after state ("gear becomes …"). (3) The instructions never said deliver-don't-offer, so the model asked permission to show data it already had; one sentence added ("When a tool result holds the answer, state it in the same reply; never offer to look…"). Kit 351 green locally; engine/data-service tests cover the delta round trip, the replace preview, and the named digest.

**2026-07-16 — Operator field round 2: "my equipment" needs no library name, and ask_user stops re-asking (Dave's build-85 test)** — Round 1's digest fix landed visibly (gear named in one turn), but "Remove barbell and weight plate" exposed the next layer: the model burned a turn on a needless SINGLE-select ask_user (the user had already named both items), and the eventual pick failed because the spec named no library — then the model invented a reason ("barbell not in routines") instead of relaying the INVALID digest. Fixes: (1) a LIBRARY update naming no target now resolves to the ACTIVE library (Kit validation exemption + engine default) — "my equipment" is the active library everywhere else in the app, and requiring a 3B model to restate a name the user never said is exactly where it fails; deletes never default. (2) ask_user's description now polices both failure modes (never re-ask named items; allowMultiple when several can apply). (3) Instructions require relaying INVALID reasons verbatim. The options card itself was correct all along — radio + tap-submits is the designed single-select behavior; the model simply chose the wrong mode.

**2026-07-16 — Operator narrow-tool rebuild: the model is a classifier, so the tools are now labels, not an algebra (Dave: "treat it like the very incapable model it apparently is")** — Two field rounds established that the on-device 3B fails at COMPOSITION: the single generic `propose_change` (operation × entity × targets × filter × values) asked it to reason a spec together, and it kept picking wrong entities, dropping targets, and stalling. Apple's own positioning of the model is summarization/extraction/classification, NOT reasoning — so the surface now matches the machine: `propose_change` is DEAD, replaced by fourteen single-intent edit tools (`add_gear`, `remove_gear`, `replace_gear`, `create_library`, `create_routine`, `edit_routine_exercises`, `set_schedule`, `set_rest`, `create_exercise`, `edit_exercise`, `convert_tracking`, `form_superset`, `rename_item`, `delete_item`). Choosing an operation degenerates into picking a labeled tool name — classification, which constrained decoding makes near-foolproof — and wrong fields become structurally impossible because each schema only contains its own intent's fields (`remove_gear` has a names array and an optional library; there is no entity to get wrong). Every tool is a thin constructor onto the SAME Kit `ChangeSpec`: validation, tiering, previews, receipts, inverse-op undo, and outcome navigation are engine territory, unchanged and still Linux/CI-tested. The `@Generable` ChangeArgs/FilterArgs/ValuesArgs mirror died with the generic tool. Cost: ~16 schemas ride the 4,096-token window instead of 4 (descriptions kept terse on purpose); the deliberate trade is context room for dispatch reliability. Deferred lever if dispatch still wobbles on device: deterministic per-turn recipe injection (keyword-triggered one-line recipes with a worked example in the prompt channel) — skills for the tiny model.

**2026-07-16 — Operator design round (Dave's build-85 screenshots): the face with ++ eyes, no dots off SYNC, wrap-don't-overflow, tap-what-you-say chips, half-height tray** — Nine tweaks, all deterministic UI. (1) The reveal trigger read "OPERATOR / Operator / Operator, the app's…" three lines deep — redesigned to one `OperatorFaceGlyph` (a rounded-square face whose eyes are the ++ mark, green when the model is ready — the brand glyph IS the eyes) + the name once + the designed tagline wrapping beneath (the last-reply snippet died; a random reply fragment was the third "Operator"). (2) Status DOTS now mean exactly one thing, sync-connection state: the Operator hero and LIBRARY row lost theirs (`statusRow` dot is optional), GitHub/Health/Calendar keep them; the tray header's dot became the face glyph. (3) Suggested-prompt pills WRAP via a minimal `OperatorFlowLayout` (a horizontal scroll cut them at the screen edge) and a pill's text IS the prompt it sends — `OperatorChip` collapsed to one string (what you tap is what you say). (4) The tray allows `.medium` alongside `.large` (opens large; `presentationBackgroundInteraction(.enabled(upThrough: .medium))`), and outcome navigation now ALSO closes the reveal drawer at post time, so a half-height tray shows the change landing behind it live and a dismissed tray lands on the result, not the drawer. (5) Model text renders sentence-cased at DISPLAY time only (`operatorSentenceCased`: uppercases sentence openers, never lowercases, stored thread + option echoes stay verbatim) — the 3B writes "want to check them out?" no matter what the instructions say. A subtle 1 pt seam separates the tray header from the scroll area. **Same PR, the review-fix round** (adversarial pass on the full diff): the engine's active-library default gained an injection seam (the real resolver reads process-global UserDefaults, which parallel test suites race on) and PINS the resolved library's name into a staged spec's targets — a target-less membership replace re-resolved "active" at Apply time, so switching libraries mid-preview would have wiped a DIFFERENT library than the card named; `form_superset` guards two-plus exercises in the tool (spec validation taught the wrong lesson and one-exercise-plus-sets silently mutated a solo block); `rename_item` narrowed to a three-case kind enum (superset was an inescapable dead end); `delete_item` pre-checks supersets in its own field vocabulary; delta receipts report what actually FLIPPED (adding gear a library already has now reads "already set that way", never a false "added").

**2026-07-16 — Operator field round 3: per-turn recipes, the skills layer for a 4k-token model (Dave's build-91 screenshot)** — The narrow tools improved the endgame but the FIRST tool pick still wobbled: "What equipment do I have?" opened with a routines lookup, and the reply narrated every irrelevant routine line before reaching the (correct) library answer. The pre-agreed lever fires: `OperatorRecipes` — a deterministic keyword→recipe table (gear · tracking conversions · supersets · history stats · schedules, first match wins, ordered so "how many workouts last week" reads as stats, not schedule) whose matched line rides the PROMPT channel as one bracketed `[recipe: …]` between the context prefix and the user's text. Recipes are FIXED strings (never interpolated user input — the injection rule), cost zero tokens on unmatched turns, and name the right tool at the point of need, which lands far harder on a 3B than standing instructions. Companions: `find_items`' kind field gains a "Libraries hold the user's gear" guide (the wrong-first-pick case, addressed at the decision point), and the instructions gain "Answer only what was asked; skip tool lines that do not bear on it" (the noise-narration half of the failure). This IS the skills pattern scaled to the window: trigger-loaded, hand-authored, deterministic.

**2026-07-20 — Routine card unification: one card design across catalog, library, and detail, one capsule vocabulary everywhere (Dave, from three screenshots)** — The catalog card (an ALL-CAPS mono `FOCUS · EFFORT · TIME · NEEDS GEAR` line, no capsules), the library card (calendar-glyph cadence + gear capsules whose TEXT truncated, "Squat Ra…"), and the routine detail header (plain mono fact lines) were three designs for the same object. Unify onto one shared body, varying only where a template genuinely differs from an added routine — the way an equipment card varies only by its in-kit glyph. **Shape**: a `RoutineCardModel` value + `RoutineCardContent` (`Views/Components/RoutineCardContent.swift`) render title (subheadline, 2 lines) · prose (2 lines) · one capsule row of `schedule · focus · effort · estimate · gear`; the library `RoutineCard` and the catalog `templateRow` each build the model, card chrome (padding/background/entrance-flash; the catalog's `Button`) stays per call site — the exact split `ExerciseRowContent`/`EquipmentRowContent` already use. The schedule capsule is the ONE necessary catalog↔library difference (a template has no schedule). **Dave's rules, encoded**: (1) no all-caps except section headings — the catalog meta line and the stroked ALL-CAPS `BUILT-IN`/`CUSTOM`/category detail capsules are retired; (2) capsules never truncate/wrap — a single-line `OverflowCapsuleRow` (measures each capsule's width from the caption2-monospaced UIFont metrics against a background-`GeometryReader` width, reserving room for the tag) collapses the tail into a trailing "N more"; (3) prose wraps to two lines then ellipsis; (4) shared facts sit in the same slots with the same treatment. **Gear is the real unification**: it reads the same soft `CardTagCapsule` in both cards, amber-washed when the active kit lacks the piece (the catalog's "NEEDS BARBELL"/"YOUR GEAR ✓" verdict is gone). Amber (unavailable) gear sorts FIRST, so the "N more" overflow can only ever drop an AVAILABLE piece — #113 flag-don't-hide is preserved without a dedicated needs-line. **Focus + effort on both cards without a migration**: they are authored on `RoutineTemplate` (deliberately, per that file — an authored "30 min" lies once the copy is edited, and effort isn't derivable) and back the catalog FOCUS/EFFORT filters, so catalog cards must show the authored values (the filter↔capsule grammar law). A `Routine` copies the template's `summary` verbatim at `instantiate`, so `Routine.catalogTemplate` recovers the authored pair by matching `RoutineCatalog.all` on that summary — `focusLabel`/`effortLabel` are computed, NO new persisted fields, NO schema migration (the SwiftData rules make migration the high-risk path; a heavily edited routine falls back to `RoutineTemplate.Focus.derived(fromMuscles:isCardio:)` for focus and drops the effort capsule). **Detail header aligns with the cards but shows the FULL set** (Dave: no cap there): the mono fact lines become a wrapping `DetailHeaderCapsules` (reusing `FlowLayout`) of schedule · focus · effort · estimate · N exercises · M sets · rest · every gear, amber-flagged. **Exercise/equipment sweep** (Dave picked rows + detail headers): exercise rows render gear as the same amber-first capsules with overflow (replacing the plain gear text + separate "needs X" line); all three detail headers move to `CardTagCapsule` in natural case; `ChipLabel` (the stroked outlined chip) is deleted and its four call sites repointed — one capsule style app-wide. swift-reviewer clean (static only — app-target files don't compile on Linux); app CI green. ⚠️ Capsule fit/feel is CI-invisible: needs Dave's on-device pass on the "N more" overflow at large Dynamic Type, catalog↔library focus/effort parity (added template vs a custom routine), and the detail header wrapping the full gear set. Build 104 dispatched from the branch (PR #414).

**2026-07-20 — Routine-catalog filter row: the Gear facet becomes a Kit sheet, and filter chips carry meaningful icons (Dave's build-104 feedback)** — Two follow-ups on the card-unification branch (build 105). (1) **Catalog row wrap fix**: the shared `EquipmentRowContent` (and the routine-card title) sized the name to its ideal width while a trailing `Spacer` took the slack; the in-kit checkmark tightened the width proposal just enough that `lineLimit(2)` tipped a medium name ("Resistance Band") onto two lines while longer checkmark-less rows stayed on one. Fix: the name/VStack claims the row's free width (`maxWidth: .infinity`) and drops the competing Spacer — the same shape `ExerciseRowContent` already used. (2) **Filter row**: `FOCUS`/`EFFORT`/`TIME` → sentence case (the chips render their facet string verbatim and were always meant to be sentence-case; the caps were literal strings). The **GEAR** facet becomes **Kit**, moved leftmost, and opens a SHEET (`RoutineKitFilterSheet`) instead of an anchored menu — one radio list that both switches the kit the catalog judges against (writing the app-wide `activeLibraryID`, exactly like the Equipment-tab switcher) and picks the fit mode: a kit (`.mine`), No equipment (`.bodyweightOnly`), or All routines (`nil`). The old `FacetChip` footer affordances ("Edit my equipment…"/"Switch kit…") and their two sheets retire; kit management (new/rename/delete) stays on the Equipment tab. `anyFilterActive` and `clearFilters` now key off the DEFAULT `.mine` lens (not `!= nil`), so the resting browse (your kit, no facets) shows no ✕ and clearing returns to your kit rather than show-all. **Every active filter chip gains a meaningful SF Symbol**, value-specific where a clean symbol exists else the attribute icon: Effort ramps `thermometer.low/medium/high` (a single pick; a union falls back to `flame.fill`), Focus `target`, Time `clock`, Kit `dumbbell.fill`/`figure.strengthtraining.functional`; the Equipment catalog's row gets the same (Kit `checkmark.circle.fill`/`circle`, Type `tag.fill`, Muscle `figure.arms.open`). The capability is reusable, added as defaulted `attributeSymbol`/`valueSymbols` on `FacetChip`/`MultiFacetChip` and `activeSymbol` on `TrayFilterChip` (untouched callers keep compiling); the sheet-opening chip is the new `KitFilterChip`. By-design note flagged for device: the Kit chip reads blue-by-default because the kit lens is the resting scope — a deliberate departure from "one blue on screen," worth an eye beside the blue facets. swift-reviewer clean; app CI green; no Kit/model change. Build 105 dispatched from the branch.

**2026-07-23 — Design review round 1: close the loops, one grammar applied to its own corners, honest states, the unlock beat (Dave-decided item by item from the review artifact)** — A full app design review (four parallel static sweeps — navigation topology, grammar consistency, disclosure/density, plus the Axiom UX-flow audit — findings hand-verified) produced 19 proposals; Dave decided each one, and this round implements the decided set. **Verdict first**: the system held — zero dead-end views, zero dismiss traps, the empty-never-dead-ends law real on every list, kit switching and onboarding the strongest flows; what needed fixing was missing connections between surfaces and the grammar not yet applied to its newest corners. **Close the loops**: the session record's "Do it again" died for **"View routine"** (Dave: doing it again IS the routine's Start; the record now links to the surface that acts — the drill-out-drill-in fix for "felt too easy, bump the weight"); exercise detail's lone "New routine with X" became **"Add to routine…"** (a sheet leading with creation, existing routines below — the missing add-to-existing door at the point of discovery); routine-start deep links (calendar/Siri/plusplus.fit) **fail loud** via one-shot alerts on the name-miss and already-running guards that used to swallow the tap (the UX audit's one HIGH; stable-id resolution filed as a follow-up); **one landing for every template add/import** — the Routines list + entrance flash, via `RoutineArrival` (a pending-uuid handoff consumed on receive OR first appear, so an unmounted tab still flashes; supersedes 2026-07-15's land-in-detail, Dave's call, and share imports land the same way instead of dismissing to nowhere); an unreadable share link alerts instead of silently dropping. **Mid-workout restructuring + honest skips**: `SessionExerciseSheet` gains **Swap for… / Remove** on non-live blocks (`WorkoutSession.swapPendingBlock` replaces remaining pending sets IN PLACE — keeps the groupIndex, first pending order slot, own set numbers; `removePendingBlock` drops pending, keeps the record; both reindex + re-pin the cursor, both refuse the live block; unit-tested), and the record renders never-completed sets as neutral **"skipped"** rows (display-level, `sortedSetLogs` grouping — a jumped-past set used to vanish silently; anti-shame: fact, not judgment). **The ad-hoc auto-end bug** (Dave hit it on device): auto-`finishSession` fired whenever `nextPendingLog == nil`, ending a scratch workout the moment its first added exercise completed — auto-finish now requires `session.routine != nil` (the plan ending IS the finish); a routine-less session lands on `stagedWorkDoneStage` (Add exercise / Finish workout). **One grammar**: the exercise editor's four capsule chip builders fold into `SelectableChip`+`FlowLayout` (the metric/muscle toggles) and family-shaped r11 chips (the removable REQUIRES tags); the kit tray's stroked-mono gear capsule became `CardTagCapsule`; the live-workout HUD joined the key family (End/Pause/Overview = r11 raised keys at QuietKey metrics, HR/pace = soft r6 data tags, explicit 8 pt header gaps); the overview's flat Add-exercise became the shared `CreateRow`; **`Theme.keyRadius` names the 11 pt radius** (~40 bare literals swept; `FilterChipShape.cornerRadius` aliases it); motion drift → tokens (0.16/0.18/`.default` → `.standard`; the list-reveal flourish through `Anim.flourish`; the new-card ring flash deliberately stays un-gated under Reduce Motion — a pure opacity fade carrying which-card-landed information, documented in place); the calendar swatch derives from `Theme.accent` (dark-side, resolved) instead of an independent approximation; the Kit tab's empty search gained the standard Clear key. **Disclosure**: the instant ✕ `ClearAllChip` died for **`FilterSummaryChip`** (selection-blue count chip → popover naming each active facet's values + Clear-all; persisted filters made a silently-narrowed catalog possible, and the summary is where narrowing explains itself — all four facet surfaces); the **superset creation tip teaches the drag** as a popover pinned to the first rail row (Dave, reversing build-45's sheet-path-only copy; display gated by a `canPair` Tip parameter so the attachment is unconditional — no #270 identity churn; the loop tip stays inline for imported supersets); `ExerciseDetailSheet` re-tiered — merge/move/delete collapse behind one quiet **Structure** disclosure (glance is the sheet's common case; icon-row and …-menu variants considered and rejected in-code). **Honest states**: denied Location during an outdoor exercise shows an amber "GPS off" control opening iOS Settings (`RunLocationMonitor.authorizationDenied`, tracked ahead of the running/armed guard so a mid-pause Settings change still reads; parity with the Health tray — denial used to render exactly like "no fix yet"); the exercise editor **confirms a dirty discard** (fingerprint baseline at open; blocked swipe + Cancel-confirm, the Mail-compose pattern — Dave's exception to Cancel-is-instant, this being the app's biggest form). **No toasts, ever** (Dave): the one live toast (pull-to-refresh quip) renders INLINE at the timeline top where the pull settles; `Toast.swift` deleted. **The unlock beat** (the round's one delight bet, Dave-approved minus the kit-switch variant): toggling equipment INTO the kit raises a green "+N exercises" chip off the toggle card — N counts exercises made FULLY doable (this piece + what the kit already holds), not mere users of the piece, because an overclaiming beat trains distrust; plays in onboarding too (the cross-link lists stay hidden there), Reduce Motion appears static, VoiceOver hears an announcement. Dropped from the round: B1 (setup cards keep committed purple — Dave likes finished tasks purple; only the stale "green node" comment was fixed). App-target only (no Kit change); smoke-test onboarding flow updated for the new landing; +2 session-model unit tests. ⚠️ Nearly everything here is device-feel: the HUD keys, the popover tip anchor, the filter popover, the unlock beat, the arrival flash across tabs, the discard guard, the 0.15 s swipe/reorder timing — Dave's pass rides the next build.

**2026-07-23 — Design review round 2a: planning-time Swap/Remove parity, the Structure disclosure retired after one build (Dave's round-1 feedback)** — Two calls from Dave on the round-1 diff. (1) The mid-session "Swap for…"/"Remove" pair belongs at PLANNING time too: `ExerciseDetailSheet` (the rail's per-exercise sheet) gains the same pair. Zero new model surface — `Routine.replaceExercise(_:with:)` already existed (the equipment-resolve swap step) and already encodes the right semantics (targets reset to the new exercise's add-time defaults; sets/rest are group facts and stay), and "Remove" converges the sheet's hand-rolled delete onto `Routine.removeExercise` (one reindex path with swipe-delete). Plumbing: the sheet's key fires `onSwap` + dismisses, RoutineDetailView sets a new uuid-keyed `PickerDestination.swap`, the PUSHED picker appears beneath the closing sheet, and the pick applies in `addExercise(_:to:)`'s new branch (deleted-slot no-op guard; self-swap no-op guard in `replaceExercise` — a confirm-tap on the current exercise must not wipe hand-tuned targets; synchronous save per the tray-flicker law). The supposed precedent for the dismiss-then-push-beneath handoff, the sheet's `onAddToSuperset` closure, turned out to be DEAD CODE — never called from anywhere, ever (swift-reviewer archaeology) — so it and its unreachable `PickerDestination.group` case were deleted with this round, and the handoff rides the device-pass list as field-unproven rather than claimed as proven. Renamed "Delete exercise" → **"Remove"**: the slot leaves the routine, the exercise stays in the catalog — Remove is the truer verb and matches the session sheet. (2) **The Structure disclosure is OUT** (round 1's B4; Dave: "I don't like the collapsed area") — replaced by always-visible COMPACT PAIRS, Dave-picked from options: `[Move up|Move down]`, the contextual superset row (`[Superset above|Superset below]` paired when both neighbors exist, full-width single otherwise, `[Move out of superset]` for members), then `[Swap for…|Remove]` anchoring the bottom in destructive ink. Net height ≈ the old disclosure row + two, far under the pre-B4 five-row stack that motivated the disclosure — the pairing, not the hiding, turned out to be the right density fix. ⚠️ Device pass: the half-width labels at large Dynamic Type, and the swap flow's sheet-dismiss → picker-push-behind timing. See the round-1 entry above for everything else this branch carries.

**2026-07-23 — Universal search: "Find or create" behind a native search tab; the per-tab header magnifiers retire (design handoff, HTML prototype + exploration record)** — The four per-tab expanding header searches consolidated into ONE surface that finds or makes a routine, an exercise, or a piece of equipment — yours or the catalog's — settled through an exploration round (`#2b` decision A: clean rows, act after opening; `#3a/#3b` before/after). **Entry is a native `Tab(role: .search)`** appended to RootTabView: iOS 26 renders it as the separated circular item beside the tab group (the prototype's placement for free, correct Liquid Glass treatment), with two accepted deviations — the system fixes the magnifier glyph (the two-tone `plus.magnifyingglass` doesn't apply, the handoff's pre-approved fallback), and a tab item takes no long-press menu, so the create menu lives in the All-scope create row's chooser (`CreateMenuRow`, `CreateRow`'s Menu twin; the handoff pre-approved this move, and "New kit…" dropped — the tray reachable from the surface's own switcher already creates kits). No `.searchable`: the surface renders its own field row, so the search tab behaves as a plain tab (the tab bar stays visible — a free escape to any tab) and owns a NavigationStack, honoring "search is a stack, not a modal": tapping a result PUSHES the existing detail screen (all four destinations registered at the surface's root, #262) and back/swipe-back returns with query, scope, and scroll intact. **Layout** is the tab-root grammar applied whole: ++ key · "Find or create" · `LibrarySwitcherKey` (kit is CONTEXT, never a filter chip — the kit-vs-filter tension resolved by putting the one app-wide switch in the header); the shared field anatomy (`SearchFieldBody`, factored out of `HeaderSearchField` so the always-open field and the expanding one can't drift) + a text **Done** key (never ✕ — ✕ stays collapse-search); scope chips All · Routines · Exercises · Kit (`SelectableChip` + type icons); then the **filter-dependent create row ABOVE results** (never a dead end, "Nothing matches." renders beneath it): All = chooser menu, Routines = blank create (query names it directly; empty query asks via the existing alert — no junk "New Routine" rows), Exercises = the prefilled editor, Kit = create-into-active-kit (the equipment catalog's dedupe recipe). **Results**: an empty query shows EVERYTHING (no blank state) — mine-first, then alphabetical; a query ranks mine → score → name. All scope = three type sections capped at 3 + "n more ›" (chevron, not ＋; section header and more-row both jump to the scope); scoped = MINE · n / CATALOG · n (`SheetSectionLabel` grammar; added templates leave CATALOG by the name rule). Scoring reuses each surface's own precedent via a pure, unit-tested `FindOrCreateEngine` (no ModelContext): the exercise name+muscle haystack, the routine catalog's deep `searchScore` (name OR contained·0.75) — with a **"has X" capsule** explaining a routine matched through a contained exercise — and equipment name+category. **Row anatomy** is the shared vocabulary with two additive params (`leadingSymbol`, `nameHighlight`): leading type icons in All scope only EXCEPT exercise modality figures, which carry information and stay in Exercises scope — the NEW Kit `ExerciseModality` derives them (gear-specific first: rower/jump rope/bikes; load beats distance so carries stay strength; road/console metrics = cardio; `.flexibility` is authored-only via a new `BuiltInExerciseDefinition.modality` column the stretch/mobility builders fill, because derivation can't tell a stretch from a plank — no model field, wrong guesses cost nothing). Matched substrings paint in `Theme.selectedTint` via the NEW `FuzzySearch.highlightRanges` (literal homes only — prefix/substring/over-typed tiers return original-string ranges; typo and abbreviation matches deliberately paint nothing rather than lie about where the match lives). **Interaction is decision A verbatim**: no inline action keys; long-press is a system `.contextMenu` (iOS-native-first — the prototype's hand-rolled peek card was an HTML approximation of exactly this; a UIKit interaction, so #99's scroll-starving trap doesn't apply) carrying Favorite / Add-Remove kit / Add to routines / Start / Open; Return opens the top result. **The no-toasts landing grammar extends to all three types**: `ExerciseArrival` + `EquipmentArrival` join `RoutineArrival` (pending-`PersistentIdentifier` slots — permanent-by-save, scroll+flash identity only, never navigation), their tabs consume on receive-or-appear and play a new `RowEntranceFlash` (the card ring choreography at row scale); the Exercises tab clears its persisted filters on arrival, because a landing that flashes a filtered-out row would be a lie. Kit membership flips from the context menu are state-flip-is-the-feedback (no landing). **Elsewhere**: the three tab headers drop their magnifiers (`searchText` state, search-branch empties, and the Routines reorder guard die with them); the Routines/Kit Add rows deep-link into the surface pre-scoped via `FindOrCreateLaunch` (a scope handoff slot + `.plusplusFindOrCreate`; the surface consumes it in the stack-level `onAppear`, which fires per tab entry but NOT on pop-back — the ephemeral-state law without breaking the round-trip); the `RoutineTemplate`/`RoutineCatalogDestination` registrations leave the Routines stack (Today's setup keeps its own — both catalogs stay alive for onboarding); the kit switcher joins the Routines header; and the Exercises availability facet names its basis ("Doable with <kit name>" / "Missing equipment" + a "Switch kit…" footer) — the handoff wrote "Gear" here, but the 2026-07-20 vocabulary law retired that word, so the law won. Blank-routine creation now lands on the Routines LIST with the flash (the handoff's table row, superseding "blank creation lands in detail" — flagged to Dave in the PR). Kit 447 green on Linux (+12); engine unit tests in the app target; smoke flows updated (the createRoutine helper walks the new landing; the template-detail flow rides the surface; +1 universal-search flow). ⚠️ Device-only: the search-tab item's placement/glyph and `onAppear` re-fire semantics on re-selection, keyboard auto-rise on tab entry, reveal-drawer gating on the search tab (`.revealRoot(tab: "search")`), context-menu feel, the row flashes, and All-scope empty-query scroll perf. See the round-1/2a entries above for the review context this rode in on.

**2026-07-23 — The selected-tab capsule's SIZE is the native bar's fixed rendering — the tint-scoping experiment is a settled NEGATIVE result (Build 118; do not retry)** — Dave's Slack side-by-side on Build 116: our selected tab's capsule platter fills nearly the bar's full height, where Slack's sits smaller and inset. The platter is the system's Liquid Glass selection treatment — no SwiftUI API parameterizes its size, insets, or prominence (checked against the Axiom iOS 26 references) — and the app feeds the bar exactly ONE input: `.tint(Theme.textPrimary)` on the whole TabView (there since build 10 so selected tabs read neutral ink, not system blue). The one testable hypothesis was that the TabView-level tint triggered a larger/heavier platter than the untinted stock wash, so Build 118 scoped the tint to the five tabs' content and let the bar render stock. **Dave's device verdict: the capsule size is UNCHANGED, and the selected icon went system-accent blue, which he rejected ("icon color for those tabs shouldn't change").** Conclusions, recorded so no future session re-derives them: (1) the platter's geometry is the native bar's own look, not driven by tint — Slack's tighter capsule is their own drawing, not a configuration we're missing; (2) the TabView-level `.tint(Theme.textPrimary)` is LOAD-BEARING for the ink selected-tab icons and stays; (3) the only remaining lever on platter size is abandoning the native TabView for a custom bar, which stays rejected (the build-10 trade: system hit targets, accessibility, scroll-edge treatment, and now the search-role circle placement, all free). The code reverted same-day (this PR carries zero code delta vs main — the record is the deliverable); the app accepts the platform's selection treatment.

## Appendix: TestFlight build genealogy

> Moved verbatim from CLAUDE.md's Current State on 2026-07-10; kept for
> archaeology. CLAUDE.md tracks only the current build and safety warnings.

**TestFlight:** `.github/workflows/testflight.yml` (manual dispatch, any ref) archives unsigned, cloud-signs at export with an Admin-role ASC API key, and uploads; build number = run number — ⚠️ which means the NEXT build number is the workflow's next RUN number, not last-build+1 (runs 38–40 were consumed by past attempts; a mislabeled What's-New entry was caught at the build-42 dispatch — check `actions_list` for the latest run number BEFORE writing the entry, and expect a cancel/relabel/redispatch cycle if you guess). **Build 46** is current — build 45 + PR #297 (heart rate: live on-screen bpm during workouts [phone header capsule + watch run view], avg/max on the Complete screen / committed cards / session records, cardio zone/bpm targets in the planning sheet, the three-screen welcome flow) + PR #304 (flexible metrics — see the decision: the 14-metric curated vocabulary, per-exercise MetricProfile with seed-table resolution, equipment-suggested configs + EXERCISE CONFIG chips, the execution driver [reps > distance > calories > duration, target decides], interval blocks via per-block rest overrides + ROUND kickers, direction-aware diffs [−0:05 /500m in green], Running/Walking/Cycling, additive interchange/watch fields; rebased over #297 with the HR band hoisted to show on distance-driven intervals too). Build 45 was — build 44 + PR #293 (Dave's build-44 walkthrough, #291: the routine catalog rides the NavigationPath — `RoutineCatalogDestination` marker pushed from the Routines `+` and Today's setup step 2, registered at both stack roots, double-tap guards on the new appends; the ++ key on every root header via `AppMenuKey`; the build-33 regression smoke test now asserts back-pop depth). The ui-test proof run flaked once at the documented step-3 assertion (discriminator passed; green on re-run).
